The Meaning of the Sun Rising from the West
Buti defines the sign and cautions against speculation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the literal meaning of the sun rising from the west and why speculating about its exact mechanism is not required for belief.

Core Idea
The sun rising from the west is a change in cosmic order known only to God.

This lesson examines a well-known eschatological sign: the sun rising from the west. Buti clarifies its literal meaning and provides a possible natural explanation, but immediately warns against claiming certainty about its mechanism. The key is to affirm the sign without overstepping into divine knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the two parts: the definition and the footnote caution.
The footnote is marked with (1) in the Arabic.
2
Identify the literal definition
Buti explains that the sun rising from the west means it appears to people rising from the west in the morning instead of the east. This is a literal change in direction.
3
Reflect on the caution about the mechanism
Buti mentions a possible mechanism (change in earth's rotation) but immediately states that this is not a definitive explanation; knowledge of the means is with God. Understand why such speculation is avoided.
This guards against the misconception that the exact mechanism is known.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعنى طلوع الشمس من مغربها أنها تظهر للناس طالعة من جهة المغرب في وقت الصباح بدلاً من ظهورها لهم من ناحية المشرق كما كان دأبها كل يوم . وذلك كأن يجعل الله دوران الأرض عندها في اتجاه آخر يتراءى معه للناس انعكاس سير الشمس بالنسبة إليهم . (1) ليس هذا تقريراً لبيان الوسيلة التي بها تخرج الشمس من مغربها ، فعلم ذلك عند الله . ولكنه تقريب لوسيلة الإيمان به، وتذكير للقارئ بأن ذلك لا يخرج عن كونه تغييراً لبعض ما درج عليه الكون - بمشيئة الله تعالى - من نظام وترتيب.
And the meaning of the sun rising from its west is that it appears to people rising from the direction of the west in the morning instead of its appearing to them from the direction of the east as was its habit every day. That is as if God makes the rotation of the earth then in another direction, so that the reflection of the sun's course relative to them becomes visible to people. (1) This is not a statement to explain the means by which the sun emerges from its west, for knowledge of that is with God. Rather, it is an approximation of the means of belief in it, and a reminder to the reader that it does not go beyond being a change in some of the system and order upon which the universe has proceeded - by the will of God Almighty.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the phenomenon of the sun rising from the west. It begins by stating the literal meaning: the sun appears to people in the morning from the west instead of the east, as it normally does. The author then suggests a possible mechanism: that God causes the earth's rotation to change direction, so that people perceive the sun's path as reversed. However, immediately in the footnote, the author clarifies that this explanation is not a definitive statement of the means, which is known only to God. Instead, it is merely an approximation to facilitate belief and to remind the reader that the event is a change in the cosmic order by God's will. The author carefully avoids claiming certain knowledge of the mechanism, guarding against the misconception that the means has been specified.

Key Terms
طلوع الشمس من مغربها
دوران الأرض
تغيير النظام
مشيئة الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The exact mechanism of the sun rising from the west is known or can be definitively explained.
Correction: Buti explicitly states that knowledge of the means is with God alone, and his mention of earth's rotation change is merely an approximation to facilitate belief.

Checkpoint
According to the footnote, what is the purpose of mentioning the change in earth's rotation?
A) To prove that the sun rising from the west is scientifically possible
B) To explain the exact mechanism as known by God
C) To approximate the means of belief and remind that it is a change in the cosmic order
D) To argue against those who deny the sign

Key Takeaway
The sun rising from the west is a literal change in the cosmic order, but its precise mechanism is known only to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about the sun rising from the west, do you feel a sense of awe and submission to Allah's absolute power, or does your mind immediately try to explain it away scientifically? What does that reveal about your heart's reliance on rational explanations over divine revelation?
?
The author intentionally leaves the mechanism unknown. Are you comfortable with not knowing how this sign will occur? Is there an area of your faith where you demand details Allah has not given, and how does that reflect a lack of trust in His wisdom?
?
If you knew for certain that the sun would rise from the west tomorrow, how would you change your life today? Take that urgency and apply it to your belief in the Hour.

The Signs of the Hour: Obligatory Belief Through Revelation and Consensus
Buti establishes the authority and purpose of the signs of the Hour.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the epistemological basis for the signs of the Hour and why belief in them is deemed necessary by scholarly consensus.

Core Idea
Belief in the signs of the Hour is not optional—it is founded on revelation and consensus.

In this final passage on the eschatological signs, Buti anchors their reality in two inviolable sources: truthful report (the Quran and Sunnah) and the consensus of the Muslim community. He reminds us that many of these signs have already occurred, confirming the truth of the Prophet's message. More importantly, he clarifies that these events, though extraordinary, are merely changes in the cosmic order permitted by Allah—not violations of nature—and serve to strengthen faith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sources of knowledge
Read the passage and locate the two grounds Buti gives for affirming the signs of the Hour: truthful report (al-khabar aṣ-ṣādiq) and consensus (ijmāʿ).
These are foundational concepts in Islamic epistemology.
2
Notice the practical implication
Buti says Muslims have agreed on the necessity (ḍarūra) of belief. Reflect on why he uses such strong language.
This refutes the idea that eschatological details are merely speculative.
3
Understand the purpose of the signs
The passage ends by stating that these signs are changes in the universe by Allah's will, meant to bring faith closer. Consider how this reframes miracles as tools for spiritual growth.
This connects eschatology with tawḥīd and Divine power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذه الأمور، من أهم أشراط الساعة التي وصل إلينا علمها عن طريق الخبر الصادق، وأجمع المسلمون على ضرورة الاعتقاد بها. وللساعة أشراط وعلامات أخرى تحدث عنها النبي في كثير من أحاديثه، وكثير منها ظهر وتحقق كما أخبر ولا مجال لذكرها والتوسع في الحديث عنها في هذا المقام. والله تعالى أعلم. تقريب لوسيلة الإيمان به، وتذكير للقارئ بأن ذلك لا يخرج عن كونه تغييراً لبعض ما درج عليه الكون - بمشيئة الله تعالى - من نظام وترتيب.
These matters are among the most important signs of the Hour whose knowledge has reached us through truthful report, and the Muslims have agreed upon the necessity of believing in them. The Hour has other signs and portents that the Prophet mentioned in many of his hadiths, and many of them have appeared and been realized as he informed, and there is no room to mention them and elaborate on them in this context. And Allah Almighty knows best. An approximation of the means of faith in it, and a reminder to the reader that this is nothing but a change in some of the order and arrangement that the universe has become accustomed to - by the will of Allah Almighty.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage defines the signs of the Hour (Ašrāṭ as-Sāʿah) as matters that must be believed based on true reports (al-khabar aṣ-ṣādiq) and the consensus (ijmāʿ) of Muslims. Buti emphasizes that many of these signs have already appeared, confirming the Prophet's prophethood. He then notes that these signs represent a change in the normal cosmic order, by Allah's will, serving as a means to strengthen faith. The passage clarifies the theological status of these signs: they are part of the unseen (ghayb) that must be accepted without doubt.

Key Terms
أشراط الساعة
الخبر الصادق
الإجماع
الاعتقاد
المسلمون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Belief in the specific signs of the Hour is optional or merely recommended.
Correction: Buti explicitly states that Muslims have reached a consensus on the necessity (ḍarūra) of believing in these signs, making it obligatory.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, why is belief in the signs of the Hour obligatory?
A) Because they are rationally undeniable
B) Because they are proven by truthful report and consensus
C) Because they are witnessed by many people
D) Because they are mentioned in scientific literature

Key Takeaway
The signs of the Hour are obligatory beliefs, known through revelation and consensus, and their fulfillment past and future serves to strengthen faith in Allah and His Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that belief in the signs of the Hour is obligatory by revelation and consensus. Do you genuinely affirm these signs in your heart, or have you allowed doubt to creep in because some seem far-fetched? What would change in your daily life if you truly lived with the certainty that these events are imminent?
?
The signs are meant to strengthen your faith. When you see world events, do you interpret them as natural coincidences or as deliberate signs from Allah? How would viewing them as purposeful reminders transform your connection with your Creator?
?
If the Prophet (peace be upon him) was truthful about the signs he foretold and many have already been realized, what does that demand of you today? Are you preparing for what is yet to come, or are you ignoring the warnings?

From the End of the World to the Day of Resurrection
Buti describes the transition from this universe's end to the Day of Resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sequence of events from the end of the world to the Day of Resurrection as described by Buti.

Core Idea
The end of the universe is the beginning of the Day of Resurrection.

Buti paints a vivid picture of the cosmic transition: the universe, which has faithfully served its Lord, will disintegrate at a moment known only to Allah. This destruction is not the end but the start of a new creation leading to the Day of Judgment. In this lesson, we trace the stages from the signs of the Hour to the final settlement in Paradise or Hell.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading Buti's description slowly. Notice the contrast between the orderly service of the universe and its sudden disintegration.
The Arabic is poetic; appreciate the flow.
2
Identify the sequence of events
List the events in order: completion of signs, arrival of the appointed moment, end of life, scattering of the cosmos, new phase, Hour, resurrection, reckoning, balance, bridge, final abodes.
This sequence is the backbone of the passage.
3
Understand the divine timing
Reflect on the phrase 'hidden from all His servants' – the precise time is known only to Allah, emphasizing divine transcendence.
This highlights the unseen nature of the Hour.
4
Connect to Qur'anic terminology
Note that Buti explicitly links this end to what the Qur'an calls 'the Hour' and 'the Day of Resurrection'. See how he uses these terms as a starting point for the hereafter.
This shows the Islamic eschatological vocabulary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تمهيد ثالثا: يوم القيامة والآخرة. إذا تكاملت أشراط الساعة التي تحدثنا عنها، وجاء ميقات اللحظة المحددة المعلومة عند رب العالمين، والخفية عن عباده أجمعين، ذلك الميقات الذي ينتهي ... أجل الدنيا بما فيها - حينئذ تنتهي الحياة من على هذه الأرض وسائر بقاع الكون الأخرى، وينتثر هذا النظام الكوني بأجمعه .. بعد أن ظل دهراً مديداً سائراً في خدمة مولاه، ملتزماً ما وضعه فيه من منهج لا ينحرف عنه. إن خدمته الرتيبة هذه تنتهي في تلك اللحظة التي لا يعلم ميقاتها إلا الله عز وجل، ليبدأ من ورائها طور جديد من الخلق والتكوين والتنظيم. فهذه النهاية التي تنعدم عندها الحياة من الكون وينهار عندها نظامه وتتبدل معالمه وتنتثر أجزاؤه، هو بدء ما يسميه القرآن، بالساعة وبيوم القيامة. ثم تمتد هذه البداية إلى حشر الأجساد وإعادة أرواحها إليها، ثم إلى يتبع من طول حساب وميزان واجتياز صراط، إلى أن يستقر أصحاب الجنة في جنان خلدهم ويستقر أصحاب العذاب في سعيرهم.
Third Prelude: The Day of Resurrection and the Hereafter. When the signs of the Hour that we have discussed are completed, and the appointed moment known only to the Lord of the worlds arrives, hidden from all His servants – that appointed time which ends the term of this world and everything in it – then life will end on this earth and all other parts of the universe, and this entire cosmic system will scatter after having for a long age been proceeding in service to its Lord, adhering to the course set for it from which it does not deviate. This orderly service ends at that moment whose time no one knows except Allah Almighty, to be followed by a new phase of creation, formation, and organization. So this end, at which life ceases from the universe, its system collapses, its features change, and its parts scatter, is the beginning of what the Qur'an calls the Hour and the Day of Resurrection. Then this beginning extends to the gathering of bodies and the return of souls to them, then to what follows of long reckoning, balance, and crossing of the bridge, until the people of Paradise settle in their eternal gardens and the people of punishment settle in their blazing fire.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a prelude (tamhīd) describing the eschatological sequence. Buti begins by stating that after the completion of the signs of the Hour, at a specific moment known only to Allah, life ends and the cosmic order disintegrates. He emphasizes that the universe has been faithfully serving its Lord throughout its duration. This end is the beginning of what the Qur'an terms as-Sāʿah and Yawm al-Qiyāmah. The process extends to the resurrection of bodies (ḥashr al-ajsād), reuniting souls, then the lengthy reckoning (ḥisāb), weighing of deeds (mīzān), crossing the bridge (ṣirāṭ), and final settlement in Paradise or Hell. The passage is a concise summary of Islamic eschatology, linking the end of the world to the hereafter.

Key Terms
أشراط الساعة
ميقات
النظام الكوني
الطور الجديد
القيامة
حشر الأجساد
الحساب
الميزان
الصراط
الجنة
العذاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the end of the world is instant and final.
Correction: Buti describes a sequence: the destruction is only the beginning of a new phase that includes resurrection, judgment, and eternal consequences.

Checkpoint
What begins at the moment the cosmic system collapses according to Buti?
A) The complete annihilation of everything
B) The beginning of what the Qur'an calls the Hour and the Day of Resurrection
C) Immediate paradise for believers
D) The judgment of souls only

Key Takeaway
The destruction of the universe is the beginning of the Hour and the sequence of resurrection and judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that the entire universe serves its Lord faithfully until the appointed moment. How is your own life serving that same Lord? Are you a faithful servant like the cosmos, or are you deviating from His course? What specific step will you take today to realign your life with His will?
?
The passage says the moment of the end is hidden from all servants except Allah. Does the uncertainty of that moment actually change how you live today? If you truly believed it could come at any second, what would you do differently starting tomorrow? Write down one attachment to this world that you need to break.
?
Reflect on the sequence: from the end, to resurrection, to judgment, to the eternal abode. Where do you see yourself in that sequence right now? Are you prepared for the reckoning and the crossing of the bridge? What single deed can you begin today to tip your scale toward mercy?

Quranic Evidence for the Sudden Hour
Buti cites Quranic verses to explain the Hour's sudden arrival.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic basis for the sudden arrival of the Hour and the cessation of life.

Core Idea
The Hour arrives suddenly through a single blast.

Buti grounds belief in the Hour's arrival directly in the Quran. He presents two vivid verses that depict the end of life and the resurrection as sudden, overwhelming events. This lesson examines those verses and their doctrinal significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses
Read both verses carefully: Az-Zumar 68 and Ya-Sin 49. Notice the imagery of the trumpet and the single shout.
The second verse mentions 'one blast' that seizes people while they are arguing.
2
Identify the two stages
In Az-Zumar 68, there are two trumpet blasts: first causes death, second causes resurrection. Contrast with Ya-Sin 49 which describes a single shout that brings immediate death.
Both emphasize suddenness.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself: why does Buti present these verses? They show that the Hour is not gradual but instant, and that this knowledge is sufficient for the believer.
4
Connect to broader belief
Link this to the Islamic creed: belief in the Hour is a pillar of faith, and the Quranic descriptions are primary evidence.
This lesson is part of the samiyyat (matters known through revelation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما ذلك كيف تقوم الساعة وتنعدم الحياة: حسبك لمعرفة ما يجب أن تعلمه من ذلك، أن تقرأ قوله تعالى: (ونُفِخَ في الصُّورِ فَصَعِقَ مَن في السَّمواتِ وَمَن في الأرضِ إِلا مَن شَاءَ اللهُ، ثم نفخ فيه أخرى فإذا هم قيام ينظرون) [الزمر: ٦٨] وأن تقرأ قوله تعالى: (ما ينظرون إلا صيحة واحدة تأخذهم وهم يخصمون، فلا يستطيعون توصية) [يس: ٤٩؟]
What is that and how does the Hour come and life cease? Sufficient for you to know what you must learn of that is that you read the saying of the Most High: 'And the trumpet will be blown, and whoever is in the heavens and whoever is on the earth will fall dead except whom Allah wills. Then it will be blown again, and at once they will be standing, looking on.' [Az-Zumar: 68] And that you read the saying of the Most High: 'They do not await except one blast which will seize them while they are disputing, and they will not be able to make a bequest.' [Ya-Sin: 49?]
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage provides the Quranic evidence for how the Hour (as-Sāʿah) will occur and life will cease (tanʿadim al-ḥayāt). Buti references two verses: first, Surah Az-Zumar 68, describing the trumpet blast (an-nafkhu fī aṣ-ṣūr) causing all creatures to fall dead except those Allah wills, followed by a second blast for resurrection. Second, a verse from Surah Ya-Sin (likely 49) describing a single shout (ṣayḥatun wāḥidatun) that seizes people suddenly while they are arguing. These verses illustrate the sudden, overwhelming nature of the Hour. The phrase 'ḥasbuka li-maʿrifah' indicates that these verses suffice for understanding the essential reality of the Hour.

Key Terms
الصور
الصعق
القيام
الصيحة الواحدة
الساعة
انعدام الحياة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Hour comes gradually over time.
Correction: The Quranic verses show it is sudden: a single blast or shout, not a process.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does Buti cite to describe the resurrection after the trumpet blast?
A) 'They do not await except one blast...'
B) 'Then it will be blown again, and at once they will be standing, looking on.'
C) 'The Day when the earth will be replaced...'
D) 'And the heaven will be split...'

Key Takeaway
The Hour arrives suddenly, as shown by the trumpet blast and single shout in the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the blast could come while you are disputing with someone today, what is one argument you would immediately want to resolve? Will you seek reconciliation now?
?
The second blast will raise you standing and looking on. What will you be looking for when you open your eyes? How does that vision change the way you live this hour?
?
You have learned that the Hour comes through a single, sudden event. What is one thing you are postponing in your relationship with Allah that you would do today if you knew the shout would come tonight?

The Hour and the Blowing of the Trumpet
Describes the Hour and the Trumpet, citing Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic concept of the Hour as the end of this world and the beginning of the Day of Resurrection, and the role of the Trumpet in initiating it, as revealed in the Quran.

Core Idea
The Hour begins with the Trumpet blast, an unseen event known only through revelation.

In this lesson, we explore the nature of the Hour as described in the Quran and the commentaries of scholars. The author explains that the Hour is not merely a metaphor but a real event that will end the current cosmic order. The key sign is the blowing of the Trumpet, which causes universal stunning. However, the exact details of this event remain known only to Allah, emphasizing the limits of human reason in matters of the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Hour as the boundary between two worlds
Read the passage's opening sentences describing the end of the universe and the beginning of a new creation. Notice how the author presents the Hour as the appointed moment known only to Allah.
The Hour is both an end and a beginning.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence for the Trumpet
Focus on the two Quranic verses cited (Az-Zumar 39:68 and Ya-Sin 36:49-50). The author uses them to establish the reality of the Trumpet and its two blasts.
The first blast stuns, the second resurrects.
3
Recognize the limits of rational knowledge about the Trumpet
The author states that the shape, location, and mechanism of the Trumpet are known only to Allah. This teaches that accepting these events is an act of faith, not rational deduction.
This is a key sam'iyyat doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تمهيد ثالثا يوم القيامة واحد الله
إذا تكاملت أشرط الساعة التي تحدثنا عنها، وجاء ميقات اللحظة المحددة المعلومة عند رب العالمين، والخفية عن عباده أجمعين، ذلك الميقات الذي ينتهي به أجل الدنيا بما فيها - حينئذ تنتهي الحياة من على هذه الأرض وسائر بقاع الكون الأخرى، وينتثر هذا النظام الكوني بأجمعه .. بعد أن ظل دهراً مديداً سائراً في خدمة مولاه، ملتزماً ما وضعه فيه من منهج لا ينحرف عنه. إنَّ خدمته الرتيبة هذه تنتهي في تلك اللحظة التي لا يعلم ميقاتها إلا الله عز وجل، ليبدأ من ورائها طور جديد من الخلق والتكوين والتنظيم.
فهذه النهاية التي تنعدم عندها الحياة من الكون وينهار عندها نظامه وتتبدل معالمه وتنتثر أجزاؤه، هو بدء ما يسميه القرآن، بالساعة ويوم القيامة. ثم تمتد هذه البداية إلى حشر الأجساد وإعادة أرواحها إليها، ثم إلى ما يتبع من طول حساب وميزان واجتياز صراط، إلى أن يستقر أصحاب الجنة في جنان خلودهم ويستقر أصحاب العذاب في سعيرهم.
كيف تقوم الساعة وتنعدم الحياة:
حسبك لمعرفة ما يجب أن تعلمه من ذلك، أن تقرأ قوله تعالى: ( ونفخ في الصور فصعق من في السماوات ومن في الأرض إلا من شاء الله، ثم نفخ فيه أخرى فإذا هم قيام ينظرون ) [ الزمر: 68] وأن تقرأ قوله تعالى: ( ما ينظرون إلا صيحة واحدة تأخذهم وهم يخصمون، فلا يستطيعون توصية ولا إلى أهلهم يرجعون ) [ يس: 49-50] ثم أن تؤمن بالأمر كما أخبر الله عز وجل.
فهنالك صور ( والصور هو البوق ) وهنالك نفخ يكون في الصور، تصعق له الأرواح، إلا من شاء الله أن لا يصعق بذلك. ويحتمل أن يكون المراد بهم أرواح الأنبياء والشهداء كما يحتمل أن يكونوا بعض الملائكة كإسرافيل وميكائيل وجبريل وملك الموت، وقد وردت أحاديث وأخبار بذلك، والله أعلم بمراده. وأين هذا الصور وكيف شكله وهيئته وما الذي يحدثه النفخ فيه حتى يترك هذا الأثر الغريب؟ علم ذلك كله عند الله عز وجل، ولو كشف لنا عن حقيقة شيء من ذلك لعلمنا، ولكن لا مجال للعقل أن يستيقن أي شيء عنه، إذ قد طوى الله علم ذلك عن عباده.
Third preamble: The Day of Resurrection (the one God?). When the conditions of the Hour that we have spoken about are complete, and the appointed time of the specific moment known to the Lord of the worlds, and hidden from all His servants, arrives—that appointed time which ends the term of this world including everything in it—then life ceases from this earth and the rest of the regions of the universe, and this entire cosmic order disintegrates, after having for a long age proceeded in service to its Master, adhering to the course He placed in it from which it does not deviate. Its constant service ends at that moment whose time none knows except Allah, Almighty and Majestic, so that from behind it a new phase of creation, formation, and organization begins. So this end, at which life ceases from the universe, its system collapses, its features change, and its parts scatter, is the beginning of what the Quran calls 'the Hour' and 'the Day of Resurrection'. Then this beginning extends to the gathering of bodies and the return of their souls to them, then to what follows of lengthy reckoning, weighing, crossing the Bridge, until the people of Paradise settle in their eternal gardens and the people of punishment settle in their blaze. How does the Hour come about and life cease? It suffices you to know what you must know of that, that you read the saying of the Most High: 'And the Trumpet will be blown, and whoever is in the heavens and whoever is on the earth will be stunned except whom Allah wills. Then it will be blown another time, and at once they will be standing, looking on' [Az-Zumar 39:68], and that you read the saying of the Most High: 'They do not await except one blast which will seize them while they are disputing, so they will not be able to make a bequest, nor to their families will they return' [Ya-Sin 36:49-50], then that you believe in the matter as Allah, Almighty and Majestic, has informed. So there is a Trumpet (and the Trumpet is a horn), and there is a blowing that occurs in the Trumpet, which stuns the souls, except whom Allah wills not to be stunned by that. And it is possible that what is meant by them are the souls of the prophets and martyrs, and it is also possible that they are some of the angels like Israfil, Mika'il, Jibra'il, and the Angel of Death. Narrations and reports have been transmitted about that, and Allah knows best His intent. And where is this Trumpet, and how is its shape and appearance, and what does the blowing in it produce that it leaves this strange effect? All of that knowledge is with Allah, Almighty and Majestic. If He had revealed to us the reality of something of that, we would know, but there is no scope for the intellect to be certain of anything about it, since Allah has concealed the knowledge of that from His servants.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a definition and description of the Hour (as-Sa'ah) and the Day of Resurrection (Yawm al-Qiyamah). The author begins by explaining that when the predetermined conditions are fulfilled, the appointed moment arrives, ending life in this world and the entire cosmic order. This end is the beginning of a new phase: the resurrection, reckoning, and final abodes. The author then turns to the Quranic evidence for how the Hour occurs, citing two verses: one about the Trumpet causing universal stunning, and another about a single blast that seizes people suddenly. From these verses, the author extracts the reality of the Trumpet (Sur) and the blowing (Nafkh) that stuns souls, with exceptions for whom Allah wills. The author then discusses possible identities of those exceptions (prophets, martyrs, certain angels) but emphasizes that the precise nature of the Trumpet—its location, shape, and mechanism—is known only to Allah. Human reason cannot grasp it; it is a matter of faith in the unseen. The key point is that acceptance of these events is based solely on divine revelation, not rational deduction.

Key Terms
الساعة
يوم القيامة
الصور
النفخ
الصعق
الحشر
الميزان
الصراط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The exact mechanism of the Hour and the nature of the Trumpet can be known through reason or scientific inquiry.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the details of the Trumpet and the Hour are hidden from human intellect and can only be accepted through faith in divine revelation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary event that initiates the Hour?
A) The occurrence of natural disasters
B) The blowing of the Trumpet (Sur)
C) The outbreak of human wars
D) The death of all living creatures

Key Takeaway
The Hour is a real, divinely ordained event initiated by the Trumpet blast, and its true nature is known only to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Hour will seize people while they are engaged in disputes (يخصمون). What is a dispute or worldly distraction that occupies your heart, and how will you release it so you are not caught unaware?
?
You know that the Trumpet could sound at any moment. If you were to face the first blast today, what would you regret not having done for your faith? Write down one concrete change you will make this week to live in readiness.
?
Allah has concealed the exact nature of the Trumpet from you. Does your heart accept this hiddenness with trust, or do you find yourself wishing for proofs beyond revelation? How can you strengthen your iman in the unseen?

Refuting Nuclear Weapons as an Explanation of the Hour
Refutes the nuclear weapons explanation of the Hour.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why speculative interpretations of the Hour using nuclear weapons are invalid from an Islamic theological perspective, based on the Quranic description of the Trumpet and the nature of the unseen.

Core Idea
Nuclear weapons are irrelevant to the Hour; only Allah's Trumpet affects all souls.

In this passage, the author addresses a modern attempt to rationalize the events of the Hour by linking them to nuclear warfare. He firmly rejects this as an inadmissible speculation that contradicts the Quran. As you read, notice how he bases his refutation on the specific effect of the Trumpet on all souls, which no human weapon can replicate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the author's tone and the key arguments he presents.
The author uses strong language like 'majhala' (ignorance) to condemn the interpretation.
2
Identify the two grounds of refutation
The author rejects the nuclear weapons explanation on two grounds: (1) it is an impermissible venture into speculative ignorance, and (2) it directly contradicts the Quranic description of the Trumpet. Find these in the text.
3
Reflect on the rhetorical question
Consider the force of the author's question: 'What effect do atomic bombs have on the souls of angels and the dead?' This shows the fundamental mismatch between human weapons and the divine event.
4
Consider the implications for belief
Think about why the author stresses that no human conflict or weapon plays a role in establishing the Hour. How does this protect the concept of the unseen from materialist explanations?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمهم أن تعلم أن لا مدخل لتهارج الناس وحروب الأمم مع بعضها وما يعقب ذلك من استعمال أسلحة فتاكة مدمرة - لا مدخل لشيء من ذلك في إقامة الساعة وإنهاء الحياة كما أخبر الله. ولعل بعض من يحبون أن يستبقوا الأشياء في الحديث عنها حسب تخيلاتهم، يطيب لهم أن يتخذوا من الأسلحة الذرية الحديثة تفسيراً لكيفية قيام الساعة، ويظنون أن فيما يقدمون عليه من هذا التفسير، تسهيلاً للإيمان بيوم القيامة على الشاكين والملحدين. ولكن هذا خوض في مجهلة لا ينبغي الخوض فيها بحال، واجتهاد في أمر لا مجال فيه للاجتهاد والنظر، عدا أنه يخالف نصوص القرآن، على ما قد رأيت، كل المخالفة. ويغيب عن هؤلاء الذين يتجرؤون على هذا الخوض بطيب نية وحسن طوية، أن نفخ الصور الذي أخبر الله عنه، تصعق له الأرواح كلها بما في ذلك أرواح الأحياء والأموات وأرواح الناس والملائكة والجان. وأين هذا مما تفعله القنابل الذرية والهيدروجينية بالغة من الخطورة والفتك مهما بلغت؟ وأي أثر أو سلطان لها على الملائكة وأرواح الموتى؟
And the important thing is that you know that there is no entry for the clamor of people and the wars of nations with each other and what follows that of using deadly destructive weapons—there is no entry for any of that in establishing the Hour and ending life, as Allah has informed. Perhaps some of those who like to anticipate things in speaking about them according to their imaginations deem it good to take modern atomic weapons as an interpretation of how the Hour occurs, and they think that in what they offer of this interpretation there is facilitation of belief in the Day of Resurrection for doubters and atheists. But this is an involvement in ignorance (majhala) that should not be engaged in at all, and an exercise of opinion in a matter for which there is no scope for opinion and reflection, besides that it contradicts the texts of the Quran, as you have seen, completely. And it escapes those who dare to engage in this with good intention and goodwill, that the blowing of the Trumpet which Allah has informed about stuns all souls, including the souls of the living and the dead, and the souls of humans, angels, and jinn. And where is this relative to what atomic and hydrogen bombs do, however great their danger and destruction may be? And what effect or authority do they have over the angels and the souls of the dead?
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of attempts to explain the Hour through human means, specifically modern nuclear weapons. The author states categorically that there is no role for human conflicts or destructive weapons in bringing about the Hour; the event is solely as Allah informed. He then identifies a contemporary error: some people, with good intentions, try to interpret nuclear weapons as the mechanism of the Hour, thinking this makes belief easier for skeptics. The author condemns this as an unacceptable venture into ignorance (majhala) and an invalid exercise of opinion where none is allowed. Moreover, it contradicts the Quranic texts. The core argument is that the Trumpet's blowing stuns all souls—living and dead, humans, angels, and jinn—whereas nuclear weapons only affect material bodies and cannot affect angels or the souls of the dead. Therefore, such interpretations are fundamentally flawed. The author uses a rhetorical question to emphasize the point: what effect could bombs have on angels and the dead? The refutation is based on two grounds: the Quranic description of the Trumpet's effect on all souls, and the prohibition of speculative interpretation in matters of the unseen.

Key Terms
الأسلحة الذرية
التفسير التخيلي
المجهلة
نفخ الصور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Nuclear weapons could be the literal or metaphorical cause of the end of the world, making belief in the Hour easier for modern people.
Correction: The Hour is brought about solely by Allah's command through the Trumpet, which affects all souls (including angels and the dead), something no human weapon can do.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject interpreting nuclear weapons as the mechanism of the Hour?
A) Because nuclear weapons are not powerful enough to end the world
B) Because the Trumpet affects all souls, including angels and the dead, which weapons cannot
C) Because such interpretation makes belief harder for atheists
D) Because it is based on weak hadith

Key Takeaway
Speculative interpretations of the unseen, however well-intentioned, are invalid when they contradict Quranic texts and the nature of divine acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you tempted to explain aspects of the unseen (like the Hour) using modern science to make faith more 'credible' to others or even to yourself? Where do you need to simply submit to Allah's description without rationalization?
?
When you think about the events of the Hour, do you truly believe it will happen exactly as Allah described—through the Trumpet—or do you secretly harbor doubts that reduce it to a natural disaster? What would change if you fully accepted it as a separate, divine act?
?
Have you ever imposed your own reasoning on a matter of faith because it felt more comfortable or digestible? How can you train yourself to say 'I hear and I obey' even when your mind struggles to comprehend?

The Reality of the Trumpet and Its Blowing
Buti describes the Trumpet, its blowing, and the limits of human knowledge about it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the Trumpet (الصور) and the blowing that stuns souls, as described in the Qur'an and Sunnah, and why its specifics are known only to Allah.

Core Idea
The Trumpet is real and its blowing stuns all souls except those Allah exempts, but its nature remains unseen.

This lesson begins by establishing the requirement to believe in the unseen matters as Allah informed. It then describes the Trumpet, the blowing, and the effect on souls, noting that some souls may be exempted. Finally, it emphasizes that the exact reality of the Trumpet is unknown to human intellect.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the obligation to believe
The passage starts with a command to believe in the matter as Allah informed. This establishes the foundation that accepting the unseen is an act of faith.
This sets the tone for the entire discussion.
2
Identify the Trumpet and its blowing
The text defines the Trumpet as a horn and describes that a blowing will stun all souls, except those Allah wills to exempt. Notice the exception indicates divine mercy.
The exempted souls may include prophets, martyrs, or specific angels.
3
Accept the limits of knowledge
The author emphasizes that the location, shape, and mechanism of the Trumpet are known only to Allah. The intellect cannot ascertain these details, so we must submit to the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أن تؤمن بالأمر كما أخبر الله عـز وجل . فهنالك صور ) والصور هو البوق ( وهنالك نفخ يكون في الصور ، تصعق له الأرواح ، إلا من شاء الله أن لا يُصعق بذلك . ويحتمل أن يكون المراد بهم أرواح الأنبياء والشهداء كما يحتمل أن يكونوا بعض الملائكة كإسرافيل وميكائيل وجبريل وملك الموت ، وقد وردت أحاديث وأخـبـار بـذلـك ، والله أعلم بمراده وأين هذا الصور وكيف شكله وهيئته وما الذي يحدثه النفخ فيه حتى يترك هذا الأثر الغريب ؟ علم ذلك كله عند الله عز وجل ، ولو كشف لنا عن حقيقة شيء ذلك لعلمنا ، ولكن لا مجال للعقل أن يستيقن أي شيء عنه ، إذ قد طوى الله من علم ذلك عن عباده والمهم أن تعلم أن لا مدخل لتهارج الناس وحروب الأمم مع بعضها وما يعقب ذلك من استعمال أسلحة فتاكة مدمرة - لا مدخل لشيء من ذلك في إقامة الساعة وإنهاء الحياة كما أخبر الله . ولعل بعض من يحبون أن يستبقوا الأشياء في الحديث عنها حسب تخيلاتهم ، يطيب لهم أن يتخذوا من الأسلحة الذرية الحديثة تفسيراً لكيفية قيام الساعة ، ويظنون أن فيما يقدمون عليه من هذا التفسير ، تسهيلاً للإيمان بيوم القيامة على الشاكين والملحدين . ولكن هذا خوض في مجهلة لا ينبغي الخوض فيها بحال ، واجتهاد في أمر لا مجال فيــه للاجتهاد والنظر ، عدا أنه يخالف نصوص القرآن ، على ما قد رأيت ، كل المخالفة . ويغيب عن هؤلاء الذين يتجرؤون على هذا الخوض بطيب نية وحسن طوية ، أن نفخ الصور الذي أخبر الله عنه ، تصعق له الأرواح كلها بما في ذلك أرواح الأحياء والأموات وأرواح الناس والملائكة والجان . وأين هذا مما تفعله القنابل الذرية والهيدروجينية بالغة من الخطورة والفتك مهما بلغت ؟ وأي أثر أو سلطان لها على الملائكة وأرواح الموتى ؟
Then that you believe in the matter as Allah Almighty informed. There is the Trumpet (and the Trumpet is the horn), and there is a blowing that will be in the Trumpet, by which souls will be stunned, except those whom Allah wills not to be stunned by that. And it is possible that the intended are the souls of the prophets and martyrs, and it is possible that they are some of the angels like Israfil, Mika'il, Jibril, and the Angel of Death, and there have come hadiths and reports about that, and Allah knows best His intent and where this Trumpet is and how its shape and form, and what the blowing in it causes until it leaves this strange effect? All knowledge of that is with Allah Almighty, and if He had revealed to us the reality of something of that, we would know, but there is no avenue for the intellect to be certain of anything about it, since Allah has concealed knowledge of that from His servants. The important thing is that you know that there is no entry for the quarrels of people and the wars of nations among themselves and what follows that of using destructive deadly weapons—there is no entry for any of that in establishing the Hour and ending life as Allah has informed. Perhaps some of those who like to anticipate things in talking about them according to their imaginations find it pleasant to take modern nuclear weapons as an explanation for how the Hour will be established, and they think that in what they are doing of this explanation, there is facilitation of belief in the Day of Resurrection for doubters and atheists. But this is wading into ignorance that should not be waded into at all, and exertion in a matter in which there is no room for exertion and reflection, besides that it contradicts the texts of the Qur'an, as you have seen, completely. And it escapes these people who dare to wade into this with good intention and good will, that the blowing of the Trumpet that Allah has informed about will stun all souls, including the souls of the living and the dead, and the souls of humans, angels, and jinn. And where is this from what atomic and hydrogen bombs do, however great their danger and destruction may be? And what effect or authority do they have over angels and the souls of the dead?

Commentary
This passage discusses the reality of the Trumpet (الصور) and its blowing, and refutes attempts to interpret the events of the Hour through modern weapons. The author begins by stating that belief in the unseen matters is required. He then identifies the Trumpet as a horn (بوق) and describes that a blowing will cause all souls to be stunned except those Allah exempts, possibly prophets, martyrs, or certain angels. He emphasizes that the exact nature and location of the Trumpet are known only to Allah, and the intellect cannot determine them. He warns against wading into ignorance and reminds that the matter is purely supernatural.

Refutation of Interpreting the Trumpet with Nuclear Weapons
Buti refutes interpreting the Trumpet as nuclear weapons and clarifies the supernatural nature of the Hour.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why interpreting the Trumpet's blowing as nuclear weapons is false and contradicts the Qur'anic texts.

Core Idea
The Trumpet's blowing affects all souls, including angels and the dead, which no weapon can do.

This lesson addresses a common modern attempt to rationalize the events of the Hour by equating the Trumpet's blowing with the effect of nuclear weapons. The author strongly refutes this, arguing that such interpretations stem from ignorance and contradict the Qur'an. He emphasizes that the Trumpet's blowing affects all souls—living, dead, humans, angels, jinn—whereas weapons have no effect on angels or deceased souls.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the false interpretation
The author states that some people try to explain the Hour's establishment using nuclear weapons, thinking it makes belief easier for doubters.
This is a contemporary attempt to rationalize eschatology.
2
Understand the refutation
He refutes this as wading into ignorance and contradicting the Qur'an. There is no room for personal reasoning in such matters.
The refutation is strong: it is not merely wrong but a violation of divine texts.
3
Compare the effects
The Trumpet's blowing stuns all souls, including those of angels and the dead. Nuclear weapons only affect physical bodies and cannot harm souls or angels.
This comparison highlights the fundamental difference between supernatural and natural events.
4
Conclude the lesson
Affirm that the Hour is a purely divine, supernatural event, not caused by human warfare or technology.

But this is wading into ignorance that should not be waded into at all, and exertion in a matter in which there is no room for exertion and reflection, besides that it contradicts the texts of the Qur'an, as you have seen, completely. And it escapes these people who dare to wade into this with good intention and good will, that the blowing of the Trumpet that Allah has informed about will stun all souls, including the souls of the living and the dead, and the souls of humans, angels, and jinn. And where is this from what atomic and hydrogen bombs do, however great their danger and destruction may be? And what effect or authority do they have over angels and the souls of the dead?
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage discusses the reality of the Trumpet (الصور) and its blowing, and refutes attempts to interpret the events of the Hour through modern weapons. The author begins by stating that belief in the unseen matters is required. He then identifies the Trumpet as a horn (بوق) and describes that a blowing will cause all souls to be stunned except those Allah exempts, possibly prophets, martyrs, or certain angels. He emphasizes that the exact nature and location of the Trumpet are known only to Allah, and the intellect cannot determine them. Then he strongly criticizes those who try to explain the Hour's occurrence using nuclear or hydrogen bombs, arguing that such explanations contradict the Qur'anic texts and ignore that the Trumpet's blowing affects all souls, including angels and the dead, whereas weapons have no effect on them. He warns against wading into ignorance and reminds that the matter is purely supernatural.

النفخ

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Trumpet's blowing is equivalent to the effect of nuclear weapons, making the Hour a natural event.
Correction: The Trumpet's blowing affects all souls including angels and the dead, while weapons only affect physical bodies. This contradicts the Qur'anic description.

Checkpoint
According to the text, why can't nuclear weapons be the explanation for the Trumpet's blowing?
A) They are not powerful enough.
B) They only affect physical bodies, not souls of angels and the dead.
C) They are not mentioned in the Qur'an.
D) They are a product of human technology.

Key Takeaway
Interpreting the Trumpet as nuclear weapons is false because the Trumpet's blowing stuns all souls, whereas weapons have no effect on angels or the deceased.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt the need to 'update' Islamic teachings about the Hereafter with modern science to make them believable? What does that desire reveal about your trust in Allah's words alone, and will you commit to accepting the supernatural as described in the Qur'an without reducing it?
?
When you read that the Trumpet's blowing stuns all souls—including yours—do you feel the weight of that reality in your daily life? How would your today change if you truly believed that a single blast could end your existence and bring you before Allah?
?
This lesson refutes the attempt to explain the Trumpet with nuclear weapons. Are there other areas of your faith where you have tried to explain away the miraculous to fit human logic? Will you repent and submit fully, even when it defies your understanding?

The Greatest Unseen News: The Day of Judgment
Buti enumerates the reasons for the supreme importance of the Day of Judgment and the Qur'an's emphasis on it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Day of Judgment is described as the most dangerous and greatest unseen news, and how the Qur'an emphasizes it above all other topics.

Core Idea
The Day of Judgment is the ultimate reality that gives meaning to all human existence.

Buti opens by declaring that the Day of Judgment is the most momentous unseen news ever conveyed. He then unfolds three profound reasons for its supreme importance—from its awe-inspiring strangeness, to the personal accountability before Allah, to the fact that our entire worldly life is a preparation for that meeting. This passage sets the stage for understanding why the Qur'an returns to this topic again and again.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the repeated phrase 'أخطرها وأعظمها' which structures the argument.
The author uses rhythmic repetition to emphasize gravity.
2
Identify the three reasons
The passage gives three reasons why the Hour is the greatest unseen news. Find each one and understand how they build on each other.
The reasons are: 1) strangeness of what awaits, 2) the day of accountability, 3) the purpose of life.
3
Reflect on the Qur'anic emphasis
Notice the author's claim that no other topic in the Qur'an is emphasized as much as the Day of Resurrection. Ask yourself: why would that be?
This connects the doctrinal point to the scripture's own pattern.
4
Apply to your own understanding
Consider how this teaching should affect a Muslim's outlook on life. The passage says life is preparation for that meeting.
This is a practical takeaway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأدلة على قيام الساعة : اعلم يا أخي المسلم أن قيام الساعة أخطر الأخبار الغيبية التي أخبر عنها الخالق جل جلاله ، على الإطلاق . هو أخطرها وأعظمها ، من حيث شدة الغرابة والبعد عن مألوف الإنسان وتصوراته ، ومن حيث ما ينتظر الإنسان إذ ذاك من العذاب المذهل الذي لا يكاد يتصوره الخيال ، أو النعيم الخالد الذي ينطوي على ما لا عين رأت ولا أذن سمعت ولا خطر على قلب بشر . وهو أخطرها وأعظمها ، من حيث إنه اليوم الذي يقف فيه هذا الإنسان ذليلاً مهيناً ضعيفاً بين يدي خالقه يكلمه ويحاسبه ويسأله عن النقير والقطمير وعن كل صغير وكبير ، بعد أن مرّ في مفازة هذه الدنيا يسمع عنه ولا يراه ولعله أيضاً لا يؤمن به . وهو أخطرها وأعظمها ، لأن عليه مدار وجود هذا الإنسان كله . فحـيـاتـه اليوم مع ما فيها من كدح ورزق وسعي وعقل وشهوات وأهواء كل ذلك تمهيد لملاقاة خالقه في هذا اليوم فمن أجل خطورة هذا الحدث العظيم من هذه النواحي كلها ، يظل القرآن يخبر الإنسان عنه وينذره إياه في تأكيد متوال لا ينقطع ، ولا تكاد تمر على صحيفة في هذا الكتاب العظيم إلا وتجد فيها حديثاً عن يوم القيامة وتنبيهاً للإنسان إليه . ولن تجد خبراً حفل به كتاب الله تعالى في تأكيد شديد لـه بشتى الأساليب العربية المختلفة ، كخبر يوم القيامة ، ولن تجد فيه تنبيهاً إلى عظيم وتحذيراً من خطير ، وبتفنن عجيب في النظم والأسلوب ، كتنبيهه الناس إلى الـقـيـامـة يوم . وتحذيرهم مما سيلاقونه فيه
The evidences for the establishment of the Hour: Know, O my Muslim brother, that the establishment of the Hour is the most dangerous of the unseen news that the Creator, exalted is His majesty, has informed about, absolutely. It is the most dangerous and greatest of them, in terms of extreme strangeness and distance from human familiarity and perceptions, and in terms of what awaits man then of stunning punishment that imagination can hardly conceive, or eternal bliss that contains what no eye has seen, no ear has heard, and has not occurred to a human heart. And it is the most dangerous and greatest of them, in that it is the day on which this man stands humiliated, abased, weak before his Creator, speaking to Him, being reckoned, and being asked about the pimple on a date stone and the thin membrane and about every small and great, after he passed through the wilderness of this world hearing about Him and not seeing Him, and perhaps also not believing in Him. And it is the most dangerous and greatest of them, because on it depends the entire existence of this man. So his life today with what is in it of toil, provision, striving, intellect, desires, and whims, all of that is preparation for meeting his Creator on this day. Because of the gravity of this great event from all these aspects, the Qur'an continues to inform man about it and warn him of it in uninterrupted successive emphasis, and hardly a page passes in this great book except you find in it mention of the Day of Resurrection and a reminder to man of it. And you will not find any news that the Book of Allah Almighty has taken care of with intense emphasis in various different Arabic styles like the news of the Day of Resurrection, and you will not find in it a warning of something great and a caution from something dangerous, with amazing artistry in composition and style, like His warning people to the Day of Resurrection and warning them of what they will meet therein.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage presents the evidences for the Day of Judgment and explains its supreme importance. The author begins by stating that the Day of Judgment is the most dangerous of all unseen reports. He then enumerates three reasons for its supreme significance: 1) Its extreme strangeness beyond human imagination, involving unimaginable punishment or bliss. 2) It is the day of standing humbly before Allah, being held accountable for every small and big deed. 3) All of human life in this world is merely preparation for that meeting. Because of this gravity, the Qur'an emphasizes it continuously with every style of Arabic rhetoric, making it the most repeated topic in the entire Book. He concludes that no other subject receives such intense and varied emphasis.

Correction: This passage shows it is the most emphasized topic, appearing on nearly every page and warned about with the strongest rhetorical devices.

Checkpoint

C) Because it is mentioned only a few times in the Qur'an.
D) Because it is related to nuclear weapons.

Key Takeaway
The Day of Judgment is the most emphasized topic in the Qur'an because it is the ultimate purpose and accountability point for human life.

?
On that day you will be asked about 'the pimple on a date stone.' What small thing are you neglecting that you will be accountable for? Will you start accounting yourself now?

The Gravity of the Day of Resurrection and the Qur'an's Emphasis
The author explains why the Day of Resurrection is the greatest unseen event and why the Quran repeatedly warns about it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Day of Resurrection is the greatest unseen event and how the Qur'an's repeated emphasis serves as proof of its reality.

Core Idea
The Day of Resurrection is the unseen par excellence; the Qur'an's intense emphasis proves its reality.

Sheikh Ramadan al-Buti explains that the Day of Resurrection is the most important and strangest of all unseen reports. He highlights three reasons for its supreme gravity and shows that the Qur'an's unparalleled emphasis on it is itself a proof of its truth. This lesson examines that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English to grasp the author's main point about the gravity of the Hour.
Notice the three reasons he gives starting with 'وهو أخطرها وأعظمها'.
2
Identify the three reasons for the Hour's gravity
The author lists three aspects: its strangeness, the humiliation of man, and its role as the purpose of life. Find each one.
These reasons build a cumulative case for why the Qur'an must emphasize it.
3
Understand the Qur'an's emphasis as proof
The author argues that because the Hour is so far from human experience, the Qur'an uses every rhetorical device to warn about it. This very emphasis is a sign of its truth.
The author quotes Qaf 22 to illustrate the unveiling.
4
Reflect on the takeaway
Consider how the Qur'an's frequent warnings strengthen faith in the unseen.
This lesson helps you appreciate the importance of the Day of Resurrection.

اعلم يا أخي المسلم أن قيام الساعة أخطر الأخبار الغيبية التي أخبر عنها الخالق جل جلاله ، على الإطلاق .
هو أخطرها وأعظمها ، من حيث شدة الغرابة والبعد عن مألوف الإنسان وتصوراته ، ومن حيث ما ينتظر الإنسان إذ ذاك من العذاب المذهل الذي لا يكاد يتصوره الخيال ، أو النعيم الخالد الذي ينطوي على ما لا عين رأت ولا أذن سمعت ولا خطر على قلب بشر

وهو أخطرها وأعظمها ، لأن عليه مدار وجود هذا الإنسان كله . فحـيـاتـه اليوم مع ما فيها من كدح ورزق وسعي وعقل وشهوات وأهواء كل ذلك تمهيد لملاقاة خالقه في هذا اليوم فمن أجل خطورة هذا الحدث العظيم من هذه النواحي كلها ، يظل القرآن يخبر الإنسان عنه وينذره إياه في تأكيد متوال لا ينقطع ، ولا تكاد تمر على صحيفة في هذا الكتاب العظيم إلا وتجد فيها حديثاً عن يوم القيامة وتنبيهاً للإنسان إليه

فلا جرم
أن هذه الإخبارات المنذرة والمنبهة والمحذرة في كتاب الله تعالى ، هو أعظم دليل وبرهان ، على قيام الساعة ويوم القيامة وكل ما يتبع ذلك من أحداث
The proofs for the establishment of the Hour: Know, O my Muslim brother, that the establishment of the Hour is the most dangerous of the unseen reports that the Creator, glorified be His majesty, has informed about, absolutely. It is the most dangerous and greatest of them, in terms of the intensity of its strangeness and distance from what is familiar to man and his perceptions, and in terms of what awaits man then of stunning torment that imagination can scarcely conceive, or eternal bliss that encompasses what no eye has seen, no ear has heard, and has never occurred to a human heart. And it is the most dangerous and greatest of them, in that it is the day when this man stands humiliated, degraded, weak before his Creator, speaking to Him, being reckoned, and being asked about the pit of a date-stone and the thin membrane on a date-stone, and about every small and great thing, after he has passed through the wilderness of this world hearing about Him but not seeing Him, and perhaps also not believing in Him. And it is the most dangerous and greatest of them, because upon it depends the entire existence of this man. So his life today, with all the toil, sustenance, striving, intellect, desires, and passions, all of that is a preparation for meeting his Creator on this Day. Because of the gravity of this momentous event from all these aspects, the Qur'an continues to inform man about it and warn him of it in unceasing successive emphasis, and you will hardly pass over a page in this great Book except that you find in it talk about the Day of Resurrection and a warning to man about it. And you will not find any report that the Book of Allah Almighty has lavished with such intense emphasis using various Arabic styles, like the report of the Day of Resurrection, and you will not find in it a warning about something great and a caution against something dangerous, with amazing artistry in composition and style, like its warning to people about the Day of Resurrection and its cautioning them against what they will encounter in it. All that is because it is something very distant and completely different from the reality of what they are in, what they see and feel. So it is one of the greatest unseen things veiled from man in this life; rather it is the unseen itself. It is the unseen which, when it is unveiled and disclosed, will appear to man's eye everything that he was almost denying and disbelieving, and his sight will become sharp, certain of it, not denying anything of it. And it is the covering about which the Qur'an said: "Indeed, you were heedless of this, so We have removed from you your covering, and your sight today is sharp." [Qaf: 22]. So no wonder that these warning, alerting, and cautioning reports in the Book of Allah Almighty are the greatest proof and evidence for the establishment of the Hour and the Day of Resurrection and all the events that follow that.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument for the reality of the Day of Resurrection (قيام الساعة) from the Qur'an's own emphasis. The author, Sheikh Ramadan al-Buti, begins by stating that the Hour is the most dangerous of all unseen reports. He then gives three reasons for its supreme importance: first, its strangeness and transcendence of human imagination, involving unimaginable torment or bliss; second, it is the day when man stands humiliated before his Creator and is called to account for everything; third, the entire purpose of human existence in this world is a preparation for that meeting. From these reasons, the author deduces that the Qur'an repeatedly and emphatically warns about the Hour, using every Arabic rhetorical device, more than any other topic. The reason for this intense emphasis is that the Hour is utterly unlike anything in human experience; it is the unseen par excellence. The author quotes Qur'an 50:22 to illustrate that at that time the veil will be lifted and sight will become sharp. He concludes that these Qur'anic reports themselves are the greatest proof of the Hour and its attendant events. The argument proceeds in the author's own order: first establishing the magnitude of the event, then linking that magnitude to the Qur'an's rhetorical emphasis, and finally concluding that the Qur'anic reports constitute sufficient evidence.

أخبار غيبية
تأكيد

Qur'anic Emphatic Style on the Day of Resurrection: An-Nisa 87
Author presents a Qur'anic verse as an example of emphatic style proving the Hour.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an uses intense rhetorical emphasis to affirm the reality of the Day of Resurrection, as exemplified in Surah an-Nisa, verse 87.

Core Idea
The Qur'an immerses the Day of Resurrection in emphatic language to dispel all doubt.

This lesson invites you to examine a single Qur'anic verse that demonstrates the Qur'an's unique emphatic style regarding the Hour. The author urges us to reflect with an alert heart and a discerning mind, recognizing the rhetorical devices that address our conscience, intellect, and emotions. By understanding these emphases, we can overcome the grip of worldly reality and prepare for the inevitable.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's call to reflect
Begin by reading the opening sentences where the author urges us to reflect on the verses with an alert heart and discerning mind. Notice the purpose: to overcome worldly attachments and awaken from heedlessness.
2
Examine the verse (An-Nisa 87)
Read the verse as quoted. Observe how it begins with a declaration of Allah's oneness, then an emphatic promise of gathering, followed by 'no doubt about it' and a rhetorical question.
Notice the author describes the verse as 'immersed' in emphasis.
3
Identify the emphatic elements
List the specific emphatic devices: the divine name, the oath-like structure (ليجمعنكم), the negation of doubt (لا ريب فيه), and the rhetorical question (ومن أصدق من الله حديثاً).
Each element reinforces certainty about the Day of Resurrection.
4
Connect to the broader argument
The author mentions that other verses follow a similar style of argument and debate to dispel skepticism. Reflect on how this verse functions as a powerful proof.
This verse is part of a larger Qur'anic pattern.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولنتأمل طائفة من هذه الآيات بقلب متيقظ وعقل متدبر ، ولنتنبه إلى ما فيها من فنون التأكيد المختلفة بشتى الوجوه والأساليب التي تخاطب في الإنسان وجدانه وعقله ومشاعره ، حتى يتغلب بذلك على الواقع الذي حصر كل خياله فيه وحتى يتحرر من سجن دنياه التي يعيش فيها ويستيقظ من الأحلام التي يتقلب فيها ، عسى أن يحسب لهذا الذي سيفجؤه عما قليل حسابه ويُعد له عدته

:
·
انظر إلى هذه الآية وتأمل في المؤكدات الشديدة التي كأنما غُمِسَت الآية فيها
ه الله لا إله إلا هُوَ ليَجْمَعَكُم إلى يوم القيامةِ لا رَيْبَ فِيهِ وَمَنْ أَصْدَقُ مِنَ الله حديثاً ﴾ [النساء : ٨٧ ] .
وانظر إلى هذه الآيات الأخرى التي سيقت مساق الحجاج والنقاش لتبديد ما يطوف بذهن الإنسان من عوامل الريب والشكوك حول إمكان وقوع هذا الأمر العظيم ، بأسلوب معجز يتجلى فيه سلطان الربوبية ، وبنفس التأكيد الذي رأيته في الآية السابقة :
And let us reflect on a group of these verses with an alert heart and a discerning mind, and let us pay attention to what is in them of various arts of emphasis in different ways and styles that address man's conscience, intellect, and emotions, so that by that he may overcome the reality that has confined all his imagination within it, and so that he may be freed from the prison of his world in which he lives and awaken from the dreams in which he tosses, hoping that he may take account of what will suddenly confront him before long and prepare for it. Immersion: Look at this verse and reflect upon the intense emphases as if the verse was immersed in them: "Allah, there is no deity except Him. He will surely assemble you on the Day of Resurrection, about which there is no doubt. And who is more truthful than Allah in statement?" [an-Nisa: 87]. And look at these other verses that were presented in the style of argument and debate to dispel what circulates in man's mind of factors of doubt and skepticism about the possibility of the occurrence of this great matter, with a miraculous style in which the sovereignty of Lordship manifests, and with the same emphasis that you saw in the previous verse:
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is an invitation to reflect on specific Qur'anic verses that illustrate the emphatic style used to affirm the reality of the Day of Resurrection. The author encourages the reader to examine these verses with an alert heart and a discerning mind, noting the various rhetorical techniques that appeal to human conscience, intellect, and emotions. The purpose is to help the reader overcome the grip of worldly reality and awaken from heedlessness. The author then presents the first example: Surah an-Nisa, verse 87. He points out that the verse seems to be 'immersed' in emphatic devices: the declaration of Allah's oneness, the oath-like structure (ليجمعنكم), the phrase 'no doubt about it', and the rhetorical question 'Who is more truthful than Allah in statement?' These all serve to remove any doubt about the gathering on the Day of Resurrection. The author then mentions that other verses follow in a similar vein, using argumentative styles and miraculous expression to dispel skepticism. The passage thus provides a concrete example of the Qur'an's unique rhetorical emphasis on the Hour.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Qur'an mentions the Hour without special emphasis, as a matter-of-fact statement.
Correction: This passage shows that the Qur'an uses intense rhetorical reinforcement, including oaths, negation of doubt, and rhetorical questions, to affirm the reality of the Hour.

Checkpoint
Which Qur'anic verse does the author present as an example of intense emphasis on the Day of Resurrection?
A) Surah al-Qaf, verse 22
B) Surah an-Nisa, verse 87
C) Surah al-Imran, verse 185
D) Surah al-Hajj, verse 7

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an employs a unique emphatic style—through oaths, negation of doubt, and rhetorical questions—to firmly establish the certainty of the Day of Resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the words 'لا ريب فيه' (no doubt about it), do you truly live with the certainty that the Day of Resurrection will come, or do your daily choices reveal a heart still attached to this world? What is one area of your life where you can replace hesitation with action based on that certainty, starting today?
?
The verse asks 'Who is more truthful than Allah in statement?'—if you believe Allah's statement is the most truthful, why do you still allow the doubts of your own mind or the distractions of society to outweigh His promise? Where in your routine do you need to intentionally remind yourself of this truth to reshape your priorities?

Quranic Warnings: The Greatest Proof for Resurrection
Buti declares Quranic warnings as the greatest proof for the resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti considers the Quran's warning announcements as the greatest evidence for the Day of Resurrection and its events.

Core Idea
The Quran's repeated warnings are the most powerful proof for the resurrection.

Buti has been building the case for the resurrection using rational arguments. Now he turns to the Quran itself. He declares that the Quran's own warning announcements are the greatest evidence. This lesson introduces that bold claim and invites us to contemplate the Quran's rhetorical power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read Buti's declaration in Arabic and English. Notice his emphatic language: 'فلا جرم' (it is no wonder) and 'أعظم دليل وبرهان' (the greatest evidence and proof).
Pay attention to the shift from rational to scriptural evidence.
2
Identify the central claim
What does Buti say the Quranic announcements are? He states they are the greatest proof for the resurrection and all that follows.
The phrase 'أعظم دليل وبرهان' is the key.
3
Understand the call to contemplation
Buti invites us to contemplate a group of verses with a vigilant heart and reflective mind, noting the various arts of emphasis.
Why does he emphasize multiple styles? To address the whole human being.
4
Reflect on the purpose
The goal is to overcome the confinement of worldly reality, liberate from the prison of this life, and awaken from heedlessness to prepare for the Hour.
This shows the practical aim of Quranic warnings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا جرم أن هذه الإخبارات المنذرة والمنبهة والمحذرة في كتاب الله تعالى، هو أعظم دليل وبرهان، على قيام الساعة ويوم القيامة وكل ما يتبع ذلك من أحداث. ولنتأمل طائفة من هذه الآيات بقلب متيقظ وعقل متدبر، ولنتنبه إلى ما فيها من فنون التأكيد المختلفة بشتى الوجوه والأساليب التي تخاطب في الإنسان وجدانه وعقله ومشاعره، حتى يتغلب بذلك على الواقع الذي حصر كل خياله فيه وحتى يتحرر من سجن دنياه التي يعيش فيها ويستيقظ من الأحلام التي يتقلب فيها، عسى أن يحسب لهذا الذي سيفجؤه عما قليل حسابه ويُعد له عدته.
It is no wonder that these warning, alerting, and cautioning announcements in the Book of Allah Almighty are the greatest evidence and proof for the establishment of the Hour and the Day of Resurrection and all that follows from that of events. And let us contemplate a group of these verses with a vigilant heart and a reflective mind, and let us pay attention to the various arts of emphasis in them in various ways and styles that address man's conscience, intellect, and emotions, so that he may thereby overcome the reality that has confined all his imagination, and so that he may be liberated from the prison of his world in which he lives and awaken from the dreams in which he tosses, hoping that he may calculate for this which will suddenly come to him soon and prepare his provision for it.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage transitions to the Quranic evidence. Buti asserts that the Quran's repeated warnings are the greatest proof for the resurrection. He then calls for a reflective examination of these verses, noting their diverse emphases that appeal to intellect, emotion, and conscience. The goal is to break free from the confines of worldly life and prepare for the inevitable Hour.

Key Terms
الإخبارات (al-ikhbarat, announcements)
الأدلة (al-adillah, proofs)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that proof for the resurrection must be empirical or scientific.
Correction: Buti argues that the Quran's rhetorical and logical depth, as seen in its warning announcements, constitutes the greatest proof.

Checkpoint

A) Stories of past nations
B) The greatest proof for the resurrection

D) Scientific facts

Key Takeaway
The Quran's own warning announcements are the greatest evidence for the resurrection, calling for deep contemplation to prepare for the Hour.

?

?
If the Hour could come at any moment, what provision have you actually prepared? Name one concrete thing you will do today to ready yourself.

Two Quranic Styles: Emphasis and Argument
Buti presents two Quranic styles: strong emphasis and argumentative debate with illustrative verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first two Quranic styles used to affirm resurrection: overwhelming emphasis and argumentative debate.

Core Idea
The Quran uses both emphatic assertion and logical argument to remove doubts about resurrection.

In this passage, Buti introduces how the Quran employs distinct rhetorical strategies to convince people of the reality of resurrection. He presents two styles: one that saturates the verse with emphatic language, and another that engages in direct argument and debate with the doubter. These verses show the Quran's ability to address both the heart and the mind.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the three Quranic verses cited
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the translation. Notice that Buti cites three sets of verses: an-Nisa 87, Maryam 66-68, and al-Anbiya 1-3.
The third set (al-Anbiya) is presented as a further example of a different emotional tone.
2
Identify the first style: strong emphasis
Look at verse an-Nisa 87. Observe the multiple emphatic elements: the negation 'لا إله إلا هو', the emphatic 'ليجمعنّ', the phrase 'لا ريب فيه', and the rhetorical question 'ومن أصدق من الله حديثا'. This style overwhelms the listener with certainty.
Buti calls this 'strong emphases in which the verse is immersed'.
3
Identify the second style: argumentative debate
Examine verse Maryam 66-68. Notice how it begins by quoting the skeptic's doubt, then rebuts it with a logical reminder of initial creation, and ends with an oath. This style mimics and defeats the doubter's reasoning.
Buti says these verses are 'presented in the manner of argument and debate'.
4
Reflect on the third set (al-Anbiya 1-3)
Read these verses and note the tone of regret and sorrow. This style appeals to emotion, warning the heedless. It complements the first two styles.
Buti uses this example to show the Quran's versatility.
5
Consider why multiple styles are used
Reflect on why the Quran would use different approaches for the same message. The commentary explains that different psychological states require different rhetorical strategies.
This connects to the core idea of the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
انظر إلى هذه الآية وتأمل في المؤكدات الشديدة التي كأنما غُمِسَت الآية فيها: ﴿ الله لا إله إلا هو ليجمعنكم إلى يوم القيامة لا ريب فيه ومن أصدق من الله حديثا ﴾ [النساء: ٨٧]. وانظر إلى هذه الآيات الأخرى التي سيقت مساق الحجاج والنقاش لتبديد ما يطوف بذهن الإنسان من عوامل الريب والشكوك حول إمكان وقوع هذا الأمر العظيم، بأسلوب معجز يتجلى فيه سلطان الربوبية، وبنفس التأكيد الذي رأيته في الآية السابقة: ﴿ ويقول الإنسان أإذا ما مت لسوف أخرج حيا. أو لا يذكر الإنسان أنا خلقناه من قبل ولم يك شيئا فوربك لنحشرنهم والشياطين ثم لنحضرنهم حول جهنم جثيا ﴾ [مريم: ٦٦-٦٨]. وتأمل في هذه الآيات الأخرى التي صاغها الخالق بأسلوب تتجلى فيه الحسرة والأسى على الناس الذين أسكرهم واقع ما هم فيه عن حقيقة ما سيرونه عن قليل، فما تنفعهم عظة ولا تؤثر فيهم ذكرى: ﴿ اقترب للناس حسابهم وهم في غفلة معرضون، ما يأتيهم من ذكر من ربهم محدث إلا استمعوه وهم يلعبون. لاهية قلوبهم ﴾ [الأنبياء: ١-٣].
Look at this verse and reflect on the strong emphases in which the verse is immersed: "Allah, there is no god but Him, surely He will gather you to the Day of Resurrection, of which there is no doubt. And who is more truthful than Allah in speech?" [an-Nisa: 87]. And look at these other verses that were presented in the manner of argument and debate to dispel the factors of doubt and suspicion that float in the human mind about the possibility of this great event occurring, in a miraculous style that manifests the authority of Lordship, and with the same emphasis that you saw in the previous verse: "And man says, 'When I am dead, shall I truly be brought forth alive?' Does not man remember that We created him before, while he was nothing? So by your Lord, surely We will gather them and the devils, then We will bring them around Hell, kneeling." [Maryam: 66-68]. And reflect on these other verses that the Creator shaped in a style that manifests regret and sorrow for people whose reality of what they are in has intoxicated them from the truth of what they will see shortly, so no admonition benefits them nor does a reminder have effect on them: "The reckoning of the people has drawn near, while they are in heedlessness, turning away. There comes to them no new reminder from their Lord but they listen to it while they play. Their hearts are distracted." [al-Anbiya: 1-3].
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage presents the first two Quranic styles. First, a verse with extreme emphasis (an-Nisa 87) where Allah swears by His oneness to assert resurrection. Second, a verse from Maryam that engages in human doubt and rebuts it by reminding of creation and swearing by the Lord. Third, a verse from al-Anbiya that combines regret and sorrow, showing how heedless people are. Buti points out the literary and psychological strategies: overwhelming emphasis, rational argument, and emotional appeal.

Key Terms
التأكيد (al-ta'kid)
الحجاج (al-hijaj)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Quranic proofs are purely emotional and lack logical structure.
Correction: Buti shows that the Quran also uses logical argument and debate (hijaj) to address doubt, as seen in Maryam 66-68.

Checkpoint
What is the common feature of the verses in this passage?
A) They are all about monotheism
B) They use emphasis and argument to affirm resurrection
C) They are all from the same surah
D) They are threats of punishment

Key Takeaway
The Quran employs diverse rhetorical strategies—emphasis, argument, and emotional appeal—to firmly establish the truth of resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the emphatic verse 'Allah, there is no god but Him, surely He will gather you to the Day of Resurrection, of which there is no doubt,' does your heart actually tremble with certainty, or do you find that doubt still creeps in? What specific thought or habit fuels that doubt, and what will you do today to replace it with trust in Allah's promise?
?
The Quran argues with you by reminding you that you were created from nothing. Have you ever truly paused to consider your own beginning—your utter non-existence—and let that destroy your pride and reinforce your hope in the afterlife? Write down one moment today when you will consciously recall your origin to silence a worldly worry.
?
Allah describes the heedless as having 'distracted hearts' (لاهية قلوبهم), too intoxicated by their current reality to remember the coming reckoning. In the past 24 hours, what distractions have stolen your heart from the reality of your meeting with Allah? Commit now to one specific change in your daily routine that will keep that reckoning near your heart.
