The Quranic Style of Divine Power
Buti introduces a verse invoking divine power to argue for resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran uses a display of divine power over the cosmos as a sign for the resurrection, and why human perception of greatness is relative.

Core Idea
Divine power makes resurrection easy for the All-Powerful.

Buti now presents a second Quranic style: invoking God's absolute power. The verse from Surat al-Anbiya reminds us that even the vast universe is like a scroll in God's hands, and our perception of its greatness is relative to our own weakness. This style refutes the denial of resurrection by showing that what seems impossible to us is trivial for the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and commentary
Begin by reading the verse from al-Anbiya (21:104) carefully along with Buti's commentary that precedes it. Note how he highlights the relativity of cosmic greatness.
The verse is: 'On the Day We shall fold up the heaven like the folding of a scroll for books...'
2
Understand the relative nature of greatness
Buti explains that the universe's grandeur is only perceived as great relative to human power. In reality, it is not absolute greatness. This is key to the argument.
3
Connect to the denial of resurrection
See how some people use the apparent permanence or vastness of the universe to deny that God can recreate it. Buti shows this is a fallacy because God's power is not bounded by human limitations.
This is the core lesson: divine power makes resurrection easy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وانظر إلى هذه الآية الأخرى كيف ينبه الخالق جل جلاله فيها العقل إلى ما يراه من عظمة هذا الكون بكل ما فيه، إنما هو بالنسبة لقدرة الإنسان فقط، فما ينبغي له أن يتخذ من العظمة التي ليست عظمةً في الواقع إلا بالنسبة لضعف الإنسان، دليلاً على إنكاره ليوم القيامة: ﴿ يوم نطوي السماء كطي السجل للكتب، كما بدأنا أول خلق نعيده، وعداً علينا إنا كنا فاعلين ﴾ [الأنبياء: ١٠٤]. وأحياناً أخرى، يظهر في مكان هذه الأساليب كلها أسلوب آخر هادئ. إنه أسلوب النظر العلمي ولفت العقل إلى ما ينبغي أن يتنبه إليه من مذاهب التأمل والفكر، في قالب تعليمي كأنه درس من أستاذ لتلاميذه وليس إخباراً من عظيم لعباده: ﴿ يا أيها الناس إن كنتم في ريب من البعث فإنا خلقناكم من تراب ثم من نطفة ثم من علقة ثم من مضغة مخلقة وغير مخلقة لنبين لكم ونقر في الأرحام ما نشاء إلى أجل مسمى ثم نخرجكم طفلاً ثم لتبلغوا أشدكم ومنكم من يتوفى ومنكم من يرد إلى أرذل العمر لكي لا يعلم من بعد علم شيئاً. وترى الأرض ﴾ [الحج: ٥].
And look at this other verse, how the Creator, exalted be His majesty, alerts the mind in it to what it sees of the greatness of this universe with everything in it—it is only relative to human power, so he should not take from greatness that is not greatness in reality except relative to man's weakness, a proof for his denial of the Day of Resurrection: "On the Day We shall fold up the heaven like the folding of a scroll for books; as We began the first creation We shall repeat it—a promise upon Us, indeed We are doers." [al-Anbiya: 104]. And other times, in place of all these styles, another calm style appears. It is the style of scientific reflection and turning the mind to what it should pay attention to from the methods of contemplation and thought, in an educational format as if it is a lesson from a teacher to his students, not an informing from the Great to His servants: "O you people, if you are in doubt about the Resurrection, indeed We created you from dust, then from a drop, then from a clinging clot, then from a lump of flesh, formed and unformed—to make clear to you. And We settle in the wombs what We will for a specified term, then We bring you out as a child, then that you may reach your maturity. And among you is he who is taken in death, and among you is he who is returned to the worst of age, so that he knows nothing after having known. And you see the earth..." [al-Hajj: 5].
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage presents two more styles. First, a verse from al-Anbiya that reminds of God's power to fold up the heavens, showing that human perception of greatness is relative. Buti warns against using the apparent smallness of cosmic phenomena as proof against resurrection. Second, a calm, educational style from al-Hajj that uses the stages of human creation as a logical argument for the possibility of resurrection. Buti notes this is like a teacher instructing students, not a mere announcement. The passage ends mid-verse, but the point about scientific reflection is clear.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudrah, power)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that the vastness and permanence of the universe disprove the possibility of resurrection.
Correction: Buti clarifies that the universe's greatness is only relative to human power; it is not absolute. God's power can easily fold it up and recreate it.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, why is it wrong to take the universe's greatness as proof against resurrection?
A) Because the universe is actually small
B) Because that greatness is only relative to human weakness, not absolute
C) Because the Quran says the universe will not last
D) Because resurrection is a matter of faith, not reason

Key Takeaway
The Quran uses the display of divine power over the cosmos to show that resurrection is easy for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever feel overwhelmed by the vastness of the world, and do you forget that Allah's power is infinitely greater than any difficulty you face? When you consider that He will fold the heavens like a scroll, what problem in your life seems small in comparison? Commit today to reminding yourself of this verse whenever anxiety strikes.
?
When you look at the scale of the universe, do you subconsciously doubt that Allah can manage your own small affairs? The same power that created the heavens can resurrect you and answer your du'as. What is one area of your life where you need to trust in His absolute power more? Write it down and make it a point of reliance.
?
The verse warns against using the apparent permanence of the cosmos to deny the afterlife. In what ways do you live as if this dunya will last forever, ignoring the reality of your own death? What is one attachment you need to loosen today because it contradicts your belief in the resurrection?

The Quranic Style of Scientific Reflection
Buti presents a calm, scientific Quranic style that uses human development as evidence for resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran employs calm, logical reasoning from observable creation to argue for resurrection, resembling a teacher instructing students.

Core Idea
The Quran uses scientific observation as a teacher, not a commander.

Buti now highlights a gentler Quranic style: scientific reflection. Instead of threats or commands, the Quran presents a step-by-step argument from human development to convince doubters of resurrection. The verse from al-Hajj reads like a biology lesson, tracing our origin from dust to maturity to old age, leading to the conclusion that God who originated life can restore it.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse from al-Hajj
Carefully read the verse (22:5) and Buti's description of it as an 'educational format' like a teacher to students.
The verse lists stages: dust, drop, clot, lump, bones, flesh, then growth to maturity.
2
Identify the stages of creation
Notice the detailed sequence: dust, then a drop (nutfah), then a clinging clot (ʿalaqah), then a lump of flesh (mudghah), both formed and unformed. This is a precise biological observation.
3
Appreciate the didactic tone
Buti emphasizes that this style is 'calm' and 'educational'—not a reprimand but an invitation to reflect. It uses human creation as a rational proof for the resurrection.
This contrasts with the earlier threatening styles.

The Analogy of Rain and Resurrection
Buti presents the Quranic verse that uses the rain-revival analogy as evidence for resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran uses the natural phenomenon of rain reviving dead earth as an analogy to prove the reality of resurrection.

Core Idea
The rain that brings life to barren land mirrors the resurrection of the dead.

Buti begins by citing a powerful Quranic verse from Surah al-Hajj that draws a direct analogy between the revival of dead earth by rain and the resurrection of the dead. This is one of the Quran's primary methods to make the abstract concept of the Hereafter tangible. The verse establishes the logical connection: just as Allah brings life to the earth, He will bring life to the dead.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse from Surah al-Hajj
Read the Arabic text and translation carefully. Notice how the verse moves from the natural observation to the theological conclusion.
The verse is a continuous argument.
2
Identify the analogy
Find the elements: dead earth, rain, life. See how this parallels resurrection.
3
Understand the conclusion
The verse explicitly states that the resurrection is certain. Reflect on the logical flow.
The conclusion is embedded in the verse itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هَامِدَةً فَإِذَا أَنزَلْنَا عَلَيْهَا الْمَاءَ اهْتَزَّتْ وَرَبَتْ وَأَنبَتَتْ مِن كُلِّ زَوْجٍ بَهِيجٍ، ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّ اللَّهَ هُوَ الْحَقُّ وَأَنَّهُ يُحْيِي الْمَوْتَى وَأَنَّهُ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ وَأَنَّ السَّاعَةَ آتِيَةٌ لَا رَيْبَ فِيهَا وَأَنَّ اللَّهَ يَبْعَثُ مَنْ فِي الْقُبُورِ ﴾ [ الحج : ٤ - ٧] . في حالات كثيرة أخرى، فإن الحديث عن يوم القيامة وأحداثه يأتي بأسلوب تصويري من شأنه أن يبدد ما بينه وبين الناس من حجب الغيب ومسافات الزمن، وينقلهم إلى جو هذه الأحداث حتى لكأنهم يشاهدونها بأعينهم، وقد خلّفوا أيامهم التي عاشوها في الدنيا من ورائهم وأخذ الندم يفري قلوب الجاحدين والمنكرين دون أي جدوى: ﴿ وَلا تَحْسَبَنَّ اللَّهَ غَافِلاً عَمَّا يَعْمَلُ الظَّالِمُونَ إِنَّا يُؤَخِّرُهُمْ لِيَوْمٍ تَشْخَصُ فِيهِ الْأَبْصَارُ مُهْطِعِينَ مُقْنِعِي رُؤوسِهِمْ لا يَرْتَدُّ إِلَيْهِمْ طَرْفُهُمْ وَأَفْئِدَتُهُمْ هَوَاءٌ، وَأَنذِرِ النَّاسَ يَوْمَ يَأْتِيهِمُ الْعَذَابُ فَيَقُولُ الَّذِينَ ظَلَمُوا رَبَّنَا أَخِّرْنَا إِلَى أَجَلٍ قَرِيبٍ نُجِبْ دَعْوَتَكَ وَنَتَّبِعِ الرُّسُلَ، أَوَ لَمْ تَكُونُوا أَقْسَمْتُمْ مِنْ قَبْلُ مَا لَكُمْ مِنْ زَوَالٍ ... ﴾ [ إبراهيم : ٤٢ - ٤٤ ] . ﴿ وَنُفِخَ فِي الصُّورِ فَإِذَا هُمْ مِنَ الْأَجْدَاثِ إِلَى رَبِّهِمْ يَنْسِلُونَ، قَالُوا يَا وَيْلَنَا مَنْ بَعَثَنَا مِنْ مَرْقَدِنَا ؟.. هَذَا مَا وَعَدَ الرَّحْمَنُ وَصَدَقَ الْمُرْسَلُونَ، إِنْ كَانَتْ إِلَّا صَيْحَةً وَاحِدَةً فَإِذَا هُمْ جَمِيعٌ لَدَيْنَا مُحْضَرُونَ ﴾ [ يس : ٥١ - ٥٣ ] . وربما عاد النظم القرآني، بعد كل هذه الأساليب المختلفة في التأكيد والبيان والتصوير، يلمس هذا الأمر على عجل لمسة المنذر الذي لم يعد يبالي أأيقن الجاحدون أم بعد، فقد جاءهم النذير واتضح المبهم وإن في ذلك لبلاغاً، انظر بعين قلبك إلى قوله: ﴿ لِكُلِّ نَبَإٍ مُسْتَقَرٌّ، وَسَوْفَ تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [الأنعام : ٦٧ ] . ﴿ يَسْأَلُونَكَ عَنِ السَّاعَةِ أَيَّانَ مُرْسَاهَا، فِيمَ أَنْتَ مِنْ ذِكْرَاهَا. إِلَى رَبِّكَ مُنْتَهَاهَا. إِنَّمَا أَنْتَ مُنْذِرُ مَنْ يَخْشَاهَا. كَأَنَّهُمْ يَوْمَ يَرَوْنَهَا لَمْ يَلْبَثُوا إِلَّا عَشِيَّةً أَوْ ضُحَاهَا ﴾ [ النازعات : ٤٢ - ٤٦ ] . وإن استقصاء الآيات التي تلح على الإنسان أن يتنبه بكل جوارحه وعقله ووجدانه الخطر هذا اليوم المقبل عليه وأن يعدَّ لذلك عدته ـ نقول إن استقصاء ذلك أمر يطول. فما عليك إلا أن تُقبل على كتاب الله جل جلاله وتتأمل ما يفيض به من حديث الساعة وشؤونها والأساليب المعجزة المختلفة في تأكيد أمرها وتحذير الإنسان من أن يخدعه أي خادع عنها فهذا دليل ما بعده دليل على قيام الناس بعد موتهم لرب العالمين.
[The earth is] lifeless, then when We send down water upon it, it quivers and swells and grows of every beautiful pair. That is because Allah is the Truth, and because He gives life to the dead, and because He is over all things competent, and because the Hour is coming, no doubt about it, and because Allah will resurrect those who are in the graves. [Surah al-Hajj: 4-7]. In many other instances, the talk about the Day of Resurrection and its events comes in a descriptive style [أسلوب تصويري] that would dissipate the veils of the unseen and the distances of time between it and the people, and transport them to the atmosphere of these events until they almost see them with their own eyes, having left behind the days they lived in the world and regret tearing the hearts of the deniers and rejecters without any benefit: {And do not think Allah is heedless of what the wrongdoers do. He only delays them for a Day when eyes will stare [in horror], hastening forward, raising their heads, their glance not returning to them, and their hearts are void. And warn the people of the Day when the punishment will come upon them, and those who did wrong will say, 'Our Lord, delay us for a short term; we will answer Your call and follow the messengers.' [They will be told], 'Did you not swear before that for you there would be no end?'} [Ibrahim: 42-44]. {And the Trumpet will be blown, and at once they will be from the graves to their Lord hastening. They will say, 'O woe to us! Who has raised us from our sleeping place?' [They will be told], 'This is what the Most Merciful had promised, and the messengers told the truth.' It will be only one blast, and at once they will be all before Us present.} [Ya Sin: 51-53]. And perhaps the Quranic discourse, after all these different methods of emphasis, clarification, and depiction, quickly touches on this matter with the touch of a warner who no longer cares whether the deniers become certain or not, for the warner has come to them and the obscure has become clear, and indeed in that is a message. Look with the eye of your heart at His statement: {For every news is a settled time, and you will come to know.} [Al-An'am: 67]. {They ask you about the Hour: when is its anchorage? In what [capacity] are you of its remembrance? To your Lord is its finality. You are only a warner for those who fear it. On the Day they see it, it will be as if they had not stayed [in the world] except an afternoon or its morning.} [Al-Nazi'at: 42-46]. And indeed, enumerating the verses that urge man to be alert with all his senses, mind, and consciousness to the danger of this coming Day and to prepare for it — we say that enumerating that is lengthy. So you have only to turn to the Book of Allah, exalted be His majesty, and contemplate what overflows from it of the discourse about the Hour and its affairs and the various miraculous methods in emphasizing its matter and warning man not to let any deceiver deceive him concerning it. For this is a proof after which there is no proof [i.e., an indisputable proof] of the resurrection of people after their death to the Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is a demonstration of Quranic methodology in presenting the Hereafter. Buti begins by citing a verse from Surah al-Hajj that uses the analogy of the dead earth revived by rain to illustrate resurrection. He then states that in many instances the Quran uses a vivid, descriptive style [أسلوب تصويري] to bring the Day of Judgment near to people's hearts, erasing the barriers of the unseen and the distance of time. He provides examples: the scene of the Day from Surah Ibrahim, the sudden resurrection from graves in Surah Ya Sin, and the concise warning from Surah al-An'am. Then he highlights the verse from Surah al-Nazi'at which succinctly describes the people's short stay in the world compared to the Hereafter. He concludes that enumerating all such verses is lengthy, but one should reflect on the Quran's emphasis on the Hour and its miraculous methods. This, he says, is an undeniable proof [دليل ما بعده دليل] of resurrection. The style is argumentative and illustrative, drawing on Quranic evidence.

Key Terms
الساعة
يحيي الموتى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the verse from Surah al-Hajj, what is the direct analogy for resurrection?
A) A seed growing into a tree
B) Rain reviving dead earth
C) A person waking from sleep
D) The sun rising each day

Key Takeaway
The Quran uses the natural cycle of rain and plant growth as a tangible analogy to prove the reality of resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see plants sprouting after rain, does your heart immediately connect that to Allah's promise of resurrection? If not, what distracts you from seeing His signs? Commit to pausing and making that connection next time you witness growth.
?
The verse says 'no doubt about it' regarding the Hour. Is there any corner of your heart that doubts the Hereafter? What specific action can you take today to strengthen your certainty?
?
If you truly believed that every dead person will be resurrected, how would that change the way you treat your own life and death? Write down one practical change you will make this week.

Unseen Matters
beginner
5 min
The Vivid Descriptive Style of the Quran
Buti explains the Quran's descriptive method and illustrates it with two vivid Quranic scenes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran uses vivid descriptive imagery to bring the events of the Day of Judgment to life, making them feel immediate and real.

Core Idea
The Quran's descriptive style collapses the distance between the present and the Hereafter, making it feel as if we are witnessing it now.

Buti then presents another powerful method: the Quran employs a vivid descriptive style (أسلوب تصويري) that erases the veils of the unseen and the distances of time. He provides two examples from Surah Ibrahim and Surah Ya Sin that paint a striking picture of the Day of Judgment, allowing the reader to almost see the events unfolding before their eyes.

Guided Path
1
Read the introductory sentence
Buti describes the effect of the Quran's descriptive style. Notice the key phrase: 'يبدد ما بينه وبين الناس من حجب الغيب ومسافات الزمن' (it dissipates the veils of the unseen and distances of time).
2
Study the first example from Surah Ibrahim
Read the verse from Surah Ibrahim (42-44). Visualize the scene: eyes staring, heads raised, hearts void, and the regret of the wrongdoers.
This is a dynamic description of the Day.
3
Study the second example from Surah Ya Sin
Read the verse from Surah Ya Sin (51-53). Notice the sudden blast of the trumpet and the immediate resurrection from graves.
The rapidity emphasizes the unexpected nature of the Hour.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Understand that this style aims to make the Hereafter feel near and impactful, not a distant abstract concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هَامِدَةً فَإِذَا أَنزَلْنَا عَلَيْهَا الْمَاءَ اهْتَزَّتْ وَرَبَتْ وَأَنبَتَتْ مِن كُلِّ زَوْجٍ بَهِيجٍ، ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّ اللَّهَ هُوَ الْحَقُّ وَأَنَّهُ يُحْيِي الْمَوْتَى وَأَنَّهُ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ وَأَنَّ السَّاعَةَ آتِيَةٌ لَا رَيْبَ فِيهَا وَأَنَّ اللَّهَ يَبْعَثُ مَنْ فِي الْقُبُورِ ﴾ [ الحج : ٤ - ٧] . في حالات كثيرة أخرى، فإن الحديث عن يوم القيامة وأحداثه يأتي بأسلوب تصويري من شأنه أن يبدد ما بينه وبين الناس من حجب الغيب ومسافات الزمن، وينقلهم إلى جو هذه الأحداث حتى لكأنهم يشاهدونها بأعينهم، وقد خلّفوا أيامهم التي عاشوها في الدنيا من ورائهم وأخذ الندم يفري قلوب الجاحدين والمنكرين دون أي جدوى: ﴿ وَلا تَحْسَبَنَّ اللَّهَ غَافِلاً عَمَّا يَعْمَلُ الظَّالِمُونَ إِنَّا يُؤَخِّرُهُمْ لِيَوْمٍ تَشْخَصُ فِيهِ الْأَبْصَارُ مُهْطِعِينَ مُقْنِعِي رُؤوسِهِمْ لا يَرْتَدُّ إِلَيْهِمْ طَرْفُهُمْ وَأَفْئِدَتُهُمْ هَوَاءٌ، وَأَنذِرِ النَّاسَ يَوْمَ يَأْتِيهِمُ الْعَذَابُ فَيَقُولُ الَّذِينَ ظَلَمُوا رَبَّنَا أَخِّرْنَا إِلَى أَجَلٍ قَرِيبٍ نُجِبْ دَعْوَتَكَ وَنَتَّبِعِ الرُّسُلَ، أَوَ لَمْ تَكُونُوا أَقْسَمْتُمْ مِنْ قَبْلُ مَا لَكُمْ مِنْ زَوَالٍ ... ﴾ [ إبراهيم : ٤٢ - ٤٤ ] . ﴿ وَنُفِخَ فِي الصُّورِ فَإِذَا هُمْ مِنَ الْأَجْدَاثِ إِلَى رَبِّهِمْ يَنْسِلُونَ، قَالُوا يَا وَيْلَنَا مَنْ بَعَثَنَا مِنْ مَرْقَدِنَا ؟.. هَذَا مَا وَعَدَ الرَّحْمَنُ وَصَدَقَ الْمُرْسَلُونَ، إِنْ كَانَتْ إِلَّا صَيْحَةً وَاحِدَةً فَإِذَا هُمْ جَمِيعٌ لَدَيْنَا مُحْضَرُونَ ﴾ [ يس : ٥١ - ٥٣ ] . وربما عاد النظم القرآني، بعد كل هذه الأساليب المختلفة في التأكيد والبيان والتصوير، يلمس هذا الأمر على عجل لمسة المنذر الذي لم يعد يبالي أأيقن الجاحدون أم بعد، فقد جاءهم النذير واتضح المبهم وإن في ذلك لبلاغاً، انظر بعين قلبك إلى قوله: ﴿ لِكُلِّ نَبَإٍ مُسْتَقَرٌّ، وَسَوْفَ تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [الأنعام : ٦٧ ] . ﴿ يَسْأَلُونَكَ عَنِ السَّاعَةِ أَيَّانَ مُرْسَاهَا، فِيمَ أَنْتَ مِنْ ذِكْرَاهَا. إِلَى رَبِّكَ مُنْتَهَاهَا. إِنَّمَا أَنْتَ مُنْذِرُ مَنْ يَخْشَاهَا. كَأَنَّهُمْ يَوْمَ يَرَوْنَهَا لَمْ يَلْبَثُوا إِلَّا عَشِيَّةً أَوْ ضُحَاهَا ﴾ [ النازعات : ٤٢ - ٤٦ ] . وإن استقصاء الآيات التي تلح على الإنسان أن يتنبه بكل جوارحه وعقله ووجدانه الخطر هذا اليوم المقبل عليه وأن يعدَّ لذلك عدته ـ نقول إن استقصاء ذلك أمر يطول. فما عليك إلا أن تُقبل على كتاب الله جل جلاله وتتأمل ما يفيض به من حديث الساعة وشؤونها والأساليب المعجزة المختلفة في تأكيد أمرها وتحذير الإنسان من أن يخدعه أي خادع عنها فهذا دليل ما بعده دليل على قيام الناس بعد موتهم لرب العالمين.
[The earth is] lifeless, then when We send down water upon it, it quivers and swells and grows of every beautiful pair. That is because Allah is the Truth, and because He gives life to the dead, and because He is over all things competent, and because the Hour is coming, no doubt about it, and because Allah will resurrect those who are in the graves. [Surah al-Hajj: 4-7]. In many other instances, the talk about the Day of Resurrection and its events comes in a descriptive style [أسلوب تصويري] that would dissipate the veils of the unseen and the distances of time between it and the people, and transport them to the atmosphere of these events until they almost see them with their own eyes, having left behind the days they lived in the world and regret tearing the hearts of the deniers and rejecters without any benefit: {And do not think Allah is heedless of what the wrongdoers do. He only delays them for a Day when eyes will stare [in horror], hastening forward, raising their heads, their glance not returning to them, and their hearts are void. And warn the people of the Day when the punishment will come upon them, and those who did wrong will say, 'Our Lord, delay us for a short term; we will answer Your call and follow the messengers.' [They will be told], 'Did you not swear before that for you there would be no end?'} [Ibrahim: 42-44]. {And the Trumpet will be blown, and at once they will be from the graves to their Lord hastening. They will say, 'O woe to us! Who has raised us from our sleeping place?' [They will be told], 'This is what the Most Merciful had promised, and the messengers told the truth.' It will be only one blast, and at once they will be all before Us present.} [Ya Sin: 51-53]. Commentary
This passage is a demonstration of Quranic methodology in presenting the Hereafter. Buti begins by citing a verse from Surah al-Hajj that uses the analogy of the dead earth revived by rain to illustrate resurrection. He then states that in many instances the Quran uses a vivid, descriptive style [أسلوب تصويري] to bring the Day of Judgment near to people's hearts, erasing the barriers of the unseen and the distance of time. He provides examples: the scene of the Day from Surah Ibrahim, the sudden resurrection from graves in Surah Ya Sin, and the concise warning from Surah al-An'am. Then he highlights the verse from Surah al-Nazi'at which succinctly describes the people's short stay in the world compared to the Hereafter. He concludes that enumerating all such verses is lengthy, but one should reflect on the Quran's emphasis on the Hour and its miraculous methods. This, he says, is an undeniable proof [دليل ما بعده دليل] of resurrection. The style is argumentative and illustrative, drawing on Quranic evidence.

Checkpoint
What does the descriptive style (أسلوب تصويري) accomplish according to Buti?
A) It confuses people about the Hereafter
B) It makes the Hereafter feel distant and abstract
C) It dissipates the veils of the unseen and distances of time
D) It only describes the punishment

Key Takeaway
The Quran's vivid descriptive style brings the Day of Judgment to life, making it nearly visible to the reader.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Quran’s style makes the Hereafter feel as if it is right in front of you. If you truly felt that the Trumpet could sound any moment, what one habit would you immediately change? Will you start today?

Unseen Matters

The Quick Warning and Final Proof
Buti presents the Quran's concise warning style and concludes that its overall presentation is an indisputable proof of resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran often concludes its discussion of the Hereafter with a concise, urgent warning, and how Buti asserts this as an indisputable proof of resurrection.

Core Idea
After multiple methods, the Quran delivers a sharp, no-nonsense warning that leaves no excuse for denial.

Buti notes that after using analogy and vivid description, the Quran sometimes returns to a brief, urgent tone – like a warner who has done his duty. He cites verses from Surah al-An'am and Surah al-Nazi'at that cut to the heart of the matter. He then concludes that the cumulative evidence from the Quran is an undeniable proof (دليل ما بعده دليل) for resurrection, urging the reader to study the Quran for themselves.

Guided Path
1
Read Buti's transition
Notice how Buti describes the Quran's shift to a quick warning. Key phrase: 'لمس هذا الأمر على عجل لمسة المنذر' (touches this matter quickly with the touch of a warner).
2
Study the warning verses
Read the verses from Al-An'am (67) and Al-Nazi'at (42-46). Notice their brevity and finality.
The nazi'at verse emphasizes the shortness of worldly life compared to the Hereafter.
3
Understand Buti's conclusion
Buti says that enumerating all such verses is lengthy, but the conclusion is clear: the Quran's various methods together form an indisputable proof.
He uses the phrase 'دليل ما بعده دليل' (a proof after which there is no proof).

هَامِدَةً فَإِذَا أَنزَلْنَا عَلَيْهَا الْمَاءَ اهْتَزَّتْ وَرَبَتْ وَأَنبَتَتْ مِن كُلِّ زَوْجٍ بَهِيجٍ، ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّ اللَّهَ هُوَ الْحَقُّ وَأَنَّهُ يُحْيِي الْمَوْتَى وَأَنَّهُ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ وَأَنَّ السَّاعَةَ آتِيَةٌ لَا رَيْبَ فِيهَا وَأَنَّ اللَّهَ يَبْعَثُ مَنْ فِي الْقُبُورِ ﴾ [ الحج : ٤ - ٧] . في حالات كثيرة أخرى، فإن الحديث عن يوم القيامة وأحداثه يأتي بأسلوب تصويري من شأنه أن يبدد ما بينه وبين الناس من حجب الغيب ومسافات الزمن، وينقلهم إلى جو هذه الأحداث حتى لكأنهم يشاهدونها بأعينهم، وقد خلّفوا أيامهم التي عاشوها في الدنيا من ورائهم وأخذ الندم يفري قلوب الجاحدين والمنكرين دون أي جدوى: ﴿ وَلا تَحْسَبَنَّ اللَّهَ غَافِلاً عَمَّا يَعْمَلُ الظَّالِمُونَ إِنَّا يُؤَخِّرُهُمْ لِيَوْمٍ تَشْخَصُ فِيهِ الْأَبْصَارُ مُهْطِعِينَ مُقْنِعِي رُؤوسِهِمْ لا يَرْتَدُّ إِلَيْهِمْ طَرْفُهُمْ وَأَفْئِدَتُهُمْ هَوَاءٌ، وَأَنذِرِ النَّاسَ يَوْمَ يَأْتِيهِمُ الْعَذَابُ فَيَقُولُ الَّذِينَ ظَلَمُوا رَبَّنَا أَخِّرْنَا إِلَى أَجَلٍ قَرِيبٍ نُجِبْ دَعْوَتَكَ وَنَتَّبِعِ الرُّسُلَ، أَوَ لَمْ تَكُونُوا أَقْسَمْتُمْ مِنْ قَبْلُ مَا لَكُمْ مِنْ زَوَالٍ ... ﴾ [ إبراهيم : ٤٢ - ٤٤ ] . ﴿ وَنُفِخَ فِي الصُّورِ فَإِذَا هُمْ مِنَ الْأَجْدَاثِ إِلَى رَبِّهِمْ يَنْسِلُونَ، قَالُوا يَا وَيْلَنَا مَنْ بَعَثَنَا مِنْ مَرْقَدِنَا ؟.. هَذَا مَا وَعَدَ الرَّحْمَنُ وَصَدَقَ الْمُرْسَلُونَ، إِنْ كَانَتْ إِلَّا صَيْحَةً وَاحِدَةً فَإِذَا هُمْ جَمِيعٌ لَدَيْنَا مُحْضَرُونَ ﴾ [ يس : ٥١ - ٥٣ ] . وربما عاد النظم القرآني، بعد كل هذه الأساليب المختلفة في التأكيد والبيان والتصوير، يلمس هذا الأمر على عجل لمسة المنذر الذي لم يعد يبالي أأيقن الجاحدون أم بعد، فقد جاءهم النذير واتضح المبهم وإن في ذلك لبلاغاً، انظر بعين قلبك إلى قوله: ﴿ لِكُلِّ نَبَإٍ مُسْتَقَرٌّ، وَسَوْفَ تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [الأنعام : ٦٧ ] . ﴿ يَسْأَلُونَكَ عَنِ السَّاعَةِ أَيَّانَ مُرْسَاهَا، فِيمَ أَنْتَ مِنْ ذِكْرَاهَا. إِلَى رَبِّكَ مُنْتَهَاهَا. إِنَّمَا أَنْتَ مُنْذِرُ مَنْ يَخْشَاهَا. كَأَنَّهُمْ يَوْمَ يَرَوْنَهَا لَمْ يَلْبَثُوا إِلَّا عَشِيَّةً أَوْ ضُحَاهَا ﴾ [ النازعات : ٤٢ - ٤٦ ] . وإن استقصاء الآيات التي تلح على الإنسان أن يتنبه بكل جوارحه وعقله ووجدانه الخطر هذا اليوم المقبل عليه وأن يعدَّ لذلك عدته ـ نقول إن استقصاء ذلك أمر يطول. فما عليك إلا أن تُقبل على كتاب الله جل جلاله وتتأمل ما يفيض به من حديث الساعة وشؤونها والأساليب المعجزة المختلفة في تأكيد أمرها وتحذير الإنسان من أن يخدعه أي خادع عنها فهذا دليل ما بعده دليل على قيام الناس بعد موتهم لرب العالمين.
[The earth is] lifeless, then when We send down water upon it, it quivers and swells and grows of every beautiful pair. That is because Allah is the Truth, and because He gives life to the dead, and because He is over all things competent, and because the Hour is coming, no doubt about it, and because Allah will resurrect those who are in the graves. [Surah al-Hajj: 4-7]. In many other instances, the talk about the Day of Resurrection and its events comes in a descriptive style [أسلوب تصويري] that would dissipate the veils of the unseen and the distances of time between it and the people, and transport them to the atmosphere of these events until they almost see them with their own eyes, having left behind the days they lived in the world and regret tearing the hearts of the deniers and rejecters without any benefit: {And do not think Allah is heedless of what the wrongdoers do. He only delays them for a Day when eyes will stare [in horror], hastening forward, raising their heads, their glance not returning to them, and their hearts are void. And warn the people of the Day when the punishment will come upon them, and those who did wrong will say, 'Our Lord, delay us for a short term; we will answer Your call and follow the messengers.' [They will be told], 'Did you not swear before that for you there would be no end?'} [Ibrahim: 42-44]. {And the Trumpet will be blown, and at once they will be from the graves to their Lord hastening. They will say, 'O woe to us! Who has raised us from our sleeping place?' [They will be told], 'This is what the Most Merciful had promised, and the messengers told the truth.' It will be only one blast, and at once they will be all before Us present.} [Ya Sin: 51-53]. And perhaps the Quranic discourse, after all these different methods of emphasis, clarification, and depiction, quickly touches on this matter with the touch of a warner who no longer cares whether the deniers become certain or not, for the warner has come to them and the obscure has become clear, and indeed in that is a message. Look with the eye of your heart at His statement: {For every news is a settled time, and you will come to know.} [Al-An'am: 67]. {They ask you about the Hour: when is its anchorage? In what [capacity] are you of its remembrance? To your Lord is its finality. You are only a warner for those who fear it. On the Day they see it, it will be as if they had not stayed [in the world] except an afternoon or its morning.} [Al-Nazi'at: 42-46]. And indeed, enumerating the verses that urge man to be alert with all his senses, mind, and consciousness to the danger of this coming Day and to prepare for it — we say that enumerating that is lengthy. So you have only to turn to the Book of Allah, exalted be His majesty, and contemplate what overflows from it of the discourse about the Hour and its affairs and the various miraculous methods in emphasizing its matter and warning man not to let any deceiver deceive him concerning it. For this is a proof after which there is no proof [i.e., an indisputable proof] of the resurrection of people after their death to the Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is a demonstration of Quranic methodology in presenting the Hereafter. Buti begins by citing a verse from Surah al-Hajj that uses the analogy of the dead earth revived by rain to illustrate resurrection. He then states that in many instances the Quran uses a vivid, descriptive style [أسلوب تصويري] to bring the Day of Judgment near to people's hearts, erasing the barriers of the unseen and the distance of time. He provides examples: the scene of the Day from Surah Ibrahim, the sudden resurrection from graves in Surah Ya Sin, and the concise warning from Surah al-An'am. Then he highlights the verse from Surah al-Nazi'at which succinctly describes the people's short stay in the world compared to the Hereafter. He concludes that enumerating all such verses is lengthy, but one should reflect on the Quran's emphasis on the Hour and its miraculous methods. This, he says, is an undeniable proof [دليل ما بعده دليل] of resurrection. The style is argumentative and illustrative, drawing on Quranic evidence.

النذير
مستقر

Checkpoint
What does Buti mean by 'دليل ما بعده دليل' (a proof after which there is no proof)?
A) The Quran's proof is weak
B) There is no proof of resurrection
C) The Quran's presentation is an irrefutable proof
D) Buti himself is providing the final proof

Key Takeaway
The Quran's multifaceted presentation of the Hereafter is an indisputable proof of the reality of resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that the warner no longer cares whether you believe or not. Does that not terrify you? Have you truly let the reality of the Hour settle in your heart, or are you still putting off preparation?
?
Buti declares the Quran's presentation an indisputable proof. If you are not yet convinced enough to change your daily priorities, what deeper deception is keeping you blind? Will you today, right now, commit to reading the Quran with the intention of finding that proof?
?
The verses tell you that on the Day of Judgment, your entire worldly life will feel like a single afternoon. If you were to stand before Allah tonight, what would you say about how you spent that afternoon? What will you actually change starting tomorrow?

Rational Proof: The Impossibility of Absurdity in Creation
Buti presents a rational proof for the Hereafter: without it, human existence would be meaningless (ʿabath), impossible for Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why human life cannot be limited to birth and death, and why the Hereafter is rationally necessary.

Core Idea
Without the Hereafter, creation would be absurd—and absurdity is impossible for Allah.

In this passage, Buti presents a compelling rational argument for the necessity of the Hereafter. He argues that if our existence ended at death, the Creator's actions would be meaningless (ʿabath), which is impossible for Allah. This lesson unpacks the logic behind this proof and its implications for understanding divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the full argument. Note the key term 'عبث' (ʿabath).
The passage is a continuous argument; let the flow carry you.
2
Understand the concept of ʿabath
Buti states that ʿabath (vain, purposeless action) is among the most manifest impossibilities for Allah. Since Allah is perfectly wise, He cannot create without purpose.
This is the core premise of the proof.
3
Reflect on the three examples
Buti gives three types of people: the tyrant, the oppressed, and the lifelong sufferer. Their lives are incomplete without a sequel where justice is fulfilled.
These examples illustrate the need for an afterlife to restore balance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتبع هذا الدليل ما كنا قد أوضحناه من قبل، وهو أن مما لا يتصوره العقل أن تكون قصة الإنسان تبدأ من غلاف الولادة وتنتهي بغلاف الموت إلا إذا تصورنا أن الذي خلقه، وأطلق يده في الحياة إنما فعل ذلك عبثاً. وقد علمت أن العبث من أجلى صور المحالات بالنسبة لذات الله جل جلاله. إن قصة الإنسان في حياته هذه ليست إلا مقدمات مبتورة تتطلب نتائجها، كالفصل الصغير من الرواية المتكاملة. فالذي عاش حياته كلها فاجراً طاغياً يفسد في الأرض ولا يخلف عليها إلا آثار ظلمه وطغيانه، والذي عاش مستضعفاً مهيض الجناح تقبل عليه الرزايا من كل جانب ويتلقى لطمات الناس وظلمهم من كل صوب، والذي عاش مبتلى مصاباً في جسمه طوال حياته ورأى الناس كيف ينعمون دون أن يذوق شيئاً من نعيمهم. كل هؤلاء إنما عاشوا مع جزء يسير من قصة وجودهم في الكون ثم أسدل عليهم ستار الموت فاصلاً بين جزئي القصة، لا منهياً لها ومتماً لأحداثها. أجل، إن من سبق أن أراد لعقله أن لا يؤمن بوجود الخالق جل جلاله فهو أحرى أن لا يؤمن بالجزء الثاني من قصة الإنسان. وليس كثيراً عليه أن يتصور
And this proof is followed by what we have already explained before, which is that it is not conceivable to the intellect that the story of man begins from the envelope of birth and ends with the envelope of death unless we imagine that the One who created him and released his hand in life did that in vain (ʿabath). And you have known that ʿabath (vain action) is among the most manifest impossible things with respect to the essence of Allah, exalted be His majesty. Indeed, the story of man in this life of his is nothing but cut-off preludes awaiting their results, like a small chapter of a complete novel. So the one who lived his entire life as a wicked tyrant, spreading corruption in the land and leaving behind only the effects of his injustice and tyranny, and the one who lived weak with a broken wing, calamities coming upon him from every side and receiving the slaps of people and their oppression from every direction, and the one who lived afflicted and stricken in his body throughout his life and saw people how they enjoy without tasting any of their bliss — all of these only lived with a small part of the story of their existence in the universe, then the curtain of death was drawn over them, separating the two parts of the story, not ending it and completing its events. Yes, indeed, the one who previously willed for his intellect not to believe in the existence of the Creator, exalted be His majesty, is more likely not to believe in the second part of the story of man. And it is not too much for him to imagine...
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof for the Hereafter based on the impossibility of ʿabath (meaninglessness) in Allah's actions. Buti begins by restating the proof they have previously explained: the human story cannot rationally be limited to birth and death unless we imagine that the Creator acted in vain (عبث). But ʿabath is impossible for Allah, because He is perfect and wise. So there must be a continuation after death. He then compares human life to a truncated chapter from a complete story, giving three examples: the oppressive tyrant, the oppressed weak person, and the lifelong sufferer. Their lives are incomplete without a sequel where justice is fulfilled. Death does not end the story but separates its two parts. Finally, he notes that those who deny the Creator will likely deny the afterlife, but it is not difficult for them to conceive it (perhaps implying that the rational evidence is clear).

Key Terms
عبث
غلاف الولادة
غلاف الموت
مقدمات مبتورة
الجزء الثاني من القصة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many people think life is only about worldly enjoyment and suffering, with no ultimate purpose or justice.
Correction: Buti argues that if there were no afterlife, the creation of humans with such varied fates would be meaningless (عبث), which is impossible for Allah. Therefore, there must be a continuation after death where justice is fulfilled.

Checkpoint
What does Buti say is impossible for Allah?
A) Creating an incomplete story.
B) Acting in vain (ʿabath).
C) Delaying punishment.
D) Resurrecting the dead.

Key Takeaway
Human life is only a fragment of a larger story; without the Hereafter, it would be absurd—and absurdity is impossible for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own life, do you live as though it is a complete story or a fragment awaiting completion? How does this perspective change what you prioritize today?
?
If you truly believe that every injustice you have suffered or witnessed will be rectified in the Hereafter, how does that change your reaction to oppression and your hope for justice right now?
?
You claim to believe in Allah's wisdom—yet do you live as if this life is all that matters? What would you do differently if you truly acted on the conviction that this life is only the first chapter?

The Rational Necessity of the Hereafter
Buti presents a rational proof for resurrection based on the impossibility of futility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti argues that the incompleteness of this life logically requires a resurrection, because otherwise creation would be futile.

Core Idea
Life's unfinished story demands a sequel; futility is impossible for Allah.

Buti builds a rational proof for the resurrection based on the nature of human existence. He argues that if this life were the whole story, then the tyrant, the oppressed, and the afflicted would have lived only a fragment. This would imply that Allah created them in vain, which is impossible. Therefore, there must be a continuation—the Hereafter—to complete the narrative.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening Quranic verse
Reflect on the verse (79:42-46) that Buti cites to set the tone: worldly life is brief compared to the Hereafter.
2
Identify the rational argument
Look for the phrase 'it is not possible for the intellect' and understand the point: a story that begins with birth and ends with death is incomplete unless it is futile, but futility is impossible for Allah.
The examples of the tyrant, the oppressed, and the afflicted illustrate this incompleteness.
3
Understand the consequence
If one denies the second part (resurrection), then one must accept futility in creation, which contradicts Allah’s wisdom.
Buti connects this to the prior discussion on God's existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إنما أنت مُنذِرُ مَن يَخشاها . كَأَنَّهُم يَومَ يَرَونَها لَمْ يَلبثوا إلا عَشِيَّةً أو ضحاها ﴾ [ النازعات : ٤٢ - ٤٦ ] . وإنَّ استقصاء الآيات التي تلح على الإنسان أن يتنبه بكل جوارحه وعقلـه ووجدانه الخطر هذا اليوم المقبل عليه وأن يعدَّ لذلك عـدتـه ـ نقول إن استقصاء ذلك أمر يطول . فما عليك إلا أن تُقبل على كتاب الله جل جلاله وتتأمل ما يفيض به من حديث الساعة وشؤونها والأساليب المعجزة المختلفة في تأكيـد أمرها وتحذير الإنسان من أن يخدعه أي خادع عنها فهذا دليل ما بعده دليل على قيام الناس بعد موتهم لرب العالمين يتصوره ويتبع هذا الدليل ما كنا قد أوضحناه من قبل ، وهو أن مما لا العقل أن تكون قصة الإنسان تبدأ من غلاف الولادة وتنتهي بغلاف الموت إلا إذا تصورنا أن الذي خلقه ، وأطلق يده في الحياة إنما فعل ذلك عبثاً . وقد علمت أن العبث من أجلى صور المحالات بالنسبة لذات الله جل جلاله إن قصة الإنسان في حياته هذه ليست إلا مقدمات مبتورة تتطلب نتائجها ، كالفصل الصغير من الرواية المتكاملة . فالذي عاش حياته كلها فاجراً طاغياً يفسد في الأرض ولا يخلف عليها إلا آثار ظلمه وطغيانه ، والـذي عـاش مستضعفاً مهيض الجناح تقبل عليه الرزايا من كل جانب ويتلقى لطمات الناس وظلمهم من كل صوب ، والذي عاش مبتلى مصاباً في جسمه طوال حياته ورأى الناس كيف ينعمون دون أن يذوق شيئاً من نعيمهم . كل هؤلاء إنما عاشوا مع جزء يسير من قصة وجودهم في الكون ثم أسدل عليهم ستــار المــوت فـاصـلاً بين جزئي القصة ، لا منهياً لها ومتماً لأحداثها أجل ، إن من سبق أن أراد لعقله أن لا يؤمن بوجود الخالق جل جلاله فهو أحرى أن لا يؤمن بالجزء الثاني من قصة الإنسان . وليس كثيراً عليه أن يتصور العبث في قصة هذا الإنسان على ظهر هذه الأرض بعد أن تصور العبث في وجود الكون كله . وقد علمت أننا إنما نخاطب من سبق أن كان معنا عند الحديث عن وجود الله وأدلة ذلك وعن بعثة الأنبياء وأدلة ذلك . وليس يغني القارئ شيئاً أن يتسمع إلى شيء مما نقول هنا ، وقد فاته الكثير ، مما قد ذكرناه في أصل هذا البحث كيفية حشر الأجساد وعودة أرواحها إليها لا يستطيع العلم أن يصف كيفية حشر الأجساد أو أن يحللها ويعللها بالطريقة العلمية التي يمارسها الإنسان في هذه الحياة ، وذلك لما كنا قد ذكرناه أن شأن العلم محصور في أنه يبدأ البحث بموضـوعـات تـوجـد في التجربة الخارجية البعيدة عن وحي العقل أو التفكير المحض ، ثم تفرض نفسها عليه طبق ما دلت عليه المشاهدة والتجربة ، وعلى العقل بعد ذلك أن يفسرها ويحللها من فقط والمعاد الجسمي لم يتحقق بعد ، ومعنى ذلك أنه لم يوجد بعد الموضوع الذي يستطيع العلم أن ينظر ويبحث فيه . فمن العبث إذا أن تسائل المجهر عن تحليل مالم يوضع تحته بعد من صنوف المركبات . كل مانملكه من نظر وبحث في هذا الموضوع ، هو أن نبدأ فنتساءل هل المعاد يكون بعد انعدام الأجساد من الوجود أصلاً ، أم بعد تفتت أجزائها وأجزاء أجزائها في طوايا الأرض أو بطون الحيتان أو أعماق البحار ؟ لم يرد بهذا أي خبر قطعي عن الله جل جلاله ، فليس علينا أن نجزم إذا بأن عدماً مطلقاً سيعتري الأشياء كلها قبل يوم القيامة ، أو أن نجزم بعكس ذلك ولكن الذي يجب الجزم به هو أن كل شيء ما عدا ذاته سبحانه وتعالى قابل في حقيقته للهلاك والعدم ، إذ إن الوجود وارد عليه من الخارج وليس نابعاً من حقيقته وجوهره ، سواء اعتراه بعد ذلك العدم فعلاً أو اعتراه التمزق والشتات والفساد .
You are only a warner for whoever fears it. On the day they see it, it will be as if they had not tarried but an afternoon or its forenoon. [Surat an-Nazi'at, 42-46]. And indeed, enumerating the verses that urge a person to be alert with all his senses, mind, and conscience to the danger of this approaching day and to prepare for it — we say that enumerating that is a lengthy matter. So you have only to turn to the Book of Allah, may His majesty be exalted, and reflect on what overflows from it of the talk of the Hour and its affairs, and the various miraculous methods in confirming its matter and warning a person not to be deceived by any deceiver about it. This is a proof beyond which there is no proof for the rising of people after their death to the Lord of the worlds. [?] And this proof is followed by what we had previously clarified, which is that it is not [possible] for the intellect that the story of a person begins from the envelope of birth and ends with the envelope of death unless we imagine that the One who created him and gave him free rein in life did so in vain. And you have known that futility is among the clearest forms of impossibilities with respect to the essence of Allah, may His majesty be exalted. Indeed, the story of a person in this life is only truncated preludes requiring their results, like a small chapter of a complete novel. So one who lived his entire life as a wicked tyrant, corrupting the earth and leaving behind nothing but traces of his oppression and transgression, and one who lived weak, broken-winged, receiving calamities from every side and enduring people's slaps and oppression from every direction, and one who lived afflicted, stricken in his body all his life, and saw people enjoying without tasting anything of their bliss — all these only lived with a small part of the story of their existence in the universe, then the curtain of death was drawn down upon them, separating the two parts of the story, not ending it and completing its events. Yes, whoever previously wanted his intellect not to believe in the existence of the Creator, may His majesty be exalted, is more likely not to believe in the second part of the story of a person. And it is not too much for him to imagine futility in the story of this person on the face of this earth after he imagined futility in the existence of the entire universe. And you have known that we only address those who previously were with us during the discussion of the existence of Allah and its proofs, and the sending of prophets and its proofs. And it does not benefit the reader at all to hear something of what we say here while he has missed much of what we mentioned in the origin of this discussion about the manner of gathering the bodies and the return of their souls to them. Science cannot describe the manner of gathering the bodies or analyze and explain it by the scientific method that a person practices in this life, because, as we have mentioned, the affair of science is confined to the fact that it begins research with subjects that exist in external experience, far from revelation of the intellect or pure thought, then they impose themselves upon it according to what observation and experience indicated, and then the intellect must interpret and analyze them from [?] only. And bodily resurrection has not yet occurred, meaning that the subject that science could look at and investigate does not yet exist. So it is futile to ask the microscope to analyze what has not yet been placed under it from the kinds of compounds. All that we possess of consideration and research on this topic is that we begin and ask: Does the resurrection occur after the complete annihilation of bodies from existence, or after the disintegration of their parts and the parts of their parts in the depths of the earth or the bellies of whales or the depths of the seas? No decisive news has come from Allah, may His majesty be exalted, about this. So we are not required to affirm that an absolute nothing will befall all things before the Day of Resurrection, nor to affirm the opposite. But what must be affirmed is that everything other than His essence, glorified and exalted is He, is in its reality susceptible to perishing and non-existence, because existence comes to it from outside and does not emanate from its reality and essence, whether subsequently it actually undergoes non-existence or undergoes fragmentation, dispersal, and corruption.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage presents a combined proof for the resurrection from Quranic warning, rational necessity, and the limits of scientific inquiry. The author begins with a Quranic verse (79:42-46) emphasizing the shortness of worldly life compared to the Hereafter, then asserts that studying all such verses is lengthy but beneficial. He declares the proof of resurrection definitive. Then he presents a rational argument: human life cannot logically begin with birth and end with death unless creation was futile (عبث), which is impossible for God. He illustrates with examples—the tyrant, the oppressed, the afflicted—each experiencing only a fragment of their story, with death separating the parts. Denying the Creator leads to denying the second part, and that requires accepting futility in the universe. The author clarifies his audience are those who already accept proofs of God and prophets. He then discusses the scientific impossibility of analyzing bodily resurrection: science requires empirical subjects, but resurrection has not yet occurred, so asking science to explain it is like asking a microscope to analyze a sample not yet placed under it. Finally, he addresses the nature of resurrection: whether after annihilation or disintegration, no definitive revelation is given, but what must be affirmed is that everything except God is fundamentally susceptible to perishing, since existence is given from outside.

Key Terms
العبث (futility)
المعاد (resurrection)
الجزء الثاني (second part)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that this life is the complete story and death is the end.
Correction: Buti argues that this life is only a fragment, and without a hereafter, creation would be futile—impossible for Allah.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what does the incompleteness of human life in this world rationally imply?
A) That death is the end of existence.
B) That there must be a second part (resurrection) to complete the story.
C) That human life is meaningless.
D) That the intellect cannot know anything about the afterlife.

Key Takeaway
Human life's incompleteness demands a sequel; otherwise creation would be futile, which is impossible for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the injustice and suffering you have witnessed or experienced, does it ever make you doubt that there is a just end? How does Buti's argument that these are 'truncated preludes' challenge you to trust that Allah's story for you is not yet complete? Tonight, before you sleep, take five minutes to name one specific injustice you have seen and ask Allah to complete it justly.
?
You have known that futility is impossible for Allah. But where in your own life have you been living as if your existence here is the whole story—building, chasing, or worrying as if death ends everything? What would change if you truly believed that your life is only the first chapter? Write down one concrete change you will make because of this truth.
?
The tyrant, the oppressed, the afflicted—you are one of these, or you know someone who is. Which of these three do you most identify with? And what does it mean for you personally that your story does not end with this world? Are you preparing for the sequel? If not, what is holding you back?

Why Science Cannot Analyze Bodily Resurrection
Buti explains the limits of science regarding resurrection and clarifies the rational position on the state of bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti argues that scientific analysis cannot be applied to bodily resurrection and what we can rationally affirm about the state of bodies before resurrection.

Core Idea
Science cannot study what hasn't happened yet; resurrection is beyond empirical investigation.

Buti addresses a common question: can science explain how resurrection occurs? He explains that science is limited to empirical observation. Since resurrection has not yet occurred, it cannot be studied scientifically. He then discusses what we can know rationally: whether bodies annihilate completely or disintegrate, no definitive revelation is given, but we must affirm their inherent contingency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on science's limitation
Focus on the statement: 'Science cannot describe the manner of gathering the bodies...' and understand why.
2
Understand the scientific method
Buti describes that science begins with subjects existing in external experience. Resurrection is not yet a subject.
The analogy of the microscope is useful.
3
Explore the rational discussion on the state of bodies
Buti then asks whether resurrection occurs after annihilation or disintegration, and concludes that we cannot be certain about the exact state, but everything besides Allah is susceptible to perishing.
This is a deeper theological point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إنما أنت مُنذِرُ مَن يَخشاها . كَأَنَّهُم يَومَ يَرَونَها لَمْ يَلبثوا إلا عَشِيَّةً أو ضحاها ﴾ [ النازعات : ٤٢ - ٤٦ ] . وإنَّ استقصاء الآيات التي تلح على الإنسان أن يتنبه بكل جوارحه وعقلـه ووجدانه الخطر هذا اليوم المقبل عليه وأن يعدَّ لذلك عـدتـه ـ نقول إن استقصاء ذلك أمر يطول . فما عليك إلا أن تُقبل على كتاب الله جل جلاله وتتأمل ما يفيض به من حديث الساعة وشؤونها والأساليب المعجزة المختلفة في تأكيـد أمرها وتحذير الإنسان من أن يخدعه أي خادع عنها فهذا دليل ما بعده دليل على قيام الناس بعد موتهم لرب العالمين يتصوره ويتبع هذا الدليل ما كنا قد أوضحناه من قبل ، وهو أن مما لا العقل أن تكون قصة الإنسان تبدأ من غلاف الولادة وتنتهي بغلاف الموت إلا إذا تصورنا أن الذي خلقه ، وأطلق يده في الحياة إنما فعل ذلك عبثاً . وقد علمت أن العبث من أجلى صور المحالات بالنسبة لذات الله جل جلاله إن قصة الإنسان في حياته هذه ليست إلا مقدمات مبتورة تتطلب نتائجها ، كالفصل الصغير من الرواية المتكاملة . فالذي عاش حياته كلها فاجراً طاغياً يفسد في الأرض ولا يخلف عليها إلا آثار ظلمه وطغيانه ، والـذي عـاش مستضعفاً مهيض الجناح تقبل عليه الرزايا من كل جانب ويتلقى لطمات الناس وظلمهم من كل صوب ، والذي عاش مبتلى مصاباً في جسمه طوال حياته ورأى الناس كيف ينعمون دون أن يذوق شيئاً من نعيمهم . كل هؤلاء إنما عاشوا مع جزء يسير من قصة وجودهم في الكون ثم أسدل عليهم ستــار المــوت فـاصـلاً بين جزئي القصة ، لا منهياً لها ومتماً لأحداثها أجل ، إن من سبق أن أراد لعقله أن لا يؤمن بوجود الخالق جل جلاله فهو أحرى أن لا يؤمن بالجزء الثاني من قصة الإنسان . وليس كثيراً عليه أن يتصور العبث في قصة هذا الإنسان على ظهر هذه الأرض بعد أن تصور العبث في وجود الكون كله . وقد علمت أننا إنما نخاطب من سبق أن كان معنا عند الحديث عن وجود الله وأدلة ذلك وعن بعثة الأنبياء وأدلة ذلك . وليس يغني القارئ شيئاً أن يتسمع إلى شيء مما نقول هنا ، وقد فاته الكثير ، مما قد ذكرناه في أصل هذا البحث كيفية حشر الأجساد وعودة أرواحها إليها لا يستطيع العلم أن يصف كيفية حشر الأجساد أو أن يحللها ويعللها بالطريقة العلمية التي يمارسها الإنسان في هذه الحياة ، وذلك لما كنا قد ذكرناه أن شأن العلم محصور في أنه يبدأ البحث بموضـوعـات تـوجـد في التجربة الخارجية البعيدة عن وحي العقل أو التفكير المحض ، ثم تفرض نفسها عليه طبق ما دلت عليه المشاهدة والتجربة ، وعلى العقل بعد ذلك أن يفسرها ويحللها من فقط والمعاد الجسمي لم يتحقق بعد ، ومعنى ذلك أنه لم يوجد بعد الموضوع الذي يستطيع العلم أن ينظر ويبحث فيه . فمن العبث إذا أن تسائل المجهر عن تحليل مالم يوضع تحته بعد من صنوف المركبات . كل مانملكه من نظر وبحث في هذا الموضوع ، هو أن نبدأ فنتساءل هل المعاد يكون بعد انعدام الأجساد من الوجود أصلاً ، أم بعد تفتت أجزائها وأجزاء أجزائها في طوايا الأرض أو بطون الحيتان أو أعماق البحار ؟ لم يرد بهذا أي خبر قطعي عن الله جل جلاله ، فليس علينا أن نجزم إذا بأن عدماً مطلقاً سيعتري الأشياء كلها قبل يوم القيامة ، أو أن نجزم بعكس ذلك ولكن الذي يجب الجزم به هو أن كل شيء ما عدا ذاته سبحانه وتعالى قابل في حقيقته للهلاك والعدم ، إذ إن الوجود وارد عليه من الخارج وليس ?

The Meaning of Annihilation (Fana') in Islamic Theology
Buti defines annihilation as disintegration, not non-existence, using language and Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and theological distinction between annihilation (fana') as disintegration and absolute non-existence, and how the Quran uses these terms to describe death.

Core Idea
Annihilation means disintegration and death, not nothingness.

Before exploring the nature of resurrection, we must clarify what happens at death. Buti begins by siding with the majority of scholars who interpret annihilation (fana') as the scattering of parts rather than absolute non-existence. He grounds this in both the Arabic language and Quranic usage, showing that 'perishing' and 'annihilation' refer to corruption and loss of function, not total disappearance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage on the majority view
Read from 'ولكن جمهور العلماء' to 'فتبين أن الفناء المعني إنما هو الموت'. Note the three Quranic verses cited.
Focus on the linguistic analysis of هلاك and فناء.
2
Understand the linguistic definitions
Buti explains that هلاك is applied when something becomes corrupted and loses its benefit, like a person dying or a house collapsing. Similarly, فناء applies when something breaks into useless fragments. Neither requires complete non-existence.
Key point: The word 'perish' can mean 'cease to function'.
3
Connect to Quranic usage
The verse 'كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْها فَانٍ' shows that فناء for living beings specifically means death, because God excepts His own essence. The earth itself perishes in a different sense (disintegration).
Notice how Buti restricts the meaning based on context.
4
Answer the checkpoint question
Test your understanding of the primary meaning of فناء for living beings as death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكن جمهور العلماء رجحوا القول الثاني وهو شتات الأجزاء وتفرقها . إذ هو ظاهر قوله تعالى : ﴿ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ هالك إلا وَجْهَهُ ﴾ [ القصص : ٨٨ ] وقوله تعالى : ﴿ كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍ وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الجلال والإكرام ﴾ [الرحمن : ٢٦ - ٢٧] وقوله تعالى : ﴿ قَدْ عَلِمُنا ما تَنقُصُ الأَرضُ مِنهُم وَعِنْدَنا كِتابٌ حَفِيظٌ ﴾ [ ق : ٤ ] فهلاك الشيء يطلق على فساده وخروجه عن أن يبقى منتفعاً به كما كان تقول هلك فلان ، أي مات ، وهلكت الدار إذا تقوضت ولم تعد صالحة للسكنى فيها ، ولا يشترط لإطلاق الهلاك الانعدام الكلي . والفناء كذلك ، تقول فني الثوب والعظم إذا أصبح كل منهما أنكاثاً وأجزاء متفرقة لا يستفاد منها لشيء ، ومما يؤكد أن المقصود بالفناء هو هذا الذي نقول ، بل خصوص الموت فقط ، قوله تعالى : ﴿ كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْها فَانٍ ﴾ ، أي كل من على الأرض فان ، فحكم بالفناء على الأحياء التي تكون على وجه الأرض واستثنى ذاته جل جلاله فتبين أن الفناء المعني إنما هو الموت ، أما الأرض ذاتها وما هو في حكمها فهي فانية بهذا المعنى من قبل[؟] . أما دلالة الآية الثانية ، فهي من حيث إنها رد على الذين استعظموا الحشر بعد الموت بقولهم : أإذا متنا وكنا تراباً ؟.. ذلك رجع بعيد ، إذ أجاب على إنكارهم واستعظامهم ذلك ، ببيان أن الله عز وجل يعلم مصير جسومهم التي ذابت في طوايا الأرض أو غيرها ، وعنده سجل يحوي عدد ذرات هذه الجسوم التي تفرقت في هذه الأمكنة ، ويضبط كل ذرة لصاحبها . فما العجب من تجميعها مرة أخرى كما تجمع برادة حديد امتزجت بين حفنة من التراب بواسطة قطعة من المغناطيس الجاذب ؟!

(۱) استعمال من التي هي للعاقل ليس تخصيصاً للفناء به ، وإنما هو من أجل أن المنتفع بالتخويف ذلك إنما هو العاقل فقط فخصه تعالى بالذكر .

فالآية دالة على أن الحشر يكون عن طريق تجميع الذرات من التفرق والشتات لا عن طريق إيجادها من العدم المطلق ، ويدل على هذا المعنى أيضاً قوله جل جلاله : ﴿ أَيَحْسَبُ الإنسانُ أَلَّنْ نَجْمَعَ عِظَامَهُ ، بَلَى ، قادرينَ عَلَى أَنْ نُسَوِّي بَنانَهُ ﴾ [ القيامة : ٣ - ٤ ] . وبهذا تعلم أن الذي يعود من الإنسان إلى التجمع والحياة إنما هو عين أجزائه التي عاش بها في الدنيا ، والمقصود بعين أجزائه ، عين أجزائه الأصلية التي بها استقبل الحياة ، أما ما زيد عليها بعد ذلك فلا يشترط أن يعاد بذاته ، وقد أطال في بحث ذلك علماء العقيدة والكلام ، وعلم ذلك في الحقيقة عند الله عز وجل . ولا سبيل لنا ، كما قلت لك ، إلى تحليل أو بيان شيء من الغيوب التي لم يكشف عنها الخالق جل جلاله سجاف غيبه بعد .

(۱) انظر ما كتبه في ذلك صاحب المواقف : ٢ / ٤٤٢ وسعد الدين التفتنازاني على العقائد النسفية : ٤٠٠ .
But the majority of scholars preferred the second view, which is the scattering of parts and their dispersal. For that is apparent from His statement: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' [al-Qasas 28:88] and His statement: 'Everyone upon it is perishing, and there remains the Face of your Lord, Possessor of Majesty and Honor' [al-Rahman 55:26-27] and His statement: 'We know what the earth diminishes of them, and with Us is a preserving record' [Qaf 50:4]. For 'perishing' of a thing is applied to its corruption and its exit from being beneficial as before; you say 'so-and-so perished' meaning he died, and 'the house perished' if it collapsed and is no longer fit for habitation. Complete non-existence is not required for the application of 'perishing'. And 'annihilation' is similar; you say 'the garment and the bone were annihilated' when each of them becomes fragmented and scattered parts from which nothing is derived. And what confirms that the intended meaning of 'annihilation' is this which we say, indeed specifically death only, is His statement: 'Everyone upon it is perishing', i.e., everyone on the earth is perishing. So He ruled annihilation upon the living beings that are on the face of the earth and excepted His Essence, so it becomes clear that the intended annihilation is indeed death. As for the earth itself and what is like it, they are annihilated in this sense beforehand[?]. As for the indication of the second verse, it is from the perspective that it is a response to those who deemed resurrection after death great, saying: 'When we are dead and become dust? That is a far return.' He responded to their denial and deeming it great by explaining that God Almighty knows the fate of their bodies that have dissolved in the earth's layers or elsewhere, and with Him is a record containing the number of atoms of these bodies that have scattered in these places, and it records every atom for its owner. So what wonder is there in gathering them again just as iron filings mixed in a handful of dust are gathered by a piece of magnetic magnet?!

(1) The use of 'man' (who) which is for rational beings is not a specification of annihilation to them, but rather because the one who benefits from the warning is only the rational being, so He specifically mentioned them.

Thus, the verse indicates that resurrection occurs through the gathering of atoms from dispersal and scattering, not through bringing them into existence from absolute non-existence. This meaning is also indicated by His statement: 'Does man think that We will not assemble his bones? Yes, We are able to proportion his fingertips' [al-Qiyamah 75:3-4]. And by this you know that what returns from man to assembly and life is exactly his parts with which he lived in the world, and by 'exactly his parts' is meant his original parts with which he received life. As for what was added to them afterwards, it is not required that it be returned in essence. The scholars of creed and kalam have elaborated on this research, and the knowledge of that in reality is with God Almighty. And there is no way for us, as I told you, to analyze or explain anything from the unseen things whose veil has not been lifted by the Creator.

(1) See what was written on that by the author of al-Mawaqif: 2/442 and Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani on al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya: 400.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument on the nature of death and resurrection. The author begins by stating that the majority of scholars prefer the view that death is the scattering and dispersal of body parts (شتات الأجزاء وتفرقها). He supports this with three Quranic verses: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' (28:88), 'Everyone upon it is perishing' (55:26-27), and 'We know what the earth diminishes of them' (50:4). He then explains the linguistic usage: 'halak' (perishing) is applied to corruption and loss of benefit, not necessarily absolute non-existence; for example, a person 'perishes' by dying, and a house 'perishes' by collapsing. Similarly, 'fana'' (annihilation) is used for disintegration into fragments, like a garment or bone becoming useless. He emphasizes that in the Quranic context, 'fana'' for living beings specifically means death, as the verse 'Everyone upon it is perishing' addresses the living on earth, while the earth itself perishes in a different sense (possibly by disintegration over time). The second verse (50:4) is a response to those who find resurrection improbable after death; God knows the fate of scattered bodies and has a precise record of all particles. The analogy of gathering iron filings with a magnet illustrates the possibility of reassembling scattered atoms. The author then concludes that resurrection is the gathering of atoms from dispersal, not creation from nothing, citing Surah al-Qiyamah (75:3-4) which mentions assembling bones and fingertips. Finally, he clarifies that the restored body consists of the original parts with which one began life, not additional parts acquired later; the precise details are known only to God, and humans cannot penetrate the unseen. The footnotes reference scholarly works.

Key Terms
هلاك
فناء
شتات الأجزاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Annihilation (fana') means absolute non-existence of the body.
Correction: Buti clarifies that fana' refers to disintegration and death, not complete disappearance; the parts remain scattered.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what does the term 'fana'' (annihilation) primarily mean for living beings?
A) Absolute non-existence
B) Death
C) Simple dispersal without death
D) Transformation into another substance

Key Takeaway
In Islamic theology, annihilation (fana') of living beings is understood as death and the disintegration of the body into scattered parts, not absolute non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that your own fana' means your body will literally break apart and return to dust, does that change how you view the urgency of preparing for what comes after? What one thing can you do today to live with that reality in mind?
?
The passage shows that 'fana'' does not require total non-existence—your body will be known and preserved in a record with God (Qaf 50:4). Are you living as though every action, every part of you, is being preserved and will be gathered again? What would change if you really believed that?
?
If the Quran uses 'fana'' for the living to mean death, and that is certain for all on earth except God, what are you doing today that will survive that 'fana'' in a way that matters to your Lord? Be specific: what legacy of faith or action will outlast the disintegration of your body?

Resurrection as Gathering of Dispersed Atoms
Buti argues resurrection gathers scattered atoms, citing Quran and reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and scriptural basis for resurrection as the gathering of scattered atoms rather than creation from nothing, and the distinction between original and acquired body parts.

Core Idea
Resurrection reassembles scattered atoms, not creates anew.

Having established that death means the scattering of parts, Buti now addresses the resurrection. He presents the Quranic response to skeptics who find it improbable, showing that God's knowledge and record-keeping make reassembly possible. Using the analogy of a magnet gathering iron filings, he illustrates how scattered atoms can be brought back. Finally, he clarifies that only the original parts of the body are restored, not all acquired matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on resurrection
Read from 'أما دلالة الآية الثانية' to the end of the passage. Focus on the argument and the analogy.
Note the response to the skeptics' objection.
2
Understand the Quranic argument
The verse Qaf 50:4 is a response to those who deem resurrection impossible. God knows the fate of bodies and has a precise record of every atom, so gathering them is easy.
The magnet analogy makes this concrete.
3
Learn the conclusion
Buti states that resurrection is the gathering of atoms from dispersal, not creation from nothing. He cites al-Qiyamah 75:3-4 as further evidence.
Note the phrase 'لا عن طريق إيجادها من العدم المطلق'.
4
Distinguish original vs. added parts
Buti explains that only the original parts (العين الأصلية) with which a person started life are restored. Additional parts acquired later are not necessarily returned.
This answers potential questions about bodily continuity.
5
Answer the checkpoint
Test your understanding of the key distinction between creation from nothing and gathering.

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument on the nature of death and resurrection. The author begins by stating that the majority of scholars prefer the view that death is the scattering and dispersal of body parts (شتات الأجزاء وتفرقها). He supports this with three Quranic verses: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' (28:88), 'Everyone upon it is perishing' (55:26-27), and 'We know what the earth diminishes of them' (50:4). Understanding al-Hisab: The Divine Accounting
Buti defines the accounting (hisab) and explains its wisdom in manifesting virtues and faults.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the divine accounting (al-Hisab) and the wisdom behind it as explained by Buti.

Core Idea
The divine accounting publicly manifests both the virtues of the pious and the faults of the disobedient.

In this passage, Buti provides a clear definition of the divine accounting (al-Hisab) — the moment when Allah discloses to His servants every deed they performed in this world. He then reveals the profound wisdom behind it: not merely punishment, but the public manifestation of the virtues of the pious and the faults of the disobedient, witnessed by all. This lesson establishes the reality and purpose of al-Hisab.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Focus on the definition of al-Hisab
Identify what al-Hisab is according to Buti: a disclosure by Allah to His servants of all their deeds before they leave the gathering place.
Note that the exact manner of this disclosure is known only to Allah.
3
Identify the wisdom (hikma) behind it
Find the purpose of this accounting: to manifest the virtues and merits of the pious and the faults and scandals of the disobedient.
This shows that the accounting is not merely punitive but also a display of divine justice and mercy.
4
Note the certainty of its occurrence
The passage states that Allah warned His servants about it in this world, so it must necessarily happen in the Hereafter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحساب وهو إطلاع الله عباده قبل انصرافهم من المحشر على كل ما قد جنوه في حياتهم الدنيا من تصرفات فعلية وقولية واعتقادية خيراً كانت أو شراً ، وذلك بالشكل أو الواسطة التي لا يعلمها أحد غيره . والحكمة من هذا الحساب أن يظهر الله فضائل المتقين ومناقبهم ، وفضائح العصاة ومثالبهم ، وذلك على رؤوس الأشهاد وسائر أهل العرصات . وهو مما أنذر الله به عباده في الدنيا ، فلا بد أن يتحقق في الآخرة . (۱) انظر ما كتبه في ذلك صاحب المواقف : ٢ / ٤٤٢ وسعد الدين التفتنازاني على العقائد النسفية : ٤٠٠ .
The accounting: it is God's disclosure to His servants before their departure from the gathering place of everything they have committed in their worldly life of deeds—actual, verbal, and doctrinal—whether good or evil, and that in the form or means that no one besides Him knows. And the wisdom behind this accounting is that God may manifest the virtues and merits of the pious, and the scandals and faults of the disobedient, before the heads of the witnesses and all the people of the plains. And it is something with which God warned His servants in this world, so it must be realized in the Hereafter. (1) See what was written on that by the author of al-Mawaqif: 2/442 and Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani on al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya: 400.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage defines the divine accounting (الحساب) as the disclosure by God to His servants of all their deeds—actions, words, and beliefs—before they leave the gathering place (المحشر). The exact manner or means of this disclosure is known only to God. The wisdom (الحكمة) behind this accounting is to publicly manifest the virtues and merits of the pious and the faults and scandals of the disobedient, before all witnesses. The author then asserts that this accounting is a matter of which God warned His servants in this world, so it must necessarily occur in the Hereafter. A footnote references scholarly works for further reading.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The purpose of the divine accounting is only to punish the disobedient.
Correction: The passage clearly states that the wisdom of the accounting is to manifest both the virtues of the pious and the faults of the disobedient, not merely punishment.

Checkpoint
What is the wisdom (الحكمة) behind the divine accounting according to the passage?
A) To allow people to refute their deeds
B) To manifest the virtues of the pious and the faults of the disobedient
C) To determine who enters heaven
D) To make people fearful

Key Takeaway
The divine accounting is a real event that will occur, designed by Allah to publicly reveal the true state of every person.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imagine standing on that plain, and every deed—every word, every belief—is laid bare. Which of your hidden faults would you be most terrified to have exposed? Knowing that the accounting also manifests virtues, how does that change your perspective on your private acts of obedience?
?
The passage says the accounting is a warning from God in this world. Are you living as if that warning is real? What would you change today if you truly believed that every deed will be publicly accounted for?
?
The wisdom of the accounting is not just punishment but to show the true state of everyone. How does that motivate you to seek sincerity (ikhlas) in your worship and to avoid hypocrisy, knowing that your true state will be revealed?

Resurrection: Gathering of Original Parts
Buti explains that resurrection gathers original atoms, not creates anew.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the resurrection (al-hashr) involves the gathering of the same original atoms, not the creation of new bodies from nothing.

Core Idea
Resurrection gathers the same original atoms, not new creation.

In this passage, Buti clarifies a key theological point about resurrection. He argues that the Qur'anic verses indicate that the resurrection is a re-gathering of the original parts of a person, not a creation from absolute non-existence. This understanding resolves some common misconceptions about the nature of the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp Buti's argument.
Notice the key terms: الحشر, الذرات.
2
Identify the two contrasting views
Buti contrasts 'gathering from dispersion' with 'creation from absolute non-existence'. Identify which view he supports and how he uses Quranic evidence.
The verse al-Qiyama 3-4 is his proof.
3
Understand the qualification about parts
Buti specifies that only the original parts are restored, not later additions. Consider why this distinction is important for the doctrine of resurrection.
This avoids the problem of identity change.
4
Reflect on the limits of human knowledge
Buti concludes that details of this process are known only to Allah. Reflect on why theologians accept this limitation.
This shows the balance between reason and revelation.
