فالآية دالة على أن الحشر يكون عن طريق تجميع الذرات من التفرق والشتات لا عن طريق إيجادها من العدم المطلق ، ويدل على هذا المعنى أيضاً قوله جل جلاله : ( أَيَحْسَبُ الإنسانُ أَلَّنْ نَجْمَعَ عِظَامَهُ ، بَلَى ، قادرينَ عَلَى أَنْ نُسَوِّي بَنانَهُ ﴾ [ القيامة : ٣ - ٤ ] . وبهذا تعلم أن الذي يعود من الإنسان إلى التجمع والحياة إنما هو عين أجزائه التي عاش بها في الدنيا ، والمقصود بعين أجزائه ، عين أجزائه الأصلية التي بها استقبل الحياة ، أما مازيد عليها بعد ذلك فلا يشترط أن يعاد بذاته ، وقد أطال (۱) في بحث ذلك علماء العقيدة والكلام ، وعلم ذلك في الحقيقة عند الله عز وجل ولا سبيل لنا ، كما قلت لك ، إلى تحليل أو بيان شيء من الغيوب التي لم يكشف عنها الخالق جل جلاله سجاف غيبه بعد
The verse indicates that the resurrection (al-hashr) is by way of gathering the atoms from dispersion and scattering, not by way of creating them from absolute non-existence. This meaning is also indicated by His saying, Exalted is His Majesty: 'Does man think that We will not assemble his bones? Yes, [We are] Able to proportion his fingertips' (al-Qiyama 3-4). And by this you know that what returns from the human to gathering and life is precisely the same parts with which he lived in the world, and by 'the same parts' is meant his original parts with which he began life. As for what increases beyond that afterwards, it is not required that it be returned in its essence. The scholars of creed and theology have extensively discussed this, and the true knowledge of it rests with Allah, Mighty and Majestic, and there is no way for us, as I told you, to analyze or explain anything of the unseen matters that the Creator, Exalted is His Majesty, has not yet unveiled His veil of the unseen.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the nature of resurrection (al-hashr). Buti argues that the Qur'anic verse (al-Qiyama 3-4) indicates that resurrection is a gathering of the scattered parts, not a creation from absolute nothingness. The same original parts that the person had in life are restored. Additional parts that accrued thereafter need not be restored in their exact identity. He notes that scholars of theology have discussed this extensively, but the true knowledge of the unseen matters rests with God, and we cannot analyze matters that God has not revealed.

Key Terms
الحشر
الذرات
إعادة المعدوم
الأجزاء الأصلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Resurrection creates new bodies from nothing.
Correction: Buti clarifies that resurrection gathers the same original atoms from dispersion.

Checkpoint
What does the verse from Surah al-Qiyama (3-4) indicate about the nature of resurrection according to Buti?
A) It is a creation from nothing.
B) It is a gathering of the same atoms from dispersion.
C) It is a spiritual event only.
D) It applies only to believers.

Key Takeaway
Resurrection is the re-gathering of the same original atoms, not a new creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If only your original parts—the very atoms with which you began life—will be resurrected, then your physical appearance, wealth, and status are temporary additions that will not return. Are you investing your heart in what will last or in what will be left behind?
?
Buti insists that the exact mechanism of resurrection is unseen and beyond human analysis. Do you trust Allah's plan for your return, or do you find yourself seeking rational explanations for matters He has kept hidden?
?
Every atom of your original body is preserved by Allah for the Day of Gathering. How does that awareness change the way you use your body today in obedience or disobedience? Will those same atoms testify for you or against you?

The Day of Accounting: Definition, Wisdom, and Qur'anic Proofs
Buti defines the Day of Accounting and provides Qur'anic proofs for its certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic concept of the Day of Accounting (al-hisab), its definition, wisdom, and the Qur'anic evidence establishing its certainty, along with the variations in how it will occur for different people.

Core Idea
The accounting on Judgment Day is a detailed review of every deed, with difficulty varying by faith and action.

Buti begins by defining the accounting as Allah's full disclosure of all human deeds before the assembly of creation. He then explains its purpose: to manifest the virtues of the righteous and the faults of the sinners. After establishing its necessity through divine warning, he provides Qur'anic proofs that name the Day of Judgment as the Day of Accounting and conclusively demonstrate its occurrence. Finally, he describes how the accounting's length and severity differ according to people's states in this world.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of al-hisab
Read the first sentence of the passage carefully. Buti defines al-hisab as Allah informing His servants of all their deeds—actions, words, and beliefs—before they leave the place of assembly. Note that the manner of this disclosure is known only to Allah.
The definition covers both good and evil deeds.
2
Grasp the wisdom behind the accounting
Buti states that the wisdom is to show the virtues of the righteous and the scandals of the sinners before all witnesses. Reflect on why this public display is important for divine justice.
3
See the Qur'anic proof texts
Buti cites several verses. Focus on three that explicitly mention 'Day of Accounting' (Surah Sad 53, 26; Ghafir 27). Then note the two longer proofs from al-Baqarah 284 and al-Inshiqaq 7-12. Understand that these are considered definitive by consensus.
The passage emphasizes that these proofs are cut by the consensus of all Muslims.
4
Reflect on the varying difficulty of the accounting
Buti explains that the length and severity of the accounting vary. Some people will have an account as brief as milking a camel, while others will experience prolonged distress. Consider how this connects to one's deeds in the world.
The passage ends by introducing the necessity of belief in the books (records), which will be covered in a following lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحساب

وهو إطلاع الله عباده قبل انصرافهم من المحشر على كل ما قد جنوه في حياتهم الدنيا من تصرفات فعلية وقولية واعتقادية خيراً كانت أو شراً ، وذلك بالشكل أو الواسطة التي لا يعلمها أحد غيره

والحكمة من هذا الحساب أن يظهر الله فضائل المتقين ومناقبهم ، وفضائح العصاة ومثالبهم ، وذلك على رؤوس الأشهاد وسائر أهل العرصات

وهو مما أنذر الله به عباده في الدنيا ، فلا بد أن يتحقق في الآخرة .

وقد دلّ الخبر الإلهي أن هذا الحساب هو أهم وأعظم ما يراه الإنسان من أحداث يوم القيامة ، حتى إنه سبحانه وتعالى أطلق على يوم القيامة اسم : يوم الحساب ، فقال في محكم كتابه : ( هذا ما توعَدُونَ لِيَوم الحساب ﴾ [ ص : ٥٣ ] . إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يُضِلُّونَ عَن سَبِيلِ اللهِ لَهُمْ عَذابٌ شَديدٌ بِما نَسوا يومَ الحِسابِ ) [ ص : ٢٦ ] . وقال مُوسَى إِنِّي عُذْتُ بِرَبِّي وَرَبِّكُمْ مِنْ كُلِّ مُتَكَبْرِ لا يُؤْمِنُ بِيَوْمِ الحساب ﴾ [ غافر : ٢٧ ] .

القيامة

ومن أجلى الآيات الدالة بشكل قطعي على محاسبة الله عباده يوم قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَإنْ تُبْدُوا ما في أَنفُسِكُمْ أَوْ تُخْفُوهُ يُحاسِبُكُم بِهِ اللهُ فَيَغْفِرُ لِمَن يَشَاءُ وَيُعَذِّبُ مَنْ يَشَاءُ ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٨٤] وقوله تعالى : ﴿ فَأَمَّا مَن أُوتِيَ كتابه بيمينه فَسَوْفَ يُحَاسَبُ حِساباً يسيراً وَيَنْقَلِبُ إلى أَهْلِهِ مَسْرُوراً ، وأمَّا مَنْ كِتابَهُ وَراءَ ظَهْرِهِ فَسَوْفَ يَدعو ثُبُوراً ويَصْلَى سَعِيراً ﴾ [ الانشقاق : ٧ - ١٢ ] . وهناك آيات كثيرة أخرى لاداعي إلى سردها إذ هي مما لاتكاد تخفى على أحد . ودلالتها على ثبوت الحساب يوم القيامة دلالة قطعية بإجماع المسلمين كلهم.

أما عن طول الحساب على الإنسان وقصره ، وصعوبته ويسره ، فهو يختلف باختلاف الناس وتفاوت درجاتهم. فمنهم من لا يستغرق الحساب بالنسبة إليه أكثر من فواق ناقة - أي حلبها - كما قال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام ، ومنهم من يتطاول عليهم أمد ذلك ويشتد عليهم الكرب ، ويتفاوت هؤلاء أيضاً في ذلك حسب أحوالهم التي كانوا قد أدبروا عنها في الدنيا

واعلم أن الإيمان بالحساب يستلزم الإيمان بالكتب ، وهي صحائف بأسماء -
The Accounting (al-Hisab): It is Allah's informing His servants, before they depart from the place of assembly, of all that they have committed in their worldly lives of actions, words, and beliefs, whether good or evil, in the manner or by the means that no one else knows. The wisdom behind this accounting is that Allah may show the virtues of the righteous and their merits, and the scandals of the sinners and their faults, before the witnesses and all the people of the plains. It is something that Allah has warned His servants about in the world, so it must inevitably occur in the Hereafter. The divine report has indicated that this accounting is the most important and greatest event that a person will see on the Day of Resurrection, to the extent that He, Glorified and Exalted, named the Day of Resurrection the Day of Accounting, saying in His firm Book: 'This is what you are promised for the Day of Accounting' (Sad 53). 'Indeed, those who lead astray from the path of Allah will have a severe punishment for having forgotten the Day of Accounting' (Sad 26). And Moses said: 'Indeed, I seek refuge in my Lord and your Lord from every arrogant one who does not believe in the Day of Accounting' (Ghafir 27). The Resurrection: And among the clearest verses that definitively indicate Allah's accounting of His servants on that Day are His statement, Exalted: 'And whether you disclose what is within yourselves or conceal it, Allah will bring you to account for it. Then He forgives whom He wills and punishes whom He wills' (al-Baqarah 284), and His statement, Exalted: 'Then as for he who is given his record in his right hand, he will be judged with an easy account and return to his people happy. But as for he who is given his record behind his back, he will call for destruction and burn in a Blaze' (al-Inshiqaq 7-12). And there are many other verses that need not be listed, as they are not hidden from anyone. Their indication of the establishment of the accounting on the Day of Resurrection is a definitive indication by the consensus of all Muslims. As for the length or shortness of the accounting for a person, and its difficulty or ease, it varies according to people and their differing degrees. Among them are those for whom the accounting will take no more than the milking of a she-camel, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, and among them are those for whom the time will be prolonged and the distress severe, and these also vary in that according to their states that they left behind in the world. And know that belief in the accounting necessitates belief in the books (al-kutub), which are records with names -
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive discussion of the accounting (al-hisab). It begins by defining it as God's informing His servants of all their deeds, both good and evil, in a manner known only to Him. The wisdom behind it is to manifest the virtues of the righteous and the faults of the sinners before witnesses. Then Buti asserts that it is a promise from God that must occur in the Hereafter. He then cites Qur'anic verses that emphasize the importance of the Day of Accounting, including that it is called 'Day of Reckoning'. He quotes verses from Surah Sad, Ghafir, and then a series of verses from Surah al-Baqarah and al-Inshiqaq as definitive proofs. He concludes that these proofs are definitive by the consensus of Muslims. Finally, he discusses the variation in the length and difficulty of the accounting depending on the person's deeds, citing a hadith that some will have a quick accounting like the time to milk a camel. He then states that belief in the accounting necessitates belief in the books (al-kutub), which are records of deeds, but the sentence is cut off.

Key Terms
الحساب
يوم الحساب
الحكمة
الكتب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The accounting is just a formality, easy for everyone.
Correction: Buti explains that the accounting is a detailed review of all deeds, and its difficulty varies greatly; some people will have a quick account, others will suffer prolonged distress.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the primary wisdom (الحكمة) behind the accounting on the Day of Judgment?
A) To punish all sinners publicly.
B) To show the virtues of the righteous and the faults of the sinners before witnesses.
C) To give everyone a second chance.
D) To register deeds for future reference.

Key Takeaway
The accounting (al-hisab) is a certain event that will review every deed, with its difficulty determined by one's faith and actions, and its occurrence is definitively proven by the Qur'an.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that every thought you conceal and every word you speak is being recorded for a public accounting, would you change what you say in private today? Tomorrow? What is one conversation you would avoid if it were to be displayed before all creation?
?
The Prophet said some will have an account as brief as milking a camel. What deeds are you doing right now that would make your account easy—or prolonged? Are you living in a way that would make you hope for the easy account, or are you accumulating deeds that will make the distress severe?
?
Allah named this day the Day of Accounting. When you wake up each morning, do you live as if you truly believe you will stand for that review, or do you act as if it is distant? What one habit could you start today to remind you of this reality before you meet it?

The Greatest Event: Divine Proof of the Accounting
The author cites Quranic naming and verses to prove the accounting's centrality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran and consensus of Muslims establish the accounting as the most significant event of the Day of Resurrection.

Core Idea
Allah named the Day of Resurrection the Day of Reckoning, making the accounting its central event.

In this passage, the author marshals evidence from the Quran and the unanimous agreement of Muslims to show that the accounting (al-hisab) is the greatest thing a person will witness. He begins by noting that Allah Himself calls the Day of Resurrection the 'Day of Reckoning' in multiple verses, and then provides specific verses that demonstrate the reality of divine accounting.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the author's claim
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the opening statement that the accounting is the most important and greatest event.
The author uses strong language (أهم وأعظم) to emphasize importance.
2
Examine the Quranic naming
Notice that Allah Himself named the Day of Resurrection as the 'Day of Reckoning' (يوم الحساب). This is a primary proof of the accounting's centrality.
Three verses are cited where this name appears.
3
Analyze the clear verses
Read the two verses from Al-Baqarah and Al-Inshiqaq that definitively prove Allah will call people to account. Reflect on their implications.
These verses are presented as the clearest evidence.
4
Understand the role of consensus
The author concludes that the indication of these verses is definitive by the consensus (ijma') of all Muslims, solidifying the certainty of the accounting.
Consensus here means universal agreement of Muslim scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد دلّ الخبر الإلهي أن هذا الحساب هو أهم وأعظم ما يراه الإنسان من أحداث يوم القيامة ، حتى إنه سبحانه وتعالى أطلق على يوم القيامة اسم : يوم الحساب ، فقال في محكم كتابه : ﴿ هذا ما توعَدُونَ لِيَوم الحساب ﴾ [ ص : ٥٣ ] . إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يُضِلُّونَ عَن سَبِيلِ اللهِ لَهُمْ عَذابٌ شَديدٌ بِما نَسوا يومَ الحِسابِ ) [ ص : ٢٦ ] . وقال مُوسَى إِنِّي عُذْتُ بِرَبِّي وَرَبِّكُمْ مِنْ كُلِّ مُتَكَبْرِ لا يُؤْمِنُ بِيَوْمِ الحساب ﴾ [ غافر : ٢٧ ] . · القيامة ومن أجلى الآيات الدالة بشكل قطعي على محاسبة الله عباده يوم قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَإنْ تُبْدُوا ما في أَنفُسِكُمْ أَوْ تُخْفُوهُ يُحاسِبُكُم بِهِ اللهُ فَيَغْفِرُ لِمَن يَشَاءُ وَيُعَذِّبُ مَنْ يَشَاءُ ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٨٤] وقوله تعالى : ﴿ فَأَمَّا مَن أُوتِيَ كتابه بيمينه فَسَوْفَ يُحَاسَبُ حِساباً يسيراً وَيَنْقَلِبُ إلى أهْلِهِ مَسْرُوراً ، وأمَّا مَنْ كِتابَهُ وَراءَ ظَهْرِهِ فَسَوْفَ يَدعو ثُبُوراً ويَصْلَى سَعِيراً ﴾ [ الانشقاق : ٧ - ١٢ ] . وهناك آيات كثيرة أخرى لاداعي إلى سردها إذ هي مما لاتكاد تخفى على أحد . ودلالتها على ثبوت الحساب يوم القيامة دلالة قطعية بإجماع المسلمين كلهم. طول الحساب على الإنسان وقصره ، وصعوبته ويسره ، فهو يختلف باختلاف الناس وتفاوت درجاتهم. فمنهم من لا يستغرق الحساب بالنسبة إليه أكثر من فواق ناقة - أي حلبها - كما قال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام ، ومنهم من يتطاول عليهم أمد ذلك ويشتد عليهم الكرب ، ويتفاوت هؤلاء أيضاً في ذلك حسب أحوالهم التي كانوا قد أدبروا عنها في الدنيا
And the divine report has indicated that this accounting is the most important and greatest thing that a person sees from the events of the Day of Resurrection, so much so that He, exalted and glorified, named the Day of Resurrection as the Day of Reckoning. He said in His clear Book: 'This is what you were promised for the Day of Reckoning' [Sad:53]. 'Indeed, those who lead astray from the path of Allah will have a severe punishment because they forgot the Day of Reckoning' [Sad:26]. And Moses said: 'Indeed, I seek refuge in my Lord and your Lord from every arrogant one who does not believe in the Day of Reckoning' [Ghafir:27]. · Resurrection And among the clearest verses that definitively indicate Allah's accounting of His servants on that day are His statement: 'Whether you disclose what is in your souls or conceal it, Allah will call you to account for it. Then He will forgive whom He wills and punish whom He wills' [Al-Baqarah:284]; and His statement: 'Then as for he who is given his book in his right hand, he will be reckoned with an easy reckoning, and he will return to his people happy; but as for he who is given his book behind his back, he will call for destruction and enter a blazing fire' [Al-Inshiqaq:7-12]. And there are many other verses that there is no need to list, as they are hardly hidden from anyone. And their indication of the establishment of the accounting on the Day of Resurrection is definitive by the consensus of all Muslims. The length and shortness of the accounting for a person, and its difficulty and ease, varies according to people and their differing degrees. Some of them do not take more than the time of milking a she-camel, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, and others have the duration prolonged and distress intensifies upon them, and these also vary in that according to their states that they had left behind in the world.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is a proof-text demonstration that the accounting (al-hisab) is the central event of the Day of Resurrection. The author begins by stating that divine revelation has informed us that this accounting is the most important and greatest thing a person will witness. He supports this by noting that Allah Himself named the Day of Resurrection the 'Day of Reckoning' and cites three Quranic verses where this name is used: from Surat Sad, then another from Sad, and from Ghafir. Then, under the subheading 'Resurrection', he presents two of the clearest verses that definitively prove that Allah will call people to account: the verse from Al-Baqarah which states that Allah will call to account for what is in souls, and the verses from Al-Inshiqaq distinguishing between the one given his book in his right hand (easy reckoning) and the one given behind his back (destruction). He then remarks that there are many such verses, well-known, and that their indication of the reality of the accounting is definitive by the consensus (ijma') of all Muslims. Following this, he turns to the application: the length and difficulty of the accounting varies according to people's deeds. He cites the hadith that for some the accounting lasts no longer than the milking of a she-camel, while for others it is prolonged and severe, and this variation is according to their previous states in the world. The passage thus establishes both the certainty of the accounting and its differentiated nature.

يوم الحساب
القيامة
إجماع المسلمين

Checkpoint

B) That Allah named the Day of Resurrection as the Day of Reckoning in the Quran
C) The hadith about the milking of a she-camel
D) The variation of the accounting among people

Key Takeaway
The accounting is the greatest event of the Day of Resurrection, proven by Allah naming that Day the Day of Reckoning and by definitive Quranic verses, confirmed by consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Variation in the Accounting: Length and Ease
The author explains the varying length and difficulty of the accounting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the length and difficulty of the accounting on the Day of Resurrection varies according to people's deeds in the world.

Core Idea
The accounting varies: for some it is as brief as milking a she-camel, for others it is long and severe.

After establishing the certainty of the accounting, the author turns to its application among people. He explains that the duration and ease of the accounting differ based on one's deeds. He supports this with a prophetic hadith indicating that for some believers the accounting is extremely short, while for others it is prolonged and severe.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on variation
Read the short Arabic passage and its translation. Note the author's general statement that the accounting varies in length, shortness, difficulty, and ease.
The variation is based on people's differing degrees (اختلاف الناس وتفاوت درجاتهم).
2
Examine the hadith example
Identify the hadith about the milking of a she-camel. Understand that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used this to illustrate the brevity of the accounting for some.
فواق ناقة means the time between milkings, a very short period.
3
Understand the opposite extreme
Read about those for whom the accounting is prolonged and severe. Note that the author says they also vary among themselves.
This emphasizes justice and individual accountability.

وقد دلّ الخبر الإلهي أن هذا الحساب هو أهم وأعظم ما يراه الإنسان من أحداث يوم القيامة ، حتى إنه سبحانه وتعالى أطلق على يوم القيامة اسم : يوم الحساب ، فقال في محكم كتابه : ﴿ هذا ما توعَدُونَ لِيَوم الحساب ﴾ [ ص : ٥٣ ] . إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يُضِلُّونَ عَن سَبِيلِ اللهِ لَهُمْ عَذابٌ شَديدٌ بِما نَسوا يومَ الحِسابِ ) [ ص : ٢٦ ] . وقال مُوسَى إِنِّي عُذْتُ بِرَبِّي وَرَبِّكُمْ مِنْ كُلِّ مُتَكَبْرِ لا يُؤْمِنُ بِيَوْمِ الحساب ﴾ [ غافر : ٢٧ ] . · القيامة ومن أجلى الآيات الدالة بشكل قطعي على محاسبة الله عباده يوم قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَإنْ تُبْدُوا ما في أَنفُسِكُمْ أَوْ تُخْفُوهُ يُحاسِبُكُم بِهِ اللهُ فَيَغْفِرُ لِمَن يَشَاءُ وَيُعَذِّبُ مَنْ يَشَاءُ ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٨٤] وقوله تعالى : ﴿ فَأَمَّا مَن أُوتِيَ كتابه بيمينه فَسَوْفَ يُحَاسَبُ حِساباً يسيراً وَيَنْقَلِبُ إلى أهْلِهِ مَسْرُوراً ، وأمَّا مَنْ كِتابَهُ وَراءَ ظَهْرِهِ فَسَوْفَ يَدعو ثُبُوراً ويَصْلَى سَعِيراً ﴾ [ الانشقاق : ٧ - ١٢ ] . وهناك آيات كثيرة أخرى لاداعي إلى سردها إذ هي مما لاتكاد تخفى على أحد . ودلالتها على ثبوت الحساب يوم القيامة دلالة قطعية بإجماع المسلمين كلهم. طول الحساب على الإنسان وقصره ، وصعوبته ويسره ، فهو يختلف باختلاف الناس وتفاوت درجاتهم. فمنهم من لا يستغرق الحساب بالنسبة إليه أكثر من فواق ناقة - أي حلبها - كما قال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام ، ومنهم من يتطاول عليهم أمد ذلك ويشتد عليهم الكرب ، ويتفاوت هؤلاء أيضاً في ذلك حسب أحوالهم التي كانوا قد أدبروا عنها في الدنيا
And the divine report has indicated that this accounting is the most important and greatest thing that a person sees from the events of the Day of Resurrection, so much so that He, exalted and glorified, named the Day of Resurrection as the Day of Reckoning. He said in His clear Book: 'This is what you were promised for the Day of Reckoning' [Sad:53]. 'Indeed, those who lead astray from the path of Allah will have a severe punishment because they forgot the Day of Reckoning' [Sad:26]. And Moses said: 'Indeed, I seek refuge in my Lord and your Lord from every arrogant one who does not believe in the Day of Reckoning' [Ghafir:27]. · Resurrection And among the clearest verses that definitively indicate Allah's accounting of His servants on that day are His statement: 'Whether you disclose what is in your souls or conceal it, Allah will call you to account for it. Then He will forgive whom He wills and punish whom He wills' [Al-Baqarah:284]; and His statement: 'Then as for he who is given his book in his right hand, he will be reckoned with an easy reckoning, and he will return to his people happy; but as for he who is given his book behind his back, he will call for destruction and enter a blazing fire' [Al-Inshiqaq:7-12]. And there are many other verses that there is no need to list, as they are hardly hidden from anyone. And their indication of the establishment of the accounting on the Day of Resurrection is definitive by the consensus of all Muslims. The length and shortness of the accounting for a person, and its difficulty and ease, varies according to people and their differing degrees. Some of them do not take more than the time of milking a she-camel, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, and others have the duration prolonged and distress intensifies upon them, and these also vary in that according to their states that they had left behind in the world.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is a proof-text demonstration that the accounting (al-hisab) is the central event of the Day of Resurrection. The author begins by stating that divine revelation has informed us that this accounting is the most important and greatest thing a person will witness. He supports this by noting that Allah Himself named the Day of Resurrection the 'Day of Reckoning' and cites three Quranic verses where this name is used: from Surat Sad, then another from Sad, and from Ghafir. Then, under the subheading 'Resurrection', he presents two of the clearest verses that definitively prove that Allah will call people to account: the verse from Al-Baqarah which states that Allah will call to account for what is in souls, and the verses from Al-Inshiqaq distinguishing between the one given his book in his right hand (easy reckoning) and the one given behind his back (destruction). He then remarks that there are many such verses, well-known, and that their indication of the reality of the accounting is definitive by the consensus (ijma') of all Muslims. Following this, he turns to the application: the length and difficulty of the accounting varies according to people's deeds. He cites the hadith that for some the accounting lasts no longer than the milking of a she-camel, while for others it is prolonged and severe, and this variation is according to their previous states in the world. The passage thus establishes both the certainty of the accounting and its differentiated nature.

Key Terms

قصره
فواق ناقة

Correction: The passage states it varies according to people's deeds; for some it is brief, for others prolonged and severe.

Key Takeaway
The accounting varies in length and difficulty according to one's deeds; for the righteous it is brief, for others it is prolonged and severe.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The passage says the accounting varies according to 'the states they had left behind in the world.' What state are you leaving behind today? Will it make your reckoning brief or prolonged?
?
If you knew that every thought, word, and action you produce this week will be scrutinized in an accounting that matches its quality, what would you change starting now?

Belief in Accounting Necessitates Belief in the Scrolls
The author explains that belief in accounting requires belief in the scrolls and cites Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in the final accounting implies belief in the scrolls of deeds, and what Quranic evidence establishes this.

Core Idea
Scrolls of deeds are the necessary evidence for the final accounting.

The author establishes a logical link between two core eschatological beliefs: the accounting (hisab) and the scrolls (kutub). He explains that the scrolls, whose true nature is known only to Allah, determine one's eternal fate based on recorded deeds. He then grounds this in Quranic verses from Surat Al-Jathiyah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through.
The passage is dense with doctrinal assertions.
2
Identify the logical link
Notice how the author states that belief in accounting necessitates belief in the scrolls. This is a key doctrinal connection.
The scrolls are the evidence for the accounting.
3
Understand the limits of knowledge
The author emphasizes that only Allah knows the modality of the scrolls and the writing. This is a guard against speculation.
Stay within revealed knowledge.
4
Reflect on the Quranic proof
The author cites verses from Al-Jathiyah. Read them in the translation and see how they depict the scene of judgment.
The verses show the book itself speaking truth.
5
Internalize the outcomes
Understand the consequence of receiving the book in the right hand vs. left hand. This determines eternal bliss or misery.
These outcomes are based on recorded deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن الإيمان بالحساب يستلزم الإيمان بالكتب ، وهي صحائف بأسماء أصحابها تعطى إلى يمين كل منهم أو يساره ، قد سجل فيها كل ما كان قد اجترحه أو اكتسبه ، والله أعلم بكيفية هذه الصحائف ونوعها وكيفية الكتـابـة المسجلة عليها . وكل ما أعلمنا الله إياه بإخباره القطعي هو أن من أوتي كتابه بيمينه كان من السعداء وكل من أوتي كتابه بشماله كان من أهل الشقوة والضلال . وحسبك أن تنصت في بيان هذا الأمر إلى هذه الآيات الباهرة ، ثم تخضع لها وتوقن بمضمونها : واللهِ مُلْكُ السَّمَواتِ والأَرْضِ وَيَوْمَ تَقُومُ السَّاعَةُ يَومَئِذٍ يَخْسَرُ الْمُبْطِلُونَ : وَتَرَى كُلَّ أُمَّةٍ جاثِيَةٌ كُلِّ أُمَّةٍ تُدْعَى إلى كِتابها اليَوْمَ تُجْزَوْنَ مَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ هذا كِتابُنا يَنْطِقُ عَلَيْكُم بالحَقِّ إِنَّا كُنَّا نَسْتَنْسِخُ مَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الجاثية : ۲۹ - ۲۷]
And know that belief in the accounting necessitates belief in the scrolls, which are sheets with the names of their owners, given to the right of each of them or to his left. In them is recorded everything that he had perpetrated or earned. Allah knows best the modality of these sheets, their type, and the modality of the writing recorded on them. And all that Allah has informed us of by His definitive information is that whoever is given his book in his right hand will be among the blissful, and whoever is given his book in his left hand will be among the people of misery and misguidance. It suffices you in the clarification of this matter to listen to these dazzling verses, then submit to them and be certain of their contents: 'And to Allah belongs the dominion of the heavens and the earth. And on the day the Hour establishes itself, that Day the falsifiers will lose. And you will see every nation kneeling. Every nation will be called to its book: Today you will be recompensed for what you used to do. This is Our Book that speaks against you with truth. Indeed, We were copying what you used to do' [Al-Jathiyah: 27-29].
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement linking belief in the accounting to belief in the scrolls (al-kutub). The author instructs the reader to know that faith in the accounting entails faith in the scrolls, which are sheets bearing the names of their owners, given to the right or left hand of each person. These scrolls contain a record of every deed, whether perpetrated (earned) or acquired. The author then emphasizes that the modality (kayfiyya) of these sheets, their type, and the nature of the writing on them is known only to Allah. What Allah has definitively informed us is the outcome: whoever receives his book in his right hand is among the blessed (sa'ada), and whoever receives it in his left hand is among the wretched and misguided. To reinforce this, the author directs the reader to ponder the 'dazzling verses' from Surat Al-Jathiyah (45:27-29), which describe the dominion of Allah, the loss of the falsifiers on that day, and the calling of every nation to its book, with the book itself speaking the truth. The passage thus establishes the necessity of believing in the scrolls as a corollary of belief in the accounting, while acknowledging that the precise nature of these scrolls is beyond human knowledge.

?
The lesson says only Allah knows the true nature of the scrolls—do you live as if your secret deeds are fully exposed before Him, or do you still hide things even from yourself?
?
Allah says, 'This is Our Book that speaks against you with truth.' What truth would your scroll speak about your use of time, your speech, and your intentions? Will you now ask for forgiveness and change before it is read aloud?

The Indescribable Terror of the Standing
Declaration of indescribability with Quranic and prophetic examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the terror of the standing (houl al-mawqif) is indescribable and that Allah has concealed its full reality, with scriptural references providing only a glimpse.

Core Idea
The terror of Judgment Day is hidden; no words can capture it.

This passage confronts the believer with the overwhelming terror of the Day of Standing. The author argues that no human description can adequately depict it; it is something Allah has concealed. To help us conceive its magnitude, he cites powerful Quranic verses and a prophetic tradition, reminding us that even these only hint at the reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the author's strong claim that no description suffices.
2
Understand the epistemological limit
The author states that the reality of this terror is hidden by Allah. Reflect on why this is important for our understanding of the unseen.
This is a key point in Islamic theology about human limits.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Look at the two Quranic verses (Al-Hajj 22:1-2 and Abasa 80:33-37). How do they illustrate the terror?
Notice the vivid imagery: nursing mothers forgetting, people appearing drunk.
4
Consider the hadith fragment
The author mentions a hadith from the two Shaykhs. Even though the text is incomplete, note that the Prophet's description is also limited.
The hadith is corrupted in the source, but its purpose is clear.
5
Formulate the key takeaway
Summarize in your own words: what is the main teaching of this passage?
Review the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هول الموقف وعظائمه واعلم أنه لن يجدي في تصوير حقيقة هذا الهول وبيانه ، أي وصف يُكتب أو حديث يُتلى . وإنما هو شيء خبأه الله وأخفاه إلى حينه ، وحسبك أن تعلم أنـه أهول من كل هول وأعظم من كل عظيم ، وأن تستحضر في تصور عظمة ذلك قوله تعالى : ( يَا أَيُّها النَّاسُ اتَّقُوا رَبَّكُم إن زَلْزَلَةَ السَّاعَةِ شَيْءٌ عَظِيمٌ ، يَومَ تَرَوْنَها تَذْهَلُ كُلِّ مُرْضِعَةٍ عَمَّا أَرْضَعَتْ وَتَضَعُ كُلِّ ذَاتِ حَمْلٍ حَمْلَهَا ، وَتَرى النَّاسَ سُكَارَى وَما هُمْ بِسُكَارَى وَلَكِنْ عَذابَ اللهِ شَديدٌ ) [ الحج : ۱ - ٢ ] . أو قوله تعالى : ( فإذا جاءَتِ الصَّاحَةُ يَومَ يَفِرُّ المرء مِنْ أَخِيهِ ، وَأُمِّهِ وَأبيه ، وَصَاحِبَتِهِ وَبَنِيه ، لِكُلِّ امرئ مِنْهُم يَوْمَئِذٍ شأن يُغنيه ﴾ [ عبس : ٣٣ - ٣٧ ] . وقد وصف رسول الله لا طرفاً من هول الموقف فقال فيما رواه الشيخان الله عنها قالت : سمعت رسول الله لا يقول : يحشر الناس يوم عائشة رضي
The terror of the standing and its great things. And know that no written description or recited speech will be of any use in depicting the reality of this terror and explaining it. Rather, it is something that Allah has hidden and concealed until its time. It suffices you to know that it is more terrifying than any terror and greater than any great thing, and to bring to mind in visualizing its greatness the statement of the Exalted: 'O humanity, fear your Lord. Indeed, the convulsion of the Hour is a tremendous thing. On the day you see it, every nursing mother will forget what she nursed, and every pregnant woman will lay down her burden, and you will see the people intoxicated, but they are not intoxicated, but the punishment of Allah is severe' [Al-Hajj:1-2]. Or His statement: 'Then when the deafening blast comes, on the day when a man will flee from his brother, and his mother and his father, and his wife and his sons, for every person on that day will have a matter that will occupy him' ['Abasa:33-37]. And the Messenger of Allah described [?] part of the terror of the standing, saying in what the two Shaykhs narrated [؟] from 'A'isha, may Allah be pleased with her, she said: I heard the Messenger of Allah [؟] say: 'The people will be gathered on the day...'.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is a declaration about the indescribable terror of the standing (houl al-mawqif) on the Day of Resurrection. The author begins with the heading 'The terror of the standing and its great things'. He then makes a crucial epistemological point: no written description or oral recitation can adequately depict or explain the true reality of this terror, because it is something Allah has hidden and concealed until its appointed time. The only way to grasp something of its magnitude is to know that it is more terrifying than any other terror and greater than any great thing. To aid in visualizing this, the author presents two Quranic passages: first, verses from Surat Al-Hajj (22:1-2) describing the convulsion of the Hour, how nursing mothers forget, pregnant women abort, and people appear drunk due to the severe punishment; second, verses from Surat 'Abasa (80:33-37) where on the day of the deafening blast, a person flees from his closest relatives, each preoccupied. The author then notes that the Prophet himself described a part of this terror, citing a hadith narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim (the two shaykhs) from 'A'isha, but the text cuts off after 'the people will be gathered on the day...'. Despite the fragmentation, the point is clear: even prophetic description only gives a glimpse of the overwhelming terror, the full reality being known only to Allah.

زَلْزَلَةَ السَّاعَةِ

الشيخان

Key Takeaway
The terror of the standing is beyond description; Allah has hidden its full reality, and scripture only gives glimpses.

The Distribution of Records on Judgment Day
Buti describes the giving of records to the right or left and cites Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of the giving of records (suhuf) on the right or left on Judgment Day, and how this outcome determines one's fate as blessed or miserable.

Core Idea
Your record determines your fate: right hand for the blessed, left hand for the miserable.

In this passage, Shaykh Buti explains the giving of the records of deeds on the Day of Judgment. He emphasizes that while the exact nature of these records is known only to God, their placement—on the right or left—decisively indicates a person's ultimate destiny. The author then directs us to the Quranic verses that vividly and indubitably confirm this reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation, to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice how the author moves from description to Quranic proof.
2
Understand key terms
Familiarize yourself with the key terms: suhuf (sheets), kitab (book), yamin (right), shimal (left), al-su'ada' (the blessed), al-shiqwa (misery).
These terms are central to the scene.
3
Reflect on the Quranic evidence
Read the quoted verses from Surah Al-Jathiyah and reflect on how they reinforce the author's point about the certainty of the judgment.
The verses show the universal gathering and the speaking of the record.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصحابها تعطى إلى يمين كل منهم أو يساره ، قد سجل فيها كل ما كان قد اجترحه أو اكتسبه ، والله أعلم بكيفية هذه الصحائف ونوعها وكيفية الكتابة المسجلة عليها . وكل ما أعلمنا الله إياه بإخباره القطعي هو أن من أوتي كتابه بيمينه كان من السعداء وكل من أوتي كتابه بشماله كان من أهل الشقوة والضلال . وحسبك أن تنصت في بيان هذا الأمر إلى هذه الآيات الباهرة ، ثم تخضع لها وتوقن بمضمونها : وَاللهِ مُلْكُ السَّمَواتِ والأَرْضِ وَيَوْمَ تَقُومُ السَّاعَةُ يَومَئِذٍ يَخْسَرُ الْمُبْطِلُونَ : وَتَرَى كُلَّ أُمَّةٍ جاثِيَةٌ كُلِّ أُمَّةٍ تُدْعَى إلى كِتابها اليَوْمَ تُجْزَوْنَ مَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ هذا كِتابُنا يَنْطِقُ عَلَيْكُم بالحَقِّ إِنَّا كُنَّا نَسْتَنْسِخُ مَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الجاثية : ۲۹ - ٢٧].
They are given to the right of each of them or to his left, having recorded in them all that he has committed or earned. And God knows best the nature of these sheets, their type, and the nature of the writing recorded on them. And all that God has informed us of by His definitive report is that whoever is given his book in his right hand will be among the blessed, and whoever is given his book in his left hand will be among the people of misery and misguidance. And it suffices you to listen in explanation of this matter to these dazzling verses, then submit to them and be certain of their content: "To God belongs the dominion of the heavens and the earth. And on the Day the Hour appears, that Day the falsifiers will lose. And you will see every nation kneeling. Every nation will be called to its record: 'Today you will be recompensed for what you used to do. This is Our Book that speaks against you with truth. Indeed, We were copying what you used to do.'" [Al-Jathiyah 27-29].
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage describes the giving of the records (suhuf) of deeds on the Day of Judgment. The author begins by stating that these records are given to each person on their right or left side, and they contain every deed committed or earned. He then affirms that the definite information from God is that whoever receives his book in his right hand will be among the blessed, and whoever receives it in his left hand will be among the people of misery and misguidance. To emphasize the certainty of this, the author urges the reader to listen to the clear Quranic verses and to submit to them. He then quotes Surah Al-Jathiyah (45:27-29), which describes the scene on the Day of Judgment: God's dominion, the loss of the falsifiers, every nation kneeling, and being called to their record. The verse concludes that God's Book speaks the truth about their deeds.

Key Terms
صحائف (suhuf)
كتاب (kitab)
يمين (yamin)
شمال (shimal)
السعداء (al-su'ada')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Correction: The author explicitly states that only God knows the true nature (kayfiyya) of these sheets and the writing. Our focus should be on the spiritual reality they represent and the outcome they determine.

?

The Overwhelming Terror of the Day of Judgment
Buti describes the horror of the Day with Quranic verses and hadith on gathering, sun, and sweat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the indescribable terror of the Day of Judgment as depicted in the Quran and Sunnah, and how it overwhelms all human bonds and comforts.

Core Idea
The terror of Judgment Day is beyond description, causing total social and personal breakdown.

In this passage, Buti draws from the Quran and authentic hadith to convey the sheer horror of the Day of Judgment. He emphasizes that no human description can fully capture it, yet the divine texts give us glimpses: mothers forgetting their infants, people fleeing their closest relatives, and the physical discomfort of being gathered naked with the sun close and sweat drenching all. This lesson explores those depictions and their meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation to absorb the tone and content. Notice how Buti begins by stating the limitation of human description.
Pay attention to the strong words: 'more terrifying than any terror.'
2
Examine the Quranic verses
Identify the two Quranic verses (Al-Hajj 1-2 and Abasa 33-37). Notice how each depicts a different aspect: the first shows physical and emotional shock, the second shows social fragmentation.
Ask yourself why a nursing mother would forget her baby, and why a person would flee from family.
3
Analyze the hadith on gathering
Read the hadith from Aisha (RA). Reflect on the conditions: barefoot, naked, uncircumcised. Note Aisha's concern and the Prophet's response that the matter is more severe.
This emphasizes that shame and physical exposure are minor compared to the overall terror.
4
Study the sun and sweat description
Focus on the part about the sun drawing near and sweat covering the earth for seventy cubits. Notice the different levels of sweat: ankle, knees, waist, and bridling. This illustrates the graduated severity of suffering.
The Prophet's gesture to his mouth may indicate the worst level.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Read the final sentences: people will wish to go to Hell to escape, and God calls it the 'great terror'. Consider why this is the ultimate description of its enormity.
The name 'great terror' (al-faza' al-akbar) is a key Quranic term.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هول الموقف وعظائمه واعلم أنه لن يجدي في تصوير حقيقة هذا الهول وبيانه ، أي وصف يُكتب أو حديث يُتلى . وإنما هو شيء خبأه الله وأخفاه إلى حينه ، وحسبك أن تعلم أنه أهول من كل هول وأعظم من كل عظيم ، وأن تستحضر في تصور عظمة ذلك قوله تعالى : ( يَا أَيُّها النَّاسُ اتَّقُوا رَبَّكُم إن زَلْزَلَةَ السَّاعَةِ شَيْءٌ عَظِيمٌ ، يَومَ تَرَوْنَها تَذْهَلُ كُلِّ مُرْضِعَةٍ عَمَّا أَرْضَعَتْ وَتَضَعُ كُلِّ ذَاتِ حَمْلٍ حَمْلَهَا ، وَتَرى النَّاسَ سُكَارَى وَما هُمْ بِسُكَارَى وَلَكِنْ عَذابَ اللهِ شَديدٌ ) [ الحج : ۱ - ۲ ] . أو قوله تعالى : ( فإذا جاءَتِ الصَّاحَةُ يَومَ يَفِرُّ المرء مِنْ أَخِيهِ ، وَأُمِّهِ وَأبيه ، وَصَاحِبَتِهِ وَبَنِيه ، لِكُلِّ امرئ مِنْهُم يَوْمَئِذٍ شأن يُغنيه ﴾ [ عبس : ٣٣ - ٣٧ ] . وقد وصف رسول الله لا طرفاً من هول الموقف فقال فيما رواه الشيخان عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت : سمعت رسول الله لا يقول : يحشر الناس يوم القيامة حفاة عراة غرلا ) ، قلت : يارسول الله النساء والرجال جميعاً ينظر بعضهم إلى بعض ؟ قال : يا عائشة الأمر أشد من أن ينظر بعضهم إلى بعض . كما أوضح أن الشمس تدنو إذ ذاك من رؤوس الخلائق ، حتى تكون علومه منهم بمقدار ميل ، ويذهب العرق يسيح في الأرض سبعين بـاعـاً ، فمنهم من يبلغ العرق كعبيه ومنهم من يكون إلى ركبتيه ومنهم من يكون إلى حقويه ومنهم من يلجمه العرق الجاماً ، وأشار رسول الله إلى فيه صلى الله وحسبك من هول هذا اليوم أن يتمنى الناس الانصراف عنه ولو إلى النار ، وأن يطلق الله عليه اسم الفزع الأكبر.
The terror of the standing and its great matters. Know that no description written or speech recited will be effective in depicting the reality of this terror and explaining it. Rather, it is something that God has hidden and concealed until its time. And it suffices you to know that it is more terrifying than any terror and greater than any greatness, and to bring to mind in imagining its greatness His saying, may He be exalted, 'O mankind, fear your Lord. Indeed, the convulsion of the Hour is a terrible thing. On the Day you see it, every nursing mother will forget what she nursed, and every pregnant woman will deliver her burden, and you will see people intoxicated, but they are not intoxicated, but the punishment of God is severe' [Al-Hajj 1-2]. Or His saying, 'But when the Deafening Blast comes, on the Day a man will flee from his brother, and his mother and his father, and his wife and his children. For every man on that Day will be a matter that occupies him' [Abasa 33-37]. And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, described a part of the terror of the standing in what the two shaykhs narrated from Aisha, may God be pleased with her. She said, 'I heard the Messenger of God say: The people will be gathered on the Day of Resurrection barefoot, naked, uncircumcised.' I said, 'O Messenger of God, women and men all together, looking at one another?' He said, 'O Aisha, the matter is more severe than that they should look at one another.' He also clarified that the sun will draw near on that day to the heads of the creatures until it will be from them at a distance of a mile, and sweat will go flowing on the earth for seventy cubits. Among them, the sweat will reach the ankles, some will reach the knees, some will reach the waist, and some will be bridled by the sweat. And the Messenger of God pointed to his mouth, peace be upon him. And it suffices you of the terror of this day that people will wish to depart from it even to the Fire, and that God will call it the 'great terror' (al-faza' al-akbar).
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage focuses on describing the overwhelming terror (houl) of the Day of Judgment. The author begins by stating that no description—whether written or spoken—can truly capture the reality of this terror; it is something only God knows fully until its time. He then provides two Quranic verses to illustrate its magnitude: Surah Al-Hajj 1-2, which describes the convulsion of the Hour causing nursing mothers to forget their infants and pregnant women to abort, and Surah Abasa 33-37, which depicts a person fleeing from his closest relatives—brother, mother, father, wife, and children—because each person is entirely absorbed in his own concern. The author then cites a hadith reported by al-Bukhari and Muslim from Aisha, where the Prophet describes that people will be gathered barefoot, naked, and uncircumcised. When Aisha expressed concern about men and women seeing each other, the Prophet replied that the matter is far more serious than that. Additionally, the Prophet explained that the sun will come near to the people's heads, about a mile away, and sweat will spread on the earth for seventy cubits, affecting people at different levels—some to the ankles, some to the knees, some to the waist, and some even bridling them. The author concludes by noting that the terror is so extreme that people will wish to escape even to the Hellfire, and that God has named this terror the 'great terror' (al-faza' al-akbar).

زَلْزَلَة السَاعَة (zalzalat al-sa'ah)
فزع أكبر (faza' akbar)
حفاة (hufah)
عراة (urah)
غرلا (ghurla)
العرق (al-araq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the terror is only physical punishment, like fire or torture.
Correction: The passage shows it includes psychological and social breakdown: mothers forgetting infants, people fleeing relatives, and overwhelming anxiety.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith from Aisha mention about the condition of people on Judgment Day?
A) They will be dressed in fine clothes.
B) They will be barefoot, naked, and uncircumcised.
C) They will be carrying their books.
D) They will be with their families.

Key Takeaway
The Day of Judgment will be a day of unprecedented terror, dissolving all human relations and inflicting physical and mental anguish, such that people will wish for Hell as relief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
On that day, you will flee from your own mother and father. What does this reveal about the attachments you have now? How can you begin to loosen your grip on them before it is too late?
?
The nursing mother forgets her child—the strongest bond imaginable. If that bond cannot save you, what can you truly rely on when you stand before Allah?
?
Imagine the sweat reaching your mouth, the sun a mile above your head, and the overwhelming terror. You will wish for Hell as relief. What change must you make today so that your wish on that day is for Paradise instead?

Exemption from the Great Terror
Buti states the exemption, gives Quranic and hadith evidence, then exhorts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the 'great terror' of the Day of Judgment does not affect prophets and certain righteous individuals, as evidenced by the Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Prophets and the righteous are shielded from the greatest terror of that Day.

Having described the overwhelming terror of the Day of Judgment, Buti now introduces an important exception: not all will experience that horror. He draws on a Quranic verse and a well-known hadith to show that prophets and those whom God has favored are protected. This lesson explores that exemption and its implications for our own striving.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, noting the key terms 'فزع أكبر' and 'الذين سبقت لهم الحسنى'. Then read the translation.
The passage ends abruptly; the translation completes the sense.
2
Identify the Quranic proof
Find the verse from Surat al-Anbiya' (103-105). Notice how it describes the state of those who are spared: they are removed from Hell, hear no sound, and are greeted by angels.
3
Identify the hadith proof
Buti references the hadith of the seven categories shaded by Allah. This is a famous hadith; recall or look up the full list if needed.
The hadith is not quoted in full; the author assumes familiarity.
4
Apply the exhortation
Reflect on the final call to action: strive through conduct, character, religion, and fulfilling God's right to be among those not grieved by the great terror.
Consider the warning against long hopes and desires.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا أن شيئاً من هذا الهول لا يمس - كما ورد بذلك الخبر الصادق - الأنبياء ، ومن قبلهم الله عز وجل عنده من عباده وأوليائه الصالحين . دل على ذلك قوله تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّ الَّذِينَ سَبَقَتْ لَهُمْ مِنَّا الْحُسْنَى أُولَئِكَ عَنها مُبعَدُونَ ، لا يَسْمَعُونَ حسيتها وهُم فيها اشْتَهَتْ أَنْفُسُهُمْ خَالِدُونَ ، لا يَحْزُنُهُم الفَرعَ الأكْبَرُ وتَتَلَقَّاهُمُ الملائِكَةُ . هذا يَوْمُكُمُ الَّذِي كُنْتُم تُوعَدُونَ ﴾ [ الأنبياء : ١٠٣ - ١٠٥ ] . وقد دل الحديث الصحيح أن من هؤلاء الذين لا يحزنهم الفزع الأكبر ويكونون في مأمن من هذا العذاب الأليم ، أولئك الأصناف السبعة الذين أخبر الرسول مع الله أنهم يظلهم الله في ظله يوم لا ظل إلا ظله لا ظل إلا ظله .... الحديث . فاجهد يا أيها الإنسان العاقل - وإن فرصة العمر لا تزال في يدك - أن تكون واحداً من هؤلاء الذين قال عنهم : لا يحزنهم الفزع الأكبر . اجهد أن تكون واحداً منهم بسلوكك وخلقك ودينك وقيامك بحق ربك ، ولا يخدعنـك عن ذلك طول الأمل وسلطان الشهوات والأهواء ، فيوشك والله أن ترى هذا
Yet nothing of this terror touches—as has come in the truthful report—the prophets, and those whom God, exalted and mighty, has favored among His servants and His righteous saints. Evidence for that is His saying, 'Indeed, those for whom the best [reward] has preceded from Us—they will be far removed from it. They will not hear its sound, and they will abide eternally in whatever their souls desire. The greatest terror will not grieve them, and the angels will receive them: This is your Day which you have been promised' [Al-Anbiya' 103-105]. And the authentic hadith has indicated that among those who will not be grieved by the greatest terror and will be safe from this painful punishment are the seven categories whom the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, informed that God will shade them in His shade on the day when there is no shade but His shade... the hadith. So strive, O rational person—while the opportunity of life is still in your hand—to be one of those about whom He said: 'The greatest terror will not grieve them.' Strive to be one of them through your conduct, character, religion, and fulfilling the right of your Lord. And do not let long hopes and the authority of desires and whims deceive you, for soon, by God, you will see this...
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage provides the exception to the universal terror: the prophets and the righteous are spared. The author begins by stating that, according to truthful reports, the terror does not touch the prophets and those whom God has favored among His servants and saints. He then quotes Surah Al-Anbiya' 103-105, which describes that those for whom God has decreed the best reward will be far removed from Hell, will not hear its sound, will enjoy whatever they desire, and will not be grieved by the greatest terror; instead, angels will greet them. The author then refers to the authentic hadith about the seven categories of people whom God will shade under His throne on the Day of Judgment, when there is no other shade. This hadith is well-known. The author concludes with an exhortation: urging the rational person, while life is still available, to strive to be among those who are not grieved by the greatest terror, through good conduct, character, religion, and fulfilling God's rights. He warns against being deceived by long hopes and the domination of desires and whims, implying that such distractions may prevent one from achieving this goal.

فزع أكبر (faza' akbar)
الذين سبقت لهم الحسنى (alladhina sabaqat lahum al-husna)
السبعة الذين يظلهم الله (al-sab'ah alladhina yuzilluhum Allah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the terror is absolute and unavoidable for everyone.
Correction: The author clarifies that God exempts prophets and certain righteous individuals from the great terror.

Key Takeaway
Prophets and the righteous are shielded from the great terror, and we are called to strive for that station through faith and good deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you consider the seven categories of people shaded by Allah, do you see yourself in any of them? What is one concrete step you can take this week to grow in that quality?
?
The passage says 'the greatest terror will not grieve them.' Do you believe that you are safe from that grief? If you are uncertain, what is holding you back from earnestly striving—through conduct, character, and worship—to be among that blessed group?

The Physical Horrors of the Day
Description of the physical terrors of the Day of Resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the physical terrors of the Day of Resurrection as described in the hadith, including nakedness, the proximity of the sun, and the sweat, and the desperation of people wishing for the Fire.

Core Idea
The Day of Resurrection will be so terrifying that people will wish for the Fire.

The author begins by describing the physical realities of the Day of Resurrection based on authentic hadith. The Prophet informed his wife Aisha that people will be raised barefoot, naked, and uncircumcised, and the sun will be extremely close. Sweat will overwhelm people to varying degrees, and the terror will be so great that people will wish to escape to the Fire. This passage establishes the severity of the situation before introducing the exception for the righteous.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Focus on the vivid imagery.
Note the Prophetic manner of description.
2
Identify the specific terrors
List the physical aspects mentioned: being raised naked, sun proximity, sweat reaching different parts, the wish to go to Fire.
3
Reflect on the severity
Consider why the Prophet said 'the matter is more severe than looking at each other' and why they would wish for the Fire.
This helps us appreciate the magnitude.
4
Connect to the lesson's objective
Understand that these are real events that will occur, and they set the stage for the exemption of the righteous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القيامة حفاة عراة غرلا، قلت: يا رسول الله النساء والرجال جميعاً ينظر بعضهم إلى بعض؟ قال: يا عائشة الأمر أشد من أن ينظر بعضهم إلى بعض. كما أوضح أن الشمس تدنو إذ ذاك من رؤوس الخلائق، حتى تكون منه منهم بمقدار ميل، ويذهب العرق يسيح في الأرض سبعين باعاً، فمنهم من يبلغ العرق كعبيه ومنهم من يكون إلى ركبتيه ومنهم من يكون إلى حقويه ومنهم من يلجمه العرق إلجاماً، وأشار رسول الله إلى فيه صلى الله عليه وسلم. وحسبك من هول هذا اليوم أن يتمنى الناس الانصراف عنه ولو إلى النار، وأن يطلق الله عليه اسم الفزع الأكبر. إلا أن شيئاً من هذا الهول لا يمس - كما ورد بذلك الخبر الصادق - الأنبياء، ومن قبلهم الله عز وجل عنده من عباده وأوليائه الصالحين. دل على ذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ الَّذِينَ سَبَقَتْ لَهُمْ مِنَّا الْحُسْنَى أُولَئِكَ عَنْهَا مُبْعَدُونَ، لا يَسْمَعُونَ حَسِيسَهَا وَهُمْ فِي مَا اشْتَهَتْ أَنْفُسُهُمْ خَالِدُونَ، لا يَحْزُنُهُمُ الْفَزَعُ الْأَكْبَرُ وَتَتَلَقَّاهُمُ الْمَلَائِكَةُ هَذَا يَوْمُكُمُ الَّذِي كُنْتُمْ تُوعَدُونَ ﴾ [الأنبياء: 103-105]. وقد دل الحديث الصحيح أن من هؤلاء الذين لا يحزنهم الفزع الأكبر ويكونون في مأمن من هذا العذاب الأليم، أولئك الأصناف السبعة الذين أخبر الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم أنهم يظلهم الله في ظله يوم لا ظل إلا ظله - الحديث. فاجهد يا أيها الإنسان العاقل - وإن فرصة العمر لا تزال في يدك - أن تكون واحداً من هؤلاء الذين قال عنهم: لا يحزنهم الفزع الأكبر. اجهد أن تكون واحداً منهم بسلوكك وخلقك ودينك وقيامك بحق ربك، ولا يخدعنك عن ذلك طول الأمل وسلطان الشهوات والأهواء، فيوشك والله أن ترى هذا الموقف بعينك وإذا البعيد قريب، وإذا المشكوك متحقق وإذا الفرصة فائتة والندم لا يفيد. ولا يجديك أن تسمع هذا الكلام وأنت منصرف عنه غير حافل به تحسبه وهماً من الأوهام، فلو أن أحداً حدثك عن أعاجيب هذه الدنيا قبل أن تراها، لكنت لها أشد إنكاراً ولكنت تحسبها أيضاً وهماً من الأوهام. ثم إن مطية الليل والنهار سائرة بك من معبر هذه الدنيا التي دخلتها البارحة وستفارقها غداً، إلى هذا الهول الذي لا تحفل به، ولن تستطيع أن توقف حركة هذه المطية عن المسير، فخير لك أن تحذر وتتأمل بفكر نقي خالص عن شوائب الأغراض والأهواء ولا يملك عقل عاقل أن يبصر صاحبه بأكثر من هذا الذي أقول.
People will be raised on the Day of Resurrection barefoot, naked, and uncircumcised. I said, 'O Messenger of Allah, will men and women all look at each other?' He said, 'O Aisha, the matter is more severe than that they look at each other.' He also clarified that the sun will then draw near to the heads of creation until it will be from them a distance of a mile, and sweat will go flowing on the earth seventy cubits, so some of them sweat will reach their ankles, some will be to their knees, some will be to their waists, and some the sweat will bridle them like a bridle. And the Messenger of Allah pointed to his mouth. Sufficient for you of the terror of this day is that people will wish to depart from it even to the Fire, and that Allah has named it the Greatest Terror. However, none of this terror touches – as the truthful report has conveyed – the prophets and those whom Allah Almighty has preferred among His servants and righteous saints. Evidence for that is His statement: 'Indeed, those for whom the best [reward] has preceded from Us – they are from it far removed. They will not hear its sound, while they, in what their souls desire, will abide eternally. The greatest terror will not grieve them, and the angels will receive them: This is your Day which you have been promised.' (Al-Anbiya: 103-105). And the authentic hadith indicates that among those who the greatest terror will not grieve and who will be safe from this painful punishment are the seven categories whom the Prophet informed that Allah will shade them in His shade on the Day when there is no shade but His shade — the hadith. So strive, O rational human being – and the opportunity of life is still in your hand – to be one of those of whom He said: 'The greatest terror will not grieve them.' Strive to be one of them through your conduct, character, religion, and fulfilling the right of your Lord, and do not let long hopes and the dominance of desires and passions deceive you about that, for it may soon, by Allah, that you see this scene with your own eyes, and then the distant will be near, and the doubtful will be certain, and the opportunity will be lost, and regret will not avail. Nor will it benefit you to hear this speech while you are turning away from it, heedless, thinking it a fantasy among fantasies. For if someone told you about the wonders of this world before you saw them, you would have denied them more strongly and would have also thought them a fantasy among fantasies. Then the mount of night and day carries you from the crossing of this world which you entered yesterday and will leave tomorrow, toward this terror which you disregard, and you will not be able to stop the movement of this mount from traveling. So it is better for you to be cautious and reflect with a pure mind free from the impurities of objectives and desires. And no rational person can make his companion see more than what I am saying.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage describes the horrors of the Day of Resurrection and then comforts by explaining that the righteous are exempt from the greatest terror. It begins with the hadith of Aisha: people will be raised naked and uncircumcised, and the sun will be extremely close. Sweat will overwhelm people to varying degrees. The Prophet noted that people will wish to go to the Fire to escape this terror. Then the author introduces the good news: based on authentic reports, prophets and righteous saints will not be affected by this terror. He quotes Quran 21:103-105 to prove this. Then he mentions the well-known hadith of seven categories of people who will be shaded by Allah's throne on that day. Finally, he delivers a passionate exhortation: the reader must strive to be among those exempted by acting righteously and not being deceived by worldly desires. He warns that time is passing quickly and that denial of these realities will not help.

B) The sweat reaching the mouth

Key Takeaway
The physical horrors of the Day of Resurrection, including the sun's closeness and overwhelming sweat, are so severe that people will wish for the Fire as relief.

?

?

?
If you truly believed the sun would be just a mile away from you on the Day of Judgment, what one thing would you change about your daily habits starting now?

The Exemption of the Righteous
Evidence for exemption of prophets and righteous from the Greatest Terror.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets and righteous saints, including seven specific categories, are exempt from the Greatest Terror on the Day of Resurrection, as proven by Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
The Greatest Terror does not touch the righteous whom Allah has favored.

After describing the immense terrors of the Day, the author now brings comfort by revealing that not everyone will suffer. Based on authentic reports, the prophets and the righteous saints are exempt from the Greatest Terror. He supports this with a Quranic verse and then mentions the famous hadith of the seven categories who will be shaded under Allah's throne. This passage establishes the hope of salvation for believers who live righteously.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the exemption
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the good news.
2
Identify the two proofs
Notice the author cites Quran 21:103-105 and then the hadith of the seven categories.
These are the primary evidences.
3
Analyze the Quranic verse
The verse describes that those for whom good has preceded will be far from Hell and not grieved by the Greatest Terror.
This is a direct promise.
4
Reflect on the seven categories
The hadith indicates that seven types of people will be shaded by Allah, implying their safety.
Though not enumerated here, it is a well-known hadith.
5
Summarize the lesson
Understand that the terror is not universal; it is reserved for the disbelievers and sinners.
This gives hope to the righteous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القيامة حفاة عراة غرلا، قلت: يا رسول الله النساء والرجال جميعاً ينظر بعضهم إلى بعض؟ قال: يا عائشة الأمر أشد من أن ينظر بعضهم إلى بعض. كما أوضح أن الشمس تدنو إذ ذاك من رؤوس الخلائق، حتى تكون منه منهم بمقدار ميل، ويذهب العرق يسيح في الأرض سبعين باعاً، فمنهم من يبلغ العرق كعبيه ومنهم من يكون إلى ركبتيه ومنهم من يكون إلى حقويه ومنهم من يلجمه العرق إلجاماً، وأشار رسول الله إلى فيه صلى الله عليه وسلم. وحسبك من هول هذا اليوم أن يتمنى الناس الانصراف عنه ولو إلى النار، وأن يطلق الله عليه اسم الفزع الأكبر. إلا أن شيئاً من هذا الهول لا يمس - كما ورد بذلك الخبر الصادق - الأنبياء، ومن قبلهم الله عز وجل عنده من عباده وأوليائه الصالحين. دل على ذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ الَّذِينَ سَبَقَتْ لَهُمْ مِنَّا الْحُسْنَى أُولَئِكَ عَنْهَا مُبْعَدُونَ، لا يَسْمَعُونَ حَسِيسَهَا وَهُمْ فِي مَا اشْتَهَتْ أَنْفُسُهُمْ خَالِدُونَ، لا يَحْزُنُهُمُ الْفَزَعُ الْأَكْبَرُ وَتَتَلَقَّاهُمُ الْمَلَائِكَةُ هَذَا يَوْمُكُمُ الَّذِي كُنْتُمْ تُوعَدُونَ ﴾ [الأنبياء: 103-105]. وقد دل الحديث الصحيح أن من هؤلاء الذين لا يحزنهم الفزع الأكبر ويكونون في مأمن من هذا العذاب الأليم، أولئك الأصناف السبعة الذين أخبر الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم أنهم يظلهم الله في ظله يوم لا ظل إلا ظله - الحديث. فاجهد يا أيها الإنسان العاقل - وإن فرصة العمر لا تزال في يدك - أن تكون واحداً من هؤلاء الذين قال عنهم: لا يحزنهم الفزع الأكبر. اجهد أن تكون واحداً منهم بسلوكك وخلقك ودينك وقيامك بحق ربك، ولا يخدعنك عن ذلك طول الأمل وسلطان الشهوات والأهواء، فيوشك والله أن ترى هذا الموقف بعينك وإذا البعيد قريب، وإذا المشكوك متحقق وإذا الفرصة فائتة والندم لا يفيد. ولا يجديك أن تسمع هذا الكلام وأنت منصرف عنه غير حافل به تحسبه وهماً من الأوهام، فلو أن أحداً حدثك عن أعاجيب هذه الدنيا قبل أن تراها، لكنت لها أشد إنكاراً ولكنت تحسبها أيضاً وهماً من الأوهام. ثم إن مطية الليل والنهار سائرة بك من معبر هذه الدنيا التي دخلتها البارحة وستفارقها غداً، إلى هذا الهول الذي لا تحفل به، ولن تستطيع أن توقف حركة هذه المطية عن المسير، فخير لك أن تحذر وتتأمل بفكر نقي خالص عن شوائب الأغراض والأهواء ولا يملك عقل عاقل أن يبصر صاحبه بأكثر من هذا الذي أقول.
People will be raised on the Day of Resurrection barefoot, naked, and uncircumcised. I said, 'O Messenger of Allah, will men and women all look at each other?' He said, 'O Aisha, the matter is more severe than that they look at each other.' He also clarified that the sun will then draw near to the heads of creation until it will be from them a distance of a mile, and sweat will go flowing on the earth seventy cubits, so some of them sweat will reach their ankles, some will be to their knees, some will be to their waists, and some the sweat will bridle them like a bridle. And the Messenger of Allah pointed to his mouth. Sufficient for you of the terror of this day is that people will wish to depart from it even to the Fire, and that Allah has named it the Greatest Terror. However, none of this terror touches – as the truthful report has conveyed – the prophets and those whom Allah Almighty has preferred among His servants and righteous saints. Evidence for that is His statement: 'Indeed, those for whom the best [reward] has preceded from Us – they are from it far removed. They will not hear its sound, while they, in what their souls desire, will abide eternally. The greatest terror will not grieve them, and the angels will receive them: This is your Day which you have been promised.' (Al-Anbiya: 103-105). And the authentic hadith indicates that among those who the greatest terror will not grieve and who will be safe from this painful punishment are the seven categories whom the Prophet informed that Allah will shade them in His shade on the Day when there is no shade but His shade — the hadith. So strive, O rational human being – and the opportunity of life is still in your hand – to be one of those of whom He said: 'The greatest terror will not grieve them.' Strive to be one of them through your conduct, character, religion, and fulfilling the right of your Lord, and do not let long hopes and the dominance of desires and passions deceive you about that, for it may soon, by Allah, that you see this scene with your own eyes, and then the distant will be near, and the doubtful will be certain, and the opportunity will be lost, and regret will not avail. Nor will it benefit you to hear this speech while you are turning away from it, heedless, thinking it a fantasy among fantasies. For if someone told you about the wonders of this world before you saw them, you would have denied them more strongly and would have also thought them a fantasy among fantasies. Then the mount of night and day carries you from the crossing of this world which you entered yesterday and will leave tomorrow, toward this terror which you disregard, and you will not be able to stop the movement of this mount from traveling. So it is better for you to be cautious and reflect with a pure mind free from the impurities of objectives and desires. And no rational person can make his companion see more than what I am saying.

The Urgent Exhortation to Strive
Exhortation to strive for righteousness and avoid worldly deceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the urgent call to action: to strive to be among the righteous who are saved from the Greatest Terror by using the opportunity of life before it is too late.

Core Idea
Life is the only chance to secure salvation; do not be deceived by worldly desires.

Having established the terrors of the Day and the exemption of the righteous, the author now directly addresses the reader with a passionate exhortation. He calls upon every rational person to strive, through conduct and faith, to be among those who are saved. He warns against being deceived by long hopes and passions, and reminds that time is swiftly passing. This lesson transforms knowledge into a personal call to action.

Guided Path
1
Read the exhortation passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. This is a direct address to you.
Notice the emotional tone.
2
Identify the core command
The author says 'strive to be one of those who will not be grieved by the Greatest Terror.'
This is the main call.
3
Recognize the obstacles
Long hopes (length of life) and dominance of desires and passions are deceptions.
These prevent us from preparing.
4
Understand the urgency metaphors
The mount of night and day is moving you toward the Hereafter; you cannot stop it. This creates urgency.
Time is limited.
5
Apply the reflection advice
The author advises to reflect with a pure mind free from biases. This is how we can truly believe and act.
This is the key to change.

The Reality of the Balance (Mizan) on Judgment Day
Explanation of the reality of the Mizan and the obligation to believe in it without interpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine of the Balance (Mizan) and the proper approach of affirming its reality without delving into its modality.

Core Idea
The Balance is real; our intellect cannot grasp its nature.

This passage from Imam al-Buti's work addresses one of the eschatological realities: the Balance (Mizan) on Judgment Day. Imam al-Buti begins by citing clear Quranic verses that establish the existence of the Balance and the weighing of deeds. He then explains the correct methodological stance: we must believe in it as a reality without attempting to interpret it metaphorically or speculating about its physical composition. This is a key example of the Sunni principle of tafwid — consigning the modality to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic evidence
Read the three verses cited about the Balance. Notice that they are given as clear and explicit (muhkam).
2
Understand the methodological stance
Imam al-Buti then instructs us to refrain from specifying the type, substance, and modality of the Balance. Reflect on why this is necessary.
3
Apply the principle of tafwid
The passage concludes with the principle of believing without interpretation (ta'wil) and without forcing our minds. This lesson teaches you how to approach such unseen matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الميزان والوزن وكلاهما مما أخبر الله عنه في محكم كتابه، بعبارات واضحة صريحة لا تحتمل التأويل. فهو حق يجب الإيمان به كما أخبر. قال الله عز وجل: ﴿ وَالْوَزْنُ يَوْمَئِذٍ الْحَقُّ ﴾ [الأعراف: 8] وقال: ﴿ وَنَضَعُ الْمَوَازِينَ الْقِسْطَ لِيَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ ﴾ [الأنبياء: 47] وقال: ﴿ فَمَنْ ثَقُلَتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْمُفْلِحُونَ، وَمَنْ خَفَّتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُولَئِكَ الَّذِينَ خَسِرُوا أَنْفُسَهُمْ فِي جَهَنَّمَ خَالِدُونَ ﴾ [المؤمنون: 102-103]. وعلينا أن نمسك، كما قال العلماء، عن تعيين نوع هذا الميزان وجوهره وكيفيته، وهل هو ميزان واحد للخلائق كلهم أم موازين كثيرة، فكل ذلك مما لا سبيل إلى القطع به. ولكننا نؤمن بما أخبر الله عنه، ونقول إنه كما أخبر جل جلاله، دون أن نؤول أو نقحم عقولنا وأخيلتنا في حمل هذه الآيات على مجاز أو استعارة أو نحو ذلك.
The Balance and the Weighing: both are among what Allah has informed about in the clear verses of His Book, in clear and explicit terms that do not admit interpretation. They are truth that must be believed as He informed. Allah Almighty said: 'And the weighing on that Day is the truth' (Al-A'raf: 8). And He said: 'And We shall set up the scales of justice for the Day of Resurrection' (Al-Anbiya: 47). And He said: 'Then those whose scales are heavy, they are the successful. And those whose scales are light, they are the ones who have lost their souls, in Hell abiding eternally' (Al-Mu'minun: 102-103). And we must, as the scholars said, refrain from specifying the type of this Balance, its substance, its modality, and whether it is one balance for all creatures or many balances, for all that is beyond definitive knowledge. But we believe in what Allah has informed us, and we say that it is as He informed, the Exalted, without interpreting or forcing our minds and imaginations to construe these verses as metaphor, allegory, or the like.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement about the reality of the Balance (Mizan) and the Weighing on the Day of Judgment. The author asserts that both are firmly established in the Quran and must be accepted literally. He cites three Quranic verses: Al-A'raf 8, Al-Anbiya 47, and Al-Mu'minun 102-103. Then he explains the correct methodology: we must refrain from speculating about the nature, substance, number, or modality of the Balance, as such knowledge is not attainable. The only proper response is to believe in the Balance exactly as Allah described it, without resorting to figurative interpretation (ta'wil) or forcing our intellects to reduce these verses to metaphor. This reflects the Sunni principle of tafwid (consigning the modality to Allah) while affirming the reality.

الوزن
موازين القسط
الإيمان بالغيب

Misconception: Some think that the Balance is merely metaphorical or that we can determine its nature through reason.
Correction: The Balance is a real entity revealed in the Quran; we must believe in it without speculating about its modality or interpreting it figuratively.

Checkpoint

A) We must investigate and determine its substance and modality
B) We must interpret it metaphorically to align with reason

D) We must allegorize it as a symbol of justice

Key Takeaway
The Balance on Judgment Day is a real entity revealed in the Quran, and we must believe in it without speculating about its modality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
