The Meaning and Types of Shafa'ah (Intercession)
Buti defines intercession as divine mercy and enumerates its types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of intercession (shafa'ah) in Islam and the major categories of intercession that will occur on the Day of Judgment.

Core Idea
Intercession is a manifestation of Allah's mercy, not a transaction.

In this lesson, we explore the Islamic concept of intercession (shafa'ah) as explained by Dr. Ramadan al-Buti. He clarifies that intercession is fundamentally a display of Allah's mercy, and then categorizes its types, distinguishing between forgiveness for minor sins and the Prophet's Great Intercession for his nation.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the Arabic passage defining shafa'ah as a manifestation of Allah's mercy. Note that it emphasizes this is a form of mercy, not a bargaining.
2
Identify the first type
Find the first type: Allah's forgiveness for those not guilty of disbelief or polytheism, supported by Qur'an 4:48.
3
Identify the Great Intercession
Notice the second type: the Prophet's Great Intercession (al-shafa'ah al-'uzma), which includes four specific forms.
4
List the four forms
List the four specific intercessions mentioned: relieving the gathering, entering Paradise without account, preventing entry into Hell, and removing believers from Hell.
5
Understand shared intercession
Note that prophets, angels, and the righteous also share in these intercessions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشفاعة والحوض . فأما الشفاعة فهي في الحقيقة مظهر من مظاهر رحمة الله عز وجل بمن شاء من عباده في ذلك الموقف . ويتجلى هذا المظهر بأشكال مختلفة ، فمنها أن يغفر الله لمن شاء من عباده العصاة ما لم يكن من أهل الكفر أو الشرك ، وفي إيضاح هذه الحقيقة يقول الله عز وجل : إنَّ اللهَ لا يَغْفِرُ أَنْ يُشْرَكَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرُ ما دونَ ذلِكَ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ . ومنها تكريم الله رسوله له بالشفاعة في أمته ، وهي ما يطلق عليه العلماء اسم الشفاعة العظمى . وهي تتمثل في شفاعات كثيرة ، أعظمها شفاعته لأهل المحشر عـامـة لإراحتهم من طول الموقف وأهواله ، ومنها إدخاله طائفة من أمته الجنة من غير حساب ، ومنها شفاعته فيمن استحق دخول النار أن لا يدخلها ، ومنها شفاعته في إخراج المؤمنين والموحدين منها بعد دخولهم فيها . ويشاركه في هذه الشفاعة والتي قبلها ، على الأصح ، الأنبياء والملائكة والمقربون من المؤمنين . والمقام المحمود الذي وعد الله رسوله به ، إنما هو المنزلة التي تخوله هذه الشفاعات المختلفة في أهل المحشر عامة وفي أمته خاصة . قال ابن جرير : قال أكثر أهل التأويل : ذلك هو المقام الذي يقومه محمد يوم القيامة للشفاعة في الناس ليريحهم ربهم من عظيم ما هم فيه من شدة ذلك اليوم . وعلى هذا فالمقام المحمود الذي سيقيم الله تعالى نبيه فيه يوم القيامة ليس اسماً لشفاعة معينة من الشفاعات المذكورة . وإنما هو اسم لجميعها حيث يغبطه الخلائق كلهم عليها . وإنما شفاعته لأهل المحشر بإراحتهم من طول الموقف هو أول هذا المقام المحمود كما قال اللقاني في شرحه الجوهرة التوحيد
Intercession and the Basin. As for intercession (al-shafa'ah), it is in reality a manifestation of the mercy of Allah Almighty to whomever He wills of His servants on that occasion. This manifestation appears in different forms. Among them is that Allah forgives whomever He wills of His disobedient servants as long as he is not among the people of disbelief or polytheism. In clarification of this reality, Allah Almighty says: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills.' And among them is Allah honoring His Messenger with intercession for his nation, which scholars call the Great Intercession (al-shafa'ah al-'uzma). It consists of many intercessions, the greatest of which is his intercession for the people of the gathering in general to relieve them of the length of the standing and its terrors. Among them is his entering a group of his nation into Paradise without account. Among them is his intercession for those who deserve to enter the Fire so that they do not enter it. Among them is his intercession to bring out the believers and monotheists from it after they have entered it. He is joined in this intercession and the one before it, according to the soundest opinion, by the prophets, angels, and those close among the believers. And the Praised Station (al-maqam al-mahmud) that Allah promised His Messenger is only the rank that authorizes him these various intercessions for the people of the gathering in general and for his nation specifically. Ibn Jarir said: Most of the exegetes said: That is the station in which Muhammad will stand on the Day of Resurrection to intercede for the people so that their Lord may relieve them of the great distress they are in from the severity of that day. On this basis, the Praised Station in which Allah Almighty will place His Prophet on the Day of Resurrection is not the name of a specific intercession among the mentioned intercessions. Rather, it is a name for all of them, whereby all creatures will envy him for it. And his intercession for the people of the gathering by relieving them from the length of the standing is the first part of this Praised Station, as al-Luqani said in his commentary on al-Jawhara.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of intercession (shafa'ah) followed by an explanation of the Praised Station (al-maqam al-mahmud). The author begins by defining intercession as a manifestation of Allah's mercy. He then enumerates its forms: (1) forgiveness for those not guilty of disbelief or polytheism, supported by the Qur'anic verse (4:48); (2) the Prophet's Great Intercession for his nation, which includes several specific intercessions: a) relieving the people of the gathering from the length of the standing, b) entering a group into Paradise without account, c) preventing some from entering Hell, d) removing believers from Hell after they have entered. The author notes that prophets, angels, and the righteous share in these intercessions. Next, he explains that the Praised Station promised to the Prophet is the rank that encompasses all these intercessions, not just one. He cites Ibn Jarir al-Tabari that it is the station of intercession to relieve the people. Concluding with al-Luqani, he states that the first part of this station is the intercession to relieve the people of the gathering.

Key Terms
الشفاعة
الشفاعة العظمى
أهل المحشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intercession is a negotiation where the Prophet pleads with Allah to change His decree.
Correction: Intercession is a manifestation of Allah's mercy, and it is by Allah's permission and will.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the first category of intercession mentioned?
A) The Prophet's intercession for his nation
B) Allah's forgiveness for those who are not idolaters
C) Intercession by angels
D) Relief from the standing

Key Takeaway
Shafa'ah is fundamentally an expression of Allah's mercy, with the greatest form being the Prophet's intercession for his nation on the Day of Judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson teaches that intercession is a manifestation of Allah's mercy, not a negotiation. Is there a sin in your life that you have been postponing repentance from, hoping someone else's intercession will save you without effort? How does this truth compel you to turn to Allah alone today?
?
The Prophet's intercession includes relieving the people of the standing on the Day of Judgment. Do you truly live as if that Day is imminent, or do your daily choices reflect a false sense of security? What concrete change will you make this week to prioritize your preparation for that moment?
?
Allah forgives everything except shirk for whom He wills. Have you ever despaired of His mercy due to repeated sins? How does this passage's affirmation of boundless mercy demand that you immediately repent and never give up on turning back to Him?

The Praised Station (Al-Maqam al-Mahmud)
Buti defines the Praised Station and distinguishes it from specific intercessions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what the Praised Station (al-maqam al-mahmud) is and how it relates to the various intercessions of the Prophet.

Core Idea
The Praised Station is the all-encompassing rank that authorizes the Prophet's intercessions.

In this lesson, we examine the Praised Station promised to the Prophet in the Qur'an. Dr. Buti explains that this station is not a specific intercession but the entire rank that enables the Prophet to perform all his intercessions. He also highlights that relieving the people of the gathering is the first and most prominent aspect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-maqam al-mahmud
Read the Arabic passage defining the Praised Station. Notice that it is described as the rank that authorizes various intercessions.
2
Understand the quote from Ibn Jarir
Ibn Jarir (al-Tabari) states that the Praised Station is the station for interceding to relieve the people.
3
Distinguish between rank and specific intercession
The passage emphasizes that the Praised Station is not a specific intercession but a name for all intercessions collectively.
4
Note the first part of the station
Al-Luqani notes that relieving the gathering is the first part of this station.

Scriptural Evidence for Intercession
Buti cites Qur'anic verses and a prophetic hadith confirming intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural basis for intercession in Islam, including the conditions set by Allah.

Core Idea
Intercession is a manifestation of Allah's mercy, not an independent power.

Buti now turns to scriptural evidence to establish the reality of intercession. He cites two Qur'anic verses and a prophetic hadith that clearly show intercession exists but is conditional upon Allah's permission and pleasure. This lesson will examine these proofs and the conditions they establish.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the full English translation to grasp the meaning.
Notice the two Qur'anic verses and the hadith.
2
Identify the conditions for intercession
From the verses, list the conditions that must be met for intercession to be accepted. Look for key terms: 'covenant', 'permission', 'pleased'.
3
Reflect on the hadith illustration
Consider how the hadith shows the process of intercession on Judgment Day. Why do people go to the prophets? What is special about the Prophet Muhammad's intercession?
The hadith emphasizes that intercession is only through Allah's mercy.

والآيات والأحاديث التي تتحدث عن الشفاعة كثيرة جداً ، فمن ذلك قوله تعالى : ( لا يَمْلِكُونَ الشَّفاعَةَ إِلا مَن اتَّخَذَ عِندَ الرَّحمن عهداً ) [مريم : ٨٧] وقوله : ( يَومَئِذٍ لا تَنفَعُ الشَّفاعَةُ إلا من أذِنَ لَهُ الرّحمن وَرَضِيَ له قولاً ) [ طه : ١٠٩ ] ومن ذلك الحديث الطويل الذي رواه الشيخان ، وفيه أن الناس ينصرفون إلى الأنبياء واحداً إثر آخر يرجون عندهم الشفاعة ثم ينصرفون إلى رسول الله فيشفع في طائفة كبيرة من المؤمنين . غير أن هذه الشفاعة ، إنما هي ، كما قلت لك ، مظهر من مظاهر رحمة الله
The verses and hadiths that speak about intercession are very many. Among that is His statement, the Most High: 'They do not possess intercession except those who have taken a covenant with the Most Merciful.' [Maryam 19:87] And His statement: 'That Day, no intercession will benefit except [that of] one to whom the Most Merciful has given permission and with whose speech He is pleased.' [Ta Ha 20:109] And among that is the long hadith narrated by the Two Shaykhs (Bukhari and Muslim), in which the people go to the prophets one after another seeking intercession from them, then they go to the Messenger of Allah and he intercedes for a large group of believers. However, this intercession is, as I have told you, only a manifestation of the mercy of Allah.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage provides scriptural proof for intercession. The author presents two Qur'anic verses: from Surah Maryam (19:87) stating that intercession is only for those who have a covenant with Allah, and from Surah Ta Ha (20:109) stating that intercession only benefits those whom Allah permits and with whose speech He is pleased. Both emphasize that intercession is not automatic but depends on divine permission and pleasure. Then the author cites a long hadith from Bukhari and Muslim describing how people will approach prophets for intercession on the Day of Judgment, ending with the Prophet Muhammad who will intercede for a large group of believers. The passage concludes by reiterating that intercession is a manifestation of Allah's mercy, not an independent power.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think intercession is guaranteed for all Muslims regardless of their state.
Correction: The verses show intercession depends on Allah's permission and pleasure, and on having a covenant with Him.

Key Takeaway
Intercession is conditional on Allah's permission and pleasure, and is a manifestation of His mercy.

The Prophet's Pool (al-Hawd) and Its Origin
Buti describes the Pool's origin from al-Kawthar and its prophetic significance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the relationship between the River Kawthar and the Pool (al-Hawd), and why belief in the Pool is a matter of consensus.

Core Idea
The Pool is the overflow of Kawthar, a mercy for believers before entering Paradise.

Buti explains the origin of the Prophet's Pool, clarifying that it is not separate from the River Kawthar but rather its outflow. This distinction is important for understanding the nature of this blessing. The passage also emphasizes the overwhelming number of hadiths about the Pool, establishing it as an article of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Note the key terms: al-Hawd, al-Kawthar, and tawatur.
The Arabic begins with 'ذلك حديث مسلم' referring to a previously mentioned hadith.
2
Identify the origin of the Pool
Locate the sentence that explains where the water of the Pool comes from. Notice the distinction between what flows inside Paradise (Kawthar) and what pours outside (the Pool).
3
Consider the significance of tawatur
Buti states that the hadiths about the Pool have reached the level of tawatur (mass transmission). Reflect on why this matters for establishing theological beliefs.
Tawatur guarantees certainty in transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك حديث مسلم السابق ذكره ، وأن أصله في الجنة . فما كان جارياً منه في داخلها فهو ماء الكوثر ، وما انصب منه في خارجها فهو ماء الحوض وهو الذي يرده المؤمنون الذين لم يبدلوا من دين الله شيئاً . قبل دخولهم الجنة ويكون رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فرطاً لهم عنده. والأحاديث الواردة في شأن الحوض وصفه كثيرة جداً ، وقد زادت عن حد التواتر. وهو أيضاً من مظاهر إكرام الله تعالى لنبيه محمد الله [؟] ورحمته بعباده.
That is the hadith of Muslim previously mentioned, and that its origin is in Paradise. So whatever flows from it within it is water of al-Kawthar, and whatever pours from it outside it is water of the Pond (al-Hawd), which the believers who have not changed anything of the religion of God will drink from before entering Paradise, and the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) will be their forerunner at it. And the hadiths narrated concerning the Pond and its description are very many, and they have exceeded the limit of tawatur (mass transmission). And it is also one of the manifestations of the honor of God Almighty to His Prophet Muhammad [؟] and His mercy to His servants.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage describes the Prophet's Pond (al-Hawd). It begins by clarifying its origin: the Pond's source is in Paradise, and its water is connected to the River Kawthar. Specifically, the water flowing within Paradise is called Kawthar, while what overflows outside Paradise is the water of the Pond. This Pond is where the faithful believers will come to drink before entering Paradise. The Prophet will be there ahead of them as their guide. The passage then notes that the hadiths describing this Pond are extremely numerous, reaching the level of tawatur (mass transmission) which confirms their authenticity. Finally, it states that the Pond is a manifestation of God's honor to His Prophet and His mercy to His servants.

Key Terms
الحوض (al-Hawd)
الكوثر (al-Kawthar)
التواتر (tawatur)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Pool is a separate body of water from the River Kawthar.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the Pool is the overflow of the same source: the water of Kawthar inside Paradise flows out to form the Pool.

Checkpoint
Where does the water of the Pond (al-Hawd) originate according to this passage?
A) From a spring in the earth
B) From the River Kawthar in Paradise
C) From rainwater
D) From a well in the Hereafter

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's Pool (al-Hawd) is the overflow of the River Kawthar, and belief in it is supported by mass-transmitted hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

If you truly believed that your deeds now determine whether you will be among those who 'have not changed anything of the religion of God,' would you change anything about how you practice Islam? What one change will you make starting today?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) will be your forerunner at the Pool. Do you live in a way that you would be comfortable meeting him there tomorrow? What would he say about your commitment to his Sunnah? Write one specific action you will take to better follow his example.
?
If the Pool is a manifestation of Allah's mercy to His servants, what does that tell you about Allah's desire for your salvation? How can you rely on that mercy while still striving to be among the believers who have not changed Allah's religion? What is the balance in your own heart?

The Material Reality of Paradise and Hell
Buti argues for the materiality of Paradise and Hell with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Paradise and Hell are material realities experienced by both body and soul, as argued by Buti using Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are not spiritual metaphors; they are tangible, physical realms for body and soul.

This lesson examines the first of two truths about the afterlife that every Muslim must believe: the materiality of Paradise and Hell. Shaykh Ramadan al-Buti argues that these are not mere spiritual states but concrete realities. He supports his argument with Quranic descriptions and addresses a common objection.

Guided Path
1
Read and identify the main claim
Read the passage carefully. Identify Buti's central claim about Paradise and Hell and what he means by 'material'.
Notice how he distinguishes this from a purely spiritual view.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
The author cites verses from Surat al-Ghashiyah and Surat al-Waqi'ah. List the sensory details mentioned (e.g., flowing springs, raised couches, fruits).
These details are meant to emphasize tangibility.
3
Understand the wisdom behind the details
Buti asks why the Quran describes such minute details. Reflect on his answer: to stress that the bliss and torment are sensory and material.
He contrasts this with those who imagine a purely spiritual afterlife.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجنة والنار ، والخلود في كل منهما. وهما العاقبة التي لا بد أن تنتهي إلى إحداهما حياة الإنسان . وهي عاقبة أخيرة ودائمة لا عاقبة من بعدها. ولا مجال لوصف أهوال النار وعذابها ، ولا لوصف نعيم الجنة وأسباب السعادة فيها ، فحديث ذلك يطول ، وهو على كل لا يكاد يصور شيئاً من الواقع الذي هو اليوم غيب عن الناس كلهم إلى أن يأتي ميقات ذلك اليوم المعلوم والمحدد في علم الله جل جلاله. وإنما يتعلق الحديث هنا ببيان حقيقتين اثنتين لا بد أن يعيها المسلم ويعتقدهما اعتقاداً جازماً. الحقيقة الأولى : الجنة والنار شيئان ماديان. نعم إن الجنة والنار حقيقتان ماديتان من متعلقات كل من النفس والجسم معاً ، وليستا مجرد وهم يطوف بالنفس أو الروح وحدها. إذ لو كان الأمر كذلك لما كان ثمة أي معنى للمعاد الجسمي الذي فرغنا من بيانه والذي حفل كتاب الله تعالى بذكره وتأكيده والتحذير من عواقبه في كثير من نصوصه وآياته القاطعة . وبدهي أنه لا ينكر مادية كل من الجنة والنار إلا من أنكر قبل ذلك الحشر والمعاد الجسمي وعودة الأرواح إلى أجسادها. ومن أوضح الأدلة وأجلاها على هذه الحقيقة ، الطريقة التي يصف بها القرآن كلاً من الجنة والنار ، وهي طريقة قد تثير استفساراً لدى بعض الناس عن حكمة اتباع القرآن لها والتزامه إياها . فالحكمة منها أنها تعبير عن أن نعيم الجنة حسي مادي يلقاه الجسد والروح معاً وعذاب جهنم حسي مادي أيضاً يلقاه الجسد والروح معاً ، وأنها تأكيد لهذه الحقيقة بأقوى الأساليب العربية المؤكدة. تأمل هذه الآيات في وصف الجنة وأهلها : هو وجوهٌ يَوْمَئِذٍ ناعِمَةٌ ، لِسَعيها راضِيَةٌ ، في جَنَّةٍ عاليةٍ ، لا تَسْمَعُ فيها لاغية ، فيها عَيْن جاريةٌ ، فيها سُرُرٌ مرفوعةٌ ، وأكواب موضوعةٌ ، وَنَمارق مصفوفَةٌ ، وزرابي مبثوثة ) [ الغاشية : ٨ - ١٦ ] وهذه الآيات أيضاً : ﴿ وأصحاب اليمين ما أصحاب اليمين ، في سِدْرٍ مخضودٍ ، وَطَلح منضودٍ ، وظل ممدود ، وماء مسكوب ، وفاكهة كثيرة ، لا مقطوعةٍ ولا مَمنوعةٍ ، وفُرُشٍ مرفوعة ) [ الواقعة : ٢٧ - ٣٤ ] . فما الحكمة من وصف هذه الجزئيات كلها من الجنة ونعيمها ، ومعلوم أن أحدنا إذا أراد أن يصف مظهراً من مظاهر النعيم قد لا يجد نفسه بحاجة إلى أن يتناول في وصفه له هذه الدقائق الجزئية كلها ؟ الجواب الجنة شيء حسي ملموس يعيش فيه الإنسان بكل حواسه ومشاعره ، وليس معنى روحياً مجرداً كما يتخيل اليوم بعض من يريدون أن يقفوا في اعتقادهم أمام حـد وسط بين الإيمان والإلحاد. وهو في الحقيقة الإلحاد ذاتـه جـاء ملوناً بهذا اللون السخيف. أنه منتهى ما يمكن أن يتمثل به الأسلوب العربي في تأكيد أن نعيم
Paradise and Hell, and eternal abiding in each of them. They are the ultimate end which a person's life must inevitably lead to one of them. And it is a final and permanent end with no end after it. And there is no room to describe the horrors of Hell and its torment, nor to describe the bliss of Paradise and the means of happiness therein, for discourse on that is lengthy, and in any case it scarcely depicts anything of the reality which today is unseen by all people until the appointed time of that known and determined day in the knowledge of God, exalted is His majesty. Rather, the discussion here concerns the clarification of two truths that the Muslim must comprehend and believe with firm conviction. The first truth: Paradise and Hell are material things. Yes, Paradise and Hell are two material realities pertaining to both the soul and the body together, and they are not mere illusion that circles around the psyche or the spirit alone. For if that were the case, then there would be no meaning to the bodily resurrection (al-ma'ād al-jismānī) which we have finished explaining and which the Book of God Almighty has filled with mention and emphasis and warning of its consequences in many of its decisive texts and verses. And it is obvious that no one denies the materiality of both Paradise and Hell except one who has previously denied the resurrection and bodily return (al-hashr wa al-ma'ād al-jismānī) and the return of souls to their bodies. And among the clearest and most evident proofs of this truth is the manner in which the Quran describes both Paradise and Hell, a manner that may raise an inquiry among some people about the wisdom of the Quran's adoption and adherence to it. For the wisdom in it is that it is an expression that the bliss of Paradise is sensory and material, experienced by the body and soul together, and the torment of Hell is likewise sensory and material, experienced by the body and soul together, and that it is an affirmation of this truth by the strongest emphatic Arabic styles. Reflect on these verses describing Paradise and its inhabitants: 'Faces that Day will be joyful, well-pleased with their effort, in a high Garden, wherein they hear no vain talk, wherein is a flowing spring, wherein are couches raised high, and cups placed, and cushions arrayed, and carpets spread' (al-Ghashiyah 88:8-16). And also these verses: 'And the Companions of the Right - what are the Companions of the Right? [They will be] among lote trees with thorns removed, and banana trees layered [with fruit], and shade extended, and water poured out, and fruit abundant, neither limited nor forbidden, and beds raised high' (al-Waqi'ah 56:27-34). So what is the wisdom in describing all these details of Paradise and its bliss, when it is known that if one of us wants to describe a manifestation of bliss, he may not find himself in need of covering all these minute details? The answer: Paradise is a sensory, tangible thing in which a person lives with all his senses and feelings, and it is not a mere spiritual meaning as imagined today by some who wish to take a middle ground in their belief between faith and atheism. And it is in reality atheism itself, colored with this ridiculous color. That it is the utmost that can be exemplified by the Arabic style in affirming that bliss...
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage presents the first of two truths about Paradise and Hell: they are material realities. The author begins by stating that Paradise and Hell are the final, eternal abode, and then focuses on clarifying this first truth. He affirms that both are material, involving both body and soul, not mere spiritual illusions. He argues that if they were not material, the doctrine of bodily resurrection (al-ma'ād al-jismānī) would be meaningless, a doctrine heavily emphasized in the Quran. He then provides evidence: the Quran's detailed, sensory descriptions of Paradise and Hell. He anticipates an objection: why does the Quran describe such minute details? The wisdom, he explains, is to emphasize that the bliss and torment are sensory and material, experienced by both body and soul. He cites verses from Surat al-Ghashiyah and Surat al-Waqi'ah as examples. Finally, he answers the wisdom question directly: Paradise is tangible, not an abstract spiritual concept, and those who imagine it as merely spiritual are actually veering into atheism. He concludes (though the passage is cut off) that this style is the ultimate Arabic emphasis on the materiality of the bliss.

الجنة
النار
المادي
المعاد الجسمي
الحشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Paradise and Hell are purely spiritual or metaphorical states.
Correction: Buti argues they are material realities for body and soul, as evidenced by Quranic sensory descriptions.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the denial of the materiality of Paradise and Hell logically lead to?
A) Denying the oneness of God
B) Denying the bodily resurrection
C) Denying the prophethood
D) Denying the existence of the soul

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell are material realms that both body and soul will experience, not mere spiritual concepts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Paradise and Hell are truly material realities that your body will experience, are you treating your body today as if it will one day feel the touch of mercy or the burn of fire? What is one physical habit you need to change right now because of this truth?
?
Buti warns that those who imagine Paradise as merely spiritual are sliding toward atheism. Have you ever spoken about the afterlife in a way that made it sound less real than your daily life? Will you commit today to describing Paradise and Hell as the tangible, overwhelming realities they are?
?
The Quran describes Paradise with specific details—rivers, fruits, couches. Does your heart long for these things as concrete pleasures you will taste and feel, or have you reduced them to symbols? Ask yourself honestly: do you yearn for Paradise as a real place, or just as an escape from Hell?

The First Truth: Detailed Description of Hell as Material Punishment
Explains the wisdom behind detailed Quranic descriptions of Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran provides such a detailed description of Hell's punishment and how it affirms its material reality.

Core Idea
Hell's punishment is real, physical, and tangible, not symbolic.

The Quran describes Hell in vivid, sensory detail. Why so much detail? This passage reveals that the purpose is to make clear that the punishment is a literal, physical reality that engages the body and senses, not a mere spiritual metaphor. As we read the verses and the author's explanation, we will uncover the first truth of the Hereafter.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses
Carefully read the four sets of verses quoted. Notice the physical details: heat, food, drink, skin replacement.
These verses form the basis of the argument.
2
Identify the wisdom
The author asks what wisdom lies behind this detail. Locate the rhetorical question and its answer in the passage.
3
Understand the refutation
The author criticizes those who reduce eschatological events to spiritual metaphors. Read how he describes their arrogance and error.
This refutation reinforces the literal interpretation.
4
Conclude with the first truth
The passage ends by stating that the detailed description is the first truth. Reflect on what that truth is and why it matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تأمل في هذه الآيات وهي تصف النار وأهلها : هو وجوهٌ يَومَئِد خاشعة ، عامِلَةٌ نَاصِبَةٌ ، تَصْلى ناراً حامِيَةً ، تُسقى مِن عَينِ آنِيَةٍ ، لَيسَ لَهُم طَعَامٌ إِلا مِنْ ضريع ، لا يُسْمِنُ ولا يُغني من جوع ) [ الغاشية : ٢ - ٧] وفي هذه الآيات الأخرى : ﴿ ثُمَّ إِنَّكُمْ أيُّها الضَّالُونَ المُكَذِّبُونَ ، لاكِلُونَ مِنْ شَجَرٍ مِنْ زَقُومٍ ، فم الثون منها البطونَ ، فَشارِبونَ عَليهِ مِنَ الحميم، فشاربون شُرب الهيم ، هذا نُزُلُهُم يَوْمَ الدِّين ﴾ [ الواقعة : ٥١ - ٥٦ ] وفي قوله : ﴿ إِنَّ المجرمينَ في ضَلال : وسُعُر ، يَوْمَ يُسْحَبونَ في النّارِ على وُجوهِهِمْ ذوقوا مَسَّ سَقَر ﴾ [ القمر ٤٨) وفي قوله : ( إن الذينَ كَفَروا بآياتِنا سوف تصليهم ناراً ، كلما نضجت جلودُهُم بدلناهم جلوداً غَيرَها لِيَذوقوا العَذابَ إنَّ اللهَ كانَ عَـزيـزاً حكيماً ) [ النساء : ٥٦ ] . فما الحكمة من هذا الوصف التفصيلي بهذا الشكل ؟ .. إنه أيضاً بيان وإيضاح للناس كلهم أنه عذاب مادي محسوس ملموس تنغمس فيه حواس الكافرين وجسومهم ومشاعرهم ، وليس كرباً روحانياً مجرداً على نحو ما يتوهم ويتخيل الذين يحلو لهم ، في غرور عجيب ، أن يصعدوا على منبر من الغرور أقاموه من سنوات عمرهم القصير وتفكيرهم المحدود ، ليبعثوا منه بقرارهم عن قصة هذا الكون كله وعن حقيقة الحياة والموت وما بعدهما ، وحقيقة ما جاء من أمر الجنة والنار والحساب والعذاب . وكأنهم شركاء الله في تدبير كونه ، وليسوا خلقاً مهيناً من ملايين مخلوقاته عاشوا لمحة واحدة من عمر الدهر وكانوا قبل ذلك عدماً في طوايا الكون ، ثم استحالوا جيفاً في باطن الأرض في انتظار الأجل المحتوم واليوم الموعود ! .. فهذه هي الحقيقة الأولى
Then reflect on these verses which describe the Fire and its inhabitants: 'Faces that Day will be humbled, laboring, weary, they will burn in a hot fire, they will be given drink from a boiling spring, they will have no food except from a bitter thorny plant, which neither nourishes nor avails against hunger' [Al-Ghashiyah: 2-7]. And in these other verses: 'Then indeed you, O those astray, the deniers, will eat from trees of Zaqqum, and fill your bellies therewith, and drink upon it of boiling water, drinking as thirsty camels drink. That is their hospitality on the Day of Recompense' [Al-Waqi'ah: 51-56]. And in His saying: 'Indeed the criminals are in error and burning. The Day they are dragged into the Fire on their faces, taste the touch of Saqar' [Al-Qamar: 48]. And in His saying: 'Indeed those who disbelieve in Our verses, We will burn them in a Fire. Whenever their skins are roasted through, We will replace them with other skins so they may taste the punishment. Indeed Allah is ever Exalted in Might and Wise' [An-Nisa: 56]. So what is the wisdom behind this detailed description in this form? It is also a clarification and explanation to all people that it is a material, tangible, felt punishment in which the senses, bodies, and feelings of the disbelievers are immersed, and not a mere spiritual distress as imagined by those who, with strange arrogance, ascend a pulpit of conceit built from the years of their short lives and limited thinking, to issue judgments about the story of this entire universe, the reality of life and death and what is after them, and the reality of what has come concerning Paradise, the Fire, the Reckoning, and the punishment. As if they are partners with Allah in managing His creation, and they are not a lowly creation among millions of His creatures, who lived for a single moment of the age of time, and before that were nothing in the folds of the universe, then became corpses in the depths of the earth awaiting the decreed term and the promised day!.. So this is the first truth.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage presents the first of two truths about the Hereafter: the detailed description of Hell in the Quran is not arbitrary but serves to emphasize that the punishment is real, physical, and tangible. The author first quotes four sets of Quranic verses describing the Fire, its heat, food, drink, and the change of skins. Then he asks the rhetorical question: what is the wisdom behind this detailed description? He answers that it is to clarify to all people that the punishment is material, involving the senses and bodies, not merely spiritual distress. He sharply criticizes those who arrogantly reduce eschatological realities to spiritual metaphors, likening them to people who claim partnership with Allah. The passage concludes by stating that this is the first truth.

Misconception: Some believe Hell's punishment is only spiritual or symbolic, not physical.
Correction: The passage affirms that the detailed descriptions in the Quran prove the punishment is material, tangible, and involves the senses and bodies.

Checkpoint

?
These verses describe faces humbled, bodies burning, skins replaced. If you were standing before that Fire today, would you be among those entering it? Take a moment: what sin do you need to abandon right now, before it leads you there?

The Second Truth: Eternity of Paradise and Hell
Affirms eternity of Paradise and Hell with evidence and a key qualification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that both Paradise and Hell are eternal as affirmed by Quran and Sunnah, and that eternal punishment applies only to disbelievers, not to sinful believers.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are eternal; eternal punishment is only for disbelievers.

This lesson presents one of the foundational truths of Islamic eschatology: the everlasting nature of Paradise and Hell. The author cites clear Quranic verses and a powerful hadith to establish this. He then clarifies a crucial distinction – eternal punishment is reserved for disbelievers, while believing sinners have hope for eventual forgiveness.

Guided Path
1
Read the thesis statement
Start by reading the opening sentence that declares the second truth: both Paradise and Hell are eternal with no end. This is the central claim.
The author uses the term 'ḫālid' (eternal) repeatedly to emphasize permanence.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
Read the three Quranic verses cited. Notice how each verse reinforces the idea of eternity for either the dwellers of Paradise or Hell.
The verses are from Surah al-Kahf and Surah az-Zukhruf.
3
Study the hadith evidence
Read the hadith about death being slaughtered. Understand that whether literal or metaphorical, it powerfully confirms the removal of death and thus the eternal state.
The author notes that the exact interpretation does not affect the core message.
4
Understand the qualification
Read the final part where the author specifies that eternal punishment applies only to disbelievers, while sinful believers will eventually be forgiven.
This corrects a common misunderstanding that all who enter Hell remain forever.

الحقيقة الثانية : كل من الجنة والنار خالد لا نهاية له . إن نعيم الجنة باقي خالد لا نهاية له ، وعذاب جهنم باق لا نهاية له . والآيات التي توضح هذه الحقيقة في كتاب الله تعالى كثيرة جداً . فمن ذلك قوله تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّ الَّذينَ آمَنوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ كَانَتْ لَهُم جَنَّاتُ الفِرْدَوْس نُزُلاً ، خالِدِينَ فيها لا يبغونَ عَنْها حِوَلاً ﴾ [ الكهف : ١٠٧-١٠٨ ] وقوله تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّ الْمُجْرِمِينَ في عَذاب جَهَنَّمَ خالدون ، لا يُفَتِّرُ عَنْهُم وَهُمْ فيه مُبْلِسونَ ﴾ [الزخرف : ٧٤ - ٧٥] وقوله تعالى : ( ونادوا يا مالك ﴿ لِيَقْض عَلَينا رَبُّكَ قالَ إِنَّكُم ماكثونَ ﴾ [الزخرف : ٧٧ ] . وقد جاءت السنة بمزيد من التأكيد لهذه الحقيقة ، وذلك في أحاديث كثيرة ، منها ما رواه الشيخان عن ابن عمر قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « إذا صار أهل الجنة إلى الجنة وأهل النار إلى النار ، جيء بالموت حتى يجعل بين الجنة والنار ، ثم يُذبح ، ثم ينادي مناد : يا أهل الجنة لا موت ، يا أهل النار لا موت ، فيزداد أهل الجنة فرحاً إلى فرحهم ويزداد أهـل النـار حـزنــاً إلى حزنهم » . وسواء أكان تجسيد الموت وذبحه بهذا الشكل حقيقة ، أم كان ذلك كناية عن القضاء على معنى الموت وإزالته من الوجود - فإن الحديث على كل حال ينطوي على أبلغ الأساليب المؤكدة لمعنى الخلود في كل من الجنة والنار . على أنا لا نرى داعياً إلى إدخال أي تأويل على ظاهر الحديث . غير أن الذين يستقرون خالدين في عذاب الله تعالى إنما هم الكافرون بمختلف فئاتهم وأضرابهم ، من مشركين وملاحدة وأهل كتاب ممن لم يؤمنوا بنبوة الأنبياء ، أما العصاة من المؤمنين بالله ورسله وكتبه واليوم الآخر فمصيرهم ، مهما طال عليهم العذاب ، إلى مغفرة الله وجنته (۱) . (۱) حاذر أن تطوف بذهنك تلك اللوثة التي يعاني منها بعض الجهال والمنافقين ، ممن يزعمون أن أهل
The second truth: Both Paradise and the Fire are eternal, with no end. Indeed, the bliss of Paradise is everlasting, eternal, with no end, and the punishment of Hell is everlasting, with no end. The verses that clarify this truth in the Book of Allah Most High are very many. Among them is His saying: 'Indeed, those who have believed and done righteous deeds - they will have the Gardens of Paradise as a lodging, wherein they abide eternally, they will not seek from it any transfer' [Al-Kahf: 107-108]. And His saying: 'Indeed, the criminals will be in the punishment of Hell, abiding eternally, it will not be lightened for them, and they will be therein in despair' [Az-Zukhruf: 74-75]. And His saying: 'And they will call, O Malik, let your Lord put an end to us! He will say, Indeed, you will remain' [Az-Zukhruf: 77]. And the Sunnah has come with further emphasis of this truth, in many hadiths, among them what the two Shaykhs narrated from Ibn Umar who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When the people of Paradise enter Paradise and the people of the Fire enter the Fire, death will be brought and placed between Paradise and the Fire, then it will be slaughtered, then a caller will call: O people of Paradise, no death! O people of the Fire, no death! So the people of Paradise will increase in joy upon their joy, and the people of the Fire will increase in sorrow upon their sorrow.' Whether the personification and slaughter of death in this form is literal, or whether it is a metaphor for the elimination of the meaning of death and its removal from existence - in any case, the hadith contains the most emphatic methods to affirm the meaning of eternity in both Paradise and the Fire. Moreover, we see no need to introduce any interpretation of the apparent meaning of the hadith. However, those who will remain eternally in the punishment of Allah Most High are only the disbelievers of various categories and kinds: polytheists, atheists, and People of the Book who did not believe in the prophethood of the prophets. As for the disobedient among the believers in Allah, His messengers, His books, and the Last Day - their destiny, no matter how long the punishment lasts, is to the forgiveness of Allah and His Paradise. (1) (1) Beware that your mind does not entertain that blot which afflicts some ignorant people and hypocrites, who claim that the people of...
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage presents the second truth: the eternity of Paradise and Hell. The author first states the thesis: both are eternal without end. Then he adduces three Quranic verses: from Surat al-Kahf (107-108) showing the eternal abode of believers, from Surat az-Zukhruf (74-75) showing the eternal punishment of criminals, and from Surat az-Zukhruf (77) where the inhabitants of Hell ask for death but are told they will remain. Next, he cites a hadith from al-Bukhari and Muslim about death being brought and slaughtered, which emphatically affirms eternity. He notes that whether the personification is literal or metaphorical, the meaning of eternity is clear. He then clarifies a crucial qualification: eternal punishment is only for disbelievers (polytheists, atheists, and People of the Book who reject prophethood), while believing sinners, no matter how long they are punished, will eventually be forgiven and enter Paradise. The footnote warns against a misunderstanding held by some ignorant people and hypocrites, but the text is cut off.

The Eternity of Paradise and Hell
Buti states the eternity of paradise and hell with evidence and clarifies who is eternally punished.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that both paradise and hell are eternal, as established by Quranic verses and prophetic hadith, and that only disbelievers are eternally punished while sinful believers eventually enter paradise.

Core Idea
Paradise and hell have no end; only disbelief earns eternal punishment.

In this passage, Buti presents the second foundational truth of the unseen: the eternal nature of paradise and hell. He supports it with clear Quranic verses and a powerful hadith about the slaughter of death. He then clarifies who will suffer eternal punishment and who will eventually be saved, addressing a common misconception about the People of the Book.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the English translation. Notice the confident tone and the use of evidence.
The passage begins with a clear statement of the truth before providing proof.
2
Identify the evidence
Find the three Quranic verses and the hadith cited. See how they directly affirm eternity without end.
The verses from Surah Al-Kahf and Az-Zukhruf are especially clear.
3
Understand the exception
Note that Buti limits eternal punishment to disbelievers, not sinful believers. Understand why this distinction matters for Islamic theology.
The footnote warns against a common error regarding the People of the Book.

الحقيقة الثانية : كل من الجنة والنار خالد لا نهاية له
إن نعيم الجنة باقي خالد لا نهاية له ، وعذاب جهنم باق لا نهاية له والآيات التي توضح هذه الحقيقة في كتاب الله تعالى كثيرة جداً
فمن ذلك قوله تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّ الَّذينَ آمَنوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ كَانَتْ لَهُم جَنَّاتُ الفِرْدَوْس نُزُلاً ، خالِدِينَ فيها لا يبغونَ عَنْها حِوَلاً ﴾ [ الكهف : ١٠٧-١٠٨ ] وقوله تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّ الْمُجْرِمِينَ في عَذاب جَهَنَّمَ خالدون ، لا يُفَتِّرُ عَنْهُم وَهُمْ فيه مُبْلِسونَ ﴾ [الزخرف : ٧٤ - ٧٥] وقوله تعالى : ( ونادوا يا مالك ﴿ لِيَقْض عَلَينا رَبُّكَ قالَ إِنَّكُم ماكثونَ ﴾ [الزخرف : ٧٧ ] . وقد جاءت السنة بمزيد من التأكيد لهذه الحقيقة ، وذلك في أحاديث كثيرة ، منها ما رواه الشيخان عن ابن عمر قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « إذا صار أهل الجنة إلى الجنة وأهل النار إلى النار ، جيء بالموت حتى يجعل بين الجنة والنار ، ثم يُذبح ، ثم ينادي مناد : يا أهل الجنة لا موت ، يا أهل النار لا موت ، فيزداد أهل الجنة فرحاً إلى فرحهم ويزداد أهـل النـار حـزنــاً إلى حزنهم » .

The second truth: Both paradise and hell are eternal, with no end. Indeed, the bliss of paradise is lasting, eternal, with no end, and the punishment of hell is lasting, with no end. And the verses that clarify this truth in the Book of God Almighty are very many. Among them is His saying, the Most High: 'Indeed, those who have believed and done righteous deeds - they will have the Gardens of Paradise as a lodging, abiding eternally therein, not desiring any transfer therefrom' [Al-Kahf 107-108]. And His saying, the Most High: 'Indeed, the criminals are in the punishment of Hell, abiding eternally, not [a torment] being lightened for them, and they, therein, are in despair' [Az-Zukhruf 74-75]. And His saying, the Most High: 'And they will call, "O Malik, let your Lord put an end to us!" He will say, "Indeed, you will remain."' [Az-Zukhruf 77]. And the Sunnah has come with further emphasis of this truth, in many hadiths, among them what the two Shaykhs narrated from Ibn Umar who said: The Messenger of God, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'When the people of Paradise enter Paradise and the people of Hell enter Hell, death will be brought and placed between Paradise and Hell, then it will be slaughtered, then a caller will call: O people of Paradise, no death! O people of Hell, no death! So the people of Paradise will increase in joy upon their joy, and the people of Hell will increase in sorrow upon their sorrow.' And whether the embodiment and slaughter of death in this form is real, or whether that is a metaphor for the elimination and removal of the meaning of death from existence - in any case, the hadith contains the most emphatic methods for confirming the meaning of eternity in both Paradise and Hell. However, we see no need to introduce any interpretation of the apparent meaning of the hadith. But those who will reside eternally in the punishment of God Almighty are only the disbelievers of various categories and types: polytheists, atheists, and People of the Book who did not believe in the prophethood of the prophets. As for the sinful believers in God, His messengers, His books, and the Last Day, their end, however long their punishment lasts, is the forgiveness of God and His Paradise. (1) (1) Beware that that stain which some ignorant and hypocrites suffer from should pass through your mind, those who claim that the People of the Book are established (i.e., a foundation) and that they are another category besides the disbelievers, so they are not punished with their punishment nor are they made to abide eternally in Hell like them. For this claim is a clear challenge to the saying of God Almighty: 'Indeed, those who disbelieved among the People of the Book and the polytheists will be in the fire of Hell, abiding eternally therein. Those are the worst of creatures' [Al-Bayyinah 6]. For the verse divided the disbelievers into People of the Book and polytheists, then included all of them in this great warning.

Commentary
This passage states the second truth: both paradise and hell are eternal. The author asserts this unequivocally and supports it with Quranic verses: Surah Al-Kahf 107-108 for the believers in paradise, and Surah Az-Zukhruf 74-75 and 77 for the criminals in hell. He then cites a sahih hadith in which death is slaughtered between paradise and hell, emphasizing that there will be no more death, which reinforces the concept of eternity. He comments that whether the hadith is literal or metaphorical, it strongly affirms eternity. He then clarifies that only disbelievers—polytheists, atheists, and People of the Book who reject prophethood—will be eternally punished. Sinful believers, no matter how long their punishment, will eventually be forgiven and enter paradise. In a footnote, he warns against a false belief that the People of the Book are a separate category from disbelievers, refuting it with Surah Al-Bayyinah 6 which includes them in the same condemnation.

Resolving the Exception in Surah Hud: Objection and Answer
Buti answers the objection that the exception in Surah Hud contradicts the eternity of paradise and hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the apparent exception in Surah Hud is reconciled with the doctrine of eternal paradise and hell for believers and disbelievers respectively.

Core Idea
The exception in Surah Hud refers to sinful believers, not to the eternity of the abodes.

The verse in Surah Hud seems to make the eternity of hell and paradise conditional on God's will, which appears to contradict clear texts and consensus. Buti addresses this objection by explaining that the exception applies to the categories of 'wretched' and 'blessed' themselves, referring to sinful believers who may be temporarily punished or exempted from eternal punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the objection based on the exception wording.
2
Identify the objection
The objection is that the exception seems to negate eternal punishment for disbelievers and eternal reward for believers. Underline the verse and the claim.
3
Understand the answer
Buti explains that the exception is from the state of being 'wretched' or 'blessed', not from eternity itself. The excepted ones are sinful believers.
4
Apply to categories
Distinguish between disbelievers (eternal punishment) and sinful believers (temporary punishment or eventual paradise). This resolves the contradiction.
Note that the exception for 'blessed' is also about temporary punishment before paradise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وربما استشكلت بهذا الصدد قوله تعالى : ( فأما الَّذِينَ شَقُوا ففي النّارِ لَهُم فيها زفيرٌ وشَهِيلٌ ، خالدين فيها ، ما دامَتِ السَّماوات والأرض إلا ما شاءَ رَبُّكَ إِنَّ رَبَّكَ فَعّالٌ لِمَا يُريدُ ، وأما الذين سعدوا ففي الجَنَّةِ خالدين فيها ما دامَتِ السَّموات والأرض إلا ما شاءَ رَبُّكَ عَطاءً غَيْرَ مَجْدُودٍ ﴾ [ هود : ١٠٦-١٠٨ ] ذلك أن ظاهر قوله : إلا ما شاء ربك ، استثناء من الخلود ، وهو يـنـافي ما تقرره الآيات الأخرى والأحاديث الثابتة وما اتفق عليه المسلمون من أن ... والجواب أنه استثناء من قوله : شقوا ، في الآية الأولى ، ومن قوله : سعدوا في الآية الثانية . أي إن جميع الأشقياء خالدون في النار إلا شاء الله لا يخلدوا فيها ، وهم العصاة من أهل الإيمان والتوحيد ، كما دلت على ذلك الأدلة الكثيرة الأخرى . وجميع أهل السعادة خالدون في الجنة إلا من شاء الله منهم أن يتعذب في النار إلى أمد قبل ذلك ، وهم أولئك الذين غمرت حياتهم بالمعاصي والأوزار من المؤمنين ولم تكتب لهم الشفاعة أولاً
وإنما لم يأت الاستثناء بصيغة : إلا من شاء ربك . كما كان يقتضي ظاهر الاستثناء ، لأن المراد من المستثنى منه العدد المجرد لا الأشخـاص بـأعيانهم حتى يراعى فيهم العقل ، وذلك كقوله تعالى : فانكحوا ما طاب لَكُم مِنَ النّساء مَثْنى  َوثُلاثَ وَرُبَاعَ ﴾ [النساء : ٣] . فقد عبر عن النساء بمـا ، عندما كان الملاحظ فيهن العدد لا الشخص
And perhaps one might be confused in this regard by His saying, the Most High: 'As for those who are wretched, they will be in the Fire; for them therein is [violent] exhaling and inhaling, abiding eternally therein as long as the heavens and the earth endure, except what your Lord wills. Indeed, your Lord does whatever He wills. And as for those who are blessed, they will be in Paradise, abiding eternally therein as long as the heavens and the earth endure, except what your Lord wills; [it is] an unceasing gift' [Hud 106-108]. That is because the apparent meaning of His saying 'except what your Lord wills' is an exception from eternity, and it contradicts what the other verses and established hadiths establish and what the Muslims have agreed upon... The answer: It is an exception from His saying 'are wretched' in the first verse, and from His saying 'are blessed' in the second verse. That is, all the wretched are abiding eternally in Hell, unless God wills that they not abide eternally in it, and they are the sinners among the people of faith and tawhid, as the many other evidences have indicated. And all the people of blessedness are abiding eternally in Paradise, except those whom God wills to be punished in Hell for a period before that, and they are those whose lives were overwhelmed with sins and burdens from among the believers, and for whom intercession was not written firstly. And the exception did not come in the form 'except whom your Lord wills', as the apparent [wording] of the exception would require, because the intended meaning of the thing excepted from is the abstract number, not the specific individuals themselves so that reason might be observed in them. And that is like His saying, the Most High: 'then marry what is good for you of women, two or three or four' [An-Nisa 3]. For He expressed women with 'what' (ma) when the observation was of number, not person.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objection is based on the verse in Surah Hud (11:106-108) which says that the wretched and the blessed are in their places 'except what your Lord wills', which appears to be an exception from eternity, contradicting other clear texts and the consensus of Muslims. The author provides the answer: The exception is not from the eternity of the abode itself, but from the state of being wretched or blessed. In other words, all the wretched (disbelievers) are eternally in hell unless God wills that some of them not be eternally punished—these are the sinful believers who will eventually be saved. Similarly, all the blessed (believers) are eternally in paradise unless God wills that some of them be punished temporarily in hell before entering paradise—these are sinful believers whose sins necessitate temporary punishment. The author then explains a grammatical nuance: the exception is worded with 'ma' (ما) rather than 'man' (من) because it refers to number, not specific individuals. This is analogous to the verse about marrying women where 'ma' is used to denote the number (two, three, four) rather than specific women. Thus the apparent contradiction is resolved.

Key Terms
استثناء
خلود
شقوا
سعدوا
عصاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The exception in Surah Hud implies that even disbelievers may not be eternally punished or that paradise is not eternal for believers.
Correction: The exception applies to sinful believers, not to disbelievers or the righteous. Disbelievers are eternally punished, and righteous believers are eternally rewarded.

Checkpoint
What does the exception in Surah Hud refer to, according to the author?
A) It refers to disbelievers who will not be punished
B) It refers to sinful believers who will not be eternally punished or will be temporarily punished
C) It refers to all people
D) It is a meaningless exception

Key Takeaway
The exception in Surah Hud is not a denial of eternal punishment for disbelievers but a qualification regarding sinful believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that the exception in Surah Hud applies only to sinful believers, does your hope in God's mercy lead you to take sin lightly? How does this verse urge you to repent sincerely before death?
?
If you were to die tonight, would you be among the 'ashqiya' or 'su'ada'? What evidence from your life supports that? How does this lesson change your sense of urgency in obeying Allah?
?
The exception refers to those for whom intercession was not written firstly. Are you relying on intercession without striving for righteousness? What concrete steps will you take today to ensure you are not among those excepted only by temporary punishment?

Grammatical Nuance of the Exception in Surah Hud
Buti explains the grammatical nuance of the exception wording in Surah Hud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the exception in Surah Hud is worded using 'ma' (ما) instead of 'man' (من), and how this grammatical choice supports the interpretation that it refers to number rather than specific individuals.

Core Idea
The use of 'ma' in the exception indicates it is about the count of people, not their identities.

After explaining that the exception applies to sinful believers, Buti addresses a grammatical subtlety: why the exception uses 'ma' (ما) instead of 'man' (من). He clarifies that the exception is from the abstract number of people in each category, not from the individuals themselves, which is why the gender-neutral 'ma' is appropriate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the grammatical explanation.
2
Identify the phrasing
Note that the exception does not use 'illa man' but 'illa ma'. This is a grammatical puzzle.
3
Understand the reasoning
Buti explains that 'ma' is used because the intended exception is from the number (adad) of the people in each group, not their specific persons.
4
Analogous verse
Compare with the verse on marriage in An-Nisa, where 'ma' is used to refer to the number of women, not specific women. This demonstrates the rule.

Reconciling the Exception in Surah Hud
Author refutes an objection about the exception clause in Hud 11:106-108.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the apparent exception in Surah Hud is reconciled with the eternity of Paradise and Hell.

Core Idea
The exception in Hud refers to sinful believers, not disbelievers.

This passage addresses a potential confusion from the verse in Surah Hud that seems to suggest that eternity in Paradise or Hell is subject to Allah's will. The author shows that the exception is about categories of people, not individuals, and it refers to the fate of sinful believers. This lesson clarifies the proper understanding of this verse and reinforces the Islamic belief in eternal reward and punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author presents an objection first, then answers it.
2
Identify the objection
The objection is that the exception clause 'except what your Lord wills' seems to contradict the established doctrine of eternal punishment for disbelievers and eternal reward for believers.
This objection is based on the apparent meaning of the verse.
3
Examine the author's answer
The author explains that the exception is from the categories 'wretched' and 'blessed', not from the state of eternity itself. This means sinful believers are excepted from eternal punishment, and some believers may be punished temporarily before entering Paradise.
The answer reconciles the verse with other definitive texts.
4
Understand the grammatical point
The author notes that the Arabic particle 'ma' (what) is used instead of 'man' (whom) to indicate that the exception concerns the abstract number or category, not individuals. This is similar to the verse on marriage.
This clarifies why the wording 'except what your Lord wills' is used.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that these unseen realities must be believed after faith in Allah, and faith in Allah is inseparable from faith in these matters.
This highlights the importance of accepting all revealed truths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وربما استشكلت بهذا الصدد قوله تعالى : ( فأما الَّذِينَ شَقُوا ففي النّارِ لَهُم فيها زفيرٌ وشَهِيلٌ ، خالدين فيها ، ما دامَتِ السَّماوات والأرض إلا ما شاءَ رَبَّكَ إِنَّ رَبَّكَ فَعّالٌ لِمَا يُريدُ ، وأما الذين سعدوا ففي الجَنَّةِ خالدين فيها ما دامَتِ السَّموات والأرض إلا ما شاءَ رَبُّكَ عَطاءً غَيْرَ مَجْدُودٍ ﴾ [ هود : ١٠٦ - ١٠٨ ] ذلك أن ظاهر قوله : إلا ما شاء ربك ، استثناء من الخلود ، وهـو يـنـافي ما تقرره الآيات الأخرى والأحاديث الثابتة وما اتفق عليه المسلمون من أن الكفار مخلدون في النار والمؤمنين مخلدون في الجنة . والجواب أنه استثناء من قوله : شقوا ، في الآية الأولى ، ومن قوله : سعدوا في الآية الثانية . أي إن جميع الأشقياء خالدون في النار إلا من شاء الله لا يخلدوا فيها ، وهم العصاة من أهل الإيمان والتوحيد ، كما دلت على ذلك الأدلة الكثيرة الأخرى . وجميع أهل السعادة خالدون في الجنة إلا من شاء الله منهم أن يتعذب في النار إلى أمد قبل ذلك ، وهم أولئك الذين غمرت حياتهم بالمعاصي والأوزار من المؤمنين ولم تكتب لهم الشفاعة أولاً . وإنما لم يأت الاستثناء بصيغة : إلا من شاء ربك . كما كان يقتضي ظاهر الاستثناء ، لأن المراد من المستثنى منه العدد المجرد لا الأشخـاص بـأعيانهم حتى يراعى فيهم العقل ، وذلك كقوله تعالى : فانكحوا ما طاب لَكُم مِنَ النّساء مَثْنى وَثُلاثَ وَرُبَاعَ ﴾ [النساء : ٣] . فقد عبر عن النساء بمـا ، عندما كان الملاحظ فيهن العدد لا الشخص . فهذه هي جملة الحقائق الغيبية التي يجب أن يعيها الإنسان ويعتقدهـا اعتقاداً جازماً ، بعد أن اجتاز مرحلة الإيمان بالله ورسوله وكتبه . ولا يمكن عقلاً أن ينفك الإيمان بالله عن الإيمان بهذه المغيبات ، إذ هما متلازمان تلازماً واضحاً لكل ذي عقل
And perhaps an objection is raised in this regard concerning the saying of the Exalted: (As for those who are wretched, they will be in the Fire, for them in it is sighing and wailing, abiding therein forever, as long as the heavens and the earth endure, except what your Lord wills. Indeed your Lord does what He intends. And as for those who are blessed, they will be in Paradise, abiding therein forever, as long as the heavens and the earth endure, except what your Lord wills – a gift never to be cut off) [Hud 11:106-108]. That is because the apparent meaning of His saying: 'except what your Lord wills' is an exception from eternity, and it contradicts what is established by other verses and authentic hadiths and what the Muslims have agreed upon, that the disbelievers are eternally in the Fire and the believers are eternally in Paradise. The answer: It is an exception from His saying: 'those who are wretched' in the first verse, and from His saying: 'those who are blessed' in the second verse. That is, all the wretched are eternal in the Fire, except those whom Allah wills not to be eternal therein – and they are the disobedient among the people of faith and tawhid, as indicated by numerous other evidences. And all the blessed are eternal in Paradise, except those among them whom Allah wills to be punished in the Fire for a period before that – and they are those whose lives were overwhelmed by sins and burdens from among the believers, and for whom intercession was not written first. And the exception did not come in the form: 'except whom your Lord wills', as the apparent exception would require, because what is intended by the thing excepted from is the abstract number, not the individuals themselves such that rationality would be observed in them. This is like His saying, Exalted: 'then marry what is pleasing to you of women, two, three, or four' [An-Nisa 4:3]. He expressed women with 'what' when the observation in them was number, not person. So these are the totality of the unseen realities that a person must comprehend and believe with firm conviction, after having passed the stage of faith in Allah, His Messenger, and His Books. And it is rationally impossible that faith in Allah be separated from faith in these unseen things, for they are two inseparable concomitants, clear to every intelligent person.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The author introduces a potential problem: the verse in Surah Hud includes an exception clause 'except what your Lord wills' concerning eternity in Paradise and Hell. This seems to conflict with other definitive texts that state disbelievers are eternally in the Fire and believers eternally in Paradise. The author then presents the answer: the exception does not apply to the eternity itself but to the people described as 'wretched' and 'blessed'. In other words, all the wretched (disbelievers) are eternal in Hell, except those whom Allah wills not to be eternal—these are the sinful monotheists who will eventually be purified and enter Paradise. Similarly, all the blessed (believers) are eternal in Paradise, except those whom Allah wills to first be punished for their sins—these are believers who die in major sins without intercession. The author further explains why the exception is phrased as 'except what your Lord wills' rather than 'except whom your Lord wills': the exception is about the abstract number or category (the 'wretched' and 'blessed' as groups), not the individuals themselves. This is analogous to the verse on marriage where 'what' is used to indicate number rather than persons. The passage concludes with the doctrinal point: these unseen realities (the details of reward and punishment) must be believed after faith in Allah and His Messenger, and faith in Allah is inseparable from faith in these unseen matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the exception in the verse allows for the possibility that disbelievers may not be eternally punished.
Correction: The exception refers to sinful believers, not disbelievers. Disbelievers remain eternally in Hell.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does the exception 'except what your Lord wills' in Surah Hud refer to?
A) It refers to the possibility that some disbelievers may not be eternally punished.
B) It refers to the possibility that some believers may not be eternally rewarded.
C) It refers to sinful believers who will be eternally punished.
D) It refers to the category of people, not individuals, meaning sinful believers are excepted from eternal punishment and some believers from eternal reward until after punishment.

Key Takeaway
The exception in Surah Hud is about the categories of people, not individuals, and it refers to sinful believers who will eventually be saved.

?

?

Refuting the Claim of Exemption for People of the Book
Author refutes the claim of exemption for People of the Book with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran explicitly includes the People of the Book in the universal threat of Hell, refuting any claim of exemption.

Core Idea
No one is exempt: the Quran groups all disbelievers under the same warning.

This lesson examines a crucial Quranic proof that demolishes the notion that the People of the Book will escape eternal punishment. The author presents a clear verse from Surah Al-Bayyinah and draws out its logical implication.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and verse
Read the Arabic passage along with its translation. Pay special attention to the Quranic verse quoted.
The verse is Surah Al-Bayyinah 98:6.
2
Notice the two groups mentioned
The verse explicitly names both 'People of the Book' and 'polytheists' as being in Hell. This is the key point.
The author uses this to show the verse covers all disbelievers.
3
Understand the inclusive force
The author explains that the verse divides disbelievers into these two categories and then includes them all in the same threat. This refutes any claim of exemption.
The word 'ثم' (then) indicates inclusion after division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن هذا الزعم تحد صارح لقول الله تعالى : ( إنَّ الَّذينَ كَفَرُوا مِن أهل الكتاب والمشركين في نار جَهَنَّمَ خالدين فيها أولئكَ هُم شَرِّ البَريَّة ﴾ [ البينة : ٦ ] فقد قسمت الآية الكفار إلى أهل كتاب ومشركين ، ثم شملتهم جميعاً هذا الوعيد العظيم
For this claim is an outright challenge to the saying of Allah, Exalted: (Indeed those who disbelieve from the People of the Book and the polytheists will be in the fire of Hell, abiding therein forever; those are the worst of creatures) [Al-Bayyinah 98:6]. For the verse divides the disbelievers into People of the Book and polytheists, then includes them all in this great threat.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a refutation. The author addresses a previous claim (not fully shown here) that the People of the Book are a separate category and will not be punished like other disbelievers. The author refutes by quoting Surah Al-Bayyinah 98:6, which explicitly mentions both 'People of the Book' and 'polytheists' as disbelievers who will be eternally in Hell. The verse uses inclusive language, thus refuting the idea of any special exemption. The author emphasizes that the verse groups them together under the same severe warning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author use to refute the claim that the People of the Book are exempt from eternal punishment?
A) A rational argument about justice.
B) A verse from Surah Al-Bayyinah that includes both the People of the Book and polytheists in the threat of Hell.
C) A hadith about the People of the Book.
D) The consensus of scholars.

Key Takeaway
Allah's threat of eternal punishment in Hell applies equally to the People of the Book and the polytheists, as stated in Surah Al-Bayyinah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself feeling spiritually superior because of your religious identity, forgetting that the same standard of judgment applies to you as to anyone else? When was the last time this verse's warning made you examine your own faith sincerity? Resolve today to abandon any sense of entitlement and humble yourself before Allah's decisive Word.
?
The People of the Book possessed scripture yet are warned of eternal fire if they disbelieve. Are there beliefs or practices you hold that conflict with clear Quranic teachings, thinking they are exempt from divine punishment? This verse strips away all excuses. Will you submit to its full weight, or continue rationalizing?
